Precedent	Reliance is placed upon the observations of <NAME> in <NAME> (at page 406) where, dealing with the above observations in Balaji, the learned Judge said:  We do not think that these observations were meant to lay down any proposition that the socially Backward Classes were those classes of people, whose conditions of life were very nearly the same as those of the Scheduled Castes and Tribes....There is no point in attempting to determine the social backwardness of other classes by applying the test of nearness to the conditions of existence of the Scheduled Castes.
Precedent	Such a test would practically nullify the provision for reservation for socially and educationally Backward Classes other than Scheduled Cast es and Tribes.
Precedent	88.
Precedent	We see no reason to qualify or restrict the meaning of the expression "backward class of citizens" by saying that it means those other backward classes who are situated similarly to Scheduled Castes and/or Scheduled Tribes.
Precedent	As pointed out in para 85, the relevant language employed in both the clauses is different.
Precedent	Article 16(4) does not expressly refer to Scheduled Castes or Scheduled Tribes; if so, there is no reason why we should treat their backwardness as the standard backwardness for all those claiming its protection.
Precedent	As a matter of fact, neither the several castes/groups/tribes within the Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes are similarly situated nor are the Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes similarly situated.
Precedent	If any group or class is situated similarly to the Scheduled Castes, they may have a case for inclusion in that class but there seems to be no basis either in fact or in principle for holding that other classes/groups must be situated similarly to them for qualifying as  backward classes.
Precedent	There is no warrant to import any such a priori notions into the concept of Other Backward Classes.
Precedent	At the same time, we think it appropriate to clarify that backwardness, being a relative term, must in the context be judged by the general level of advancement of the entire population of the country or the <ORG>, as the case may be.
Precedent	More than this, it is difficult to say.
Precedent	How difficult is the process of ascertainment of backwardness would be known if one peruses Chapters III and XI of Volume I of the Mandal Commission Report along with Appendixes 12 and 21 in Volume II.
Precedent	It must be left to the Commission/Authority appointed to identify the backward classes to evolve a proper and relevant criteria and test the several groups, castes, classes and sections of people against that criteria.
Precedent	If, in any case, a particular caste or class is wrongly designated or not designated a backward class, it can always be questioned before a court of law as well.
Precedent	We may add that relevancy of the criteria evolve d by <ORG> (Chapter XI) has not been questioned by any of the counsel before us.
Precedent	Actual identification is a different matter, which we shall deal with elsewhere.
Precedent	88A.
Precedent	We may now summarise our discussion under Question No.
Precedent	3.
Precedent	(a) a caste can be an quite often is a social class in India.
Precedent	If it is backward socially, it would be a backward class for the purposes of Article 16(4).
Precedent	Among <ORG>, there are several occupational groups, sects and denominations, which for historical reasons are socially backward.
Precedent	They too represent backward social collectives for the purposes of Article 16(4).
Precedent	(b) Neither the Constitution nor the law prescribe the procedure or method of identification of backward classes.
Precedent	Nor is it possible or advisable for the court to lay down any such procedure or method.
Precedent	It must be left to the authority appointed to identify.
Precedent	If can adopt such method/procedure as it thinks convenient and so long as its survey covers the entire populace, no objection can be taken to it.
Precedent	Identificatio n of the backward classes can certainly be down with reference to castes among, and along with, other groups, classes and sections of people.
Precedent	One can start the process with the castes, wherever they are found, apply the criteria (evolved for determining backwardness) and find out whether it satisfies the criteria.
Precedent	If it does - what emerges is a "backward class of citizens" within the meaning of and for the purposes of Article 16(4).
Precedent	Similar process can be adopted in the case of other occupational groups, communities and classes, so as to cover the entire populace.
Precedent	The central idea and overall objective should be to consider all available groups, sections and classes in society.
Precedent	Since caste represents an existing, identifiable social group/class encompassing an overwhelming majority of the country's population, one can well begin with it and then go to other groups, sections and classes.
Precedent	(c) It is not necessary for a class to be designated as a backward class that it is situated similarly to the Scheduled Cast es/Scheduled Tribes, (d) 'Creamy layer' can be, and must be, excluded.
Precedent	(e) It is not correct to say that the backward class contemplated by Article 16(4) is limited to the socially and educationally backward classes referred to in Article 15(4) and Article 340.
Precedent	It is much wider.
Precedent	The test or requirement of social and educational backwardness cannot be applied to Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes, who indubitably fall within the expression "backward class of citizens."
Precedent	The accent in Article 16(4) appears to be on social backwardness.
Precedent	Of course, social, educational and economic backwardness are closely inter-twined in the Indian context.
Precedent	The classes contemplated by Article 16(4) may be wider than those contemplated by Article 15(4).
Precedent	Adequacy of Representation in the services under the <ORG>:  89.
Precedent	Not only should a class be a backward class for meriting reservations, it should also be inadequately represented in the services under the <ORG>.
Precedent	The language of Clause (4) makes it clear that the question whethe r a backward class of citizens is not adequately represented in the services under the <ORG> is a matter within the subjective satisfaction of the <ORG>.
Precedent	This is evident from the fact that the said requirement is preceded by the words "in the opinion of the <ORG>".
Precedent	This opinion can be formed by the <ORG> on its own, i.e., on the basis of the material it has in its possession already or it may gather such material through <ORG>, person or authority.
Precedent	All that is required is, there must be some material upon which the opinion is formed.
Precedent	Indeed, in this matter the court should show due deference to the opinion of the <ORG>, which in the present context means the executive.
Precedent	The executive is supposed to know the existing conditions in the society, drawn as it is from among the representatives of the people in <ORG>.
Precedent	It does not, however, mean that the opinion formed is beyond judicial scrutiny altogether.
Precedent	The scope and reach of judicial scrutiny in matters within subjective satisfa ction of the executive are well and extensively stated in <CITATION_1748256> , which need not be repeated here.
Precedent	Sufficed it to mention that the said principles apply equally in the case of a constitutional provision like Article 16(4) which expressly places the particular fact (inadequate representation) within the subjective judgment of the State/executive.
Precedent	Question 4: (a) Whether backward classes can be identified only and exclusively with reference to the economic criterion:  90.
Precedent	It follow from the discussion under Question No.
Precedent	3 that a backward class cannot be determined only and exclusively with reference to economic criterion.
Precedent	It may be a consideration or basis alongwith and in addition to social backwardness, but it can never be the sole criterion.
Precedent	This is the view uniformly taken by this <ORG> and we respectfully agree with the same.
Precedent	(b).
Precedent	Whether a backward class can be identified on the basis of occupation-cum-income without reference to caste?
Precedent	91.
Precedent	In Chitralekha, this <ORG> held that such an iden tification is permissible.
RatioOfTheDecision	We see no reason to differ with the said view inasmuch as this is but another method to find socially backward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	Indeed, this test in the Indian context is broadly the same as the one adopted by <ORG>.
Precedent	While answering Question 3(b), we said that identification of backward classes can be done with reference to castes alongwith other occupational groups, communities and classes.
Precedent	We did not say that that is the only permissible method.
Precedent	Indeed, there may be some groups or classes in whose case caste may not be relevant to all.
Precedent	For example, agricultural labourers, Rickshawpullers/drivers, street-hawkers etc.
Precedent	may well qualify for being designated as Backward Classes.
Precedent	Question No.
Precedent	5: Whether Backward Classes can be further divided into backward and more backward categories?
Precedent	92.
Precedent	In Balaji it was held "that the sub-classification made by the order between Backward Classes and more backward classes does not appear to be justified under Article 15(4).
Precedent	Article 15(4) au thorises special provision being made for the really backward classes.
Precedent	In introducing two categories of backward classes, what the impugned order, in substance, purports to do is to devise measures for the benefit of all the classes of citizens who are less advanced compared to the more advanced classes in the <ORG> and that, in our opinion, is not the scope of Article 15(4).
Precedent	The result of the method adopted by the impugned order is that nearly 90% of the population of the <ORG> is treated as backward, and that illustrates how the order in fact divides the population of the <ORG> into most advanced and the rest, and puts the latter into two categories of backward and more backward.
Precedent	The classification of the two categories, therefore, is not warranted by Article 15(4)."
Precedent	The correctness of this holding is questioned before us by the counsel for the respondents.
Precedent	It is submitted that in principle there is no justification for the said holding.
Precedent	It is submitted that even among backward classes there are some who ar e more backward than the others and that the backwardness is not and cannot be uniform throughout the country nor even within a <ORG>.
Precedent	In support of this contention, the Respondents rely upon the observations of <NAME>, J. in Vasant Kumar, where the learned judge said:  We do not see why on principle there cannot be a classification into Backward Classes and More Backward Classes, if both classes are not merely a little behind, but far far behind the most advanced classes.
RulingByLowerCourt	In fact such a classification would be necessary to help the More Backward Classes; otherwise those of the Backward Classes who might be a little more advanced than the More Backward Classes might walk away with all the seats.
RulingByLowerCourt	92A.
RulingByLowerCourt	We are of the opinion that there is no constitutional or legal bar to a <ORG> categorizing the backward classes as backward and more backward.
RulingByLowerCourt	We are not saying that it ought to be done.
RulingByLowerCourt	We are concerned with the question if a <ORG> makes such a categorisation, whether it would be invalid?
RulingByLowerCourt	We think not.
RulingByLowerCourt	Let us take the criteria evolved by <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Any caste, group or class which scored eleven or more points was treated as a backward class.
RatioOfTheDecision	Now, it is not as if all the several thousands of castes/groups/classes scored identical points.
RatioOfTheDecision	There may be some castes/groups/classes which have scored points between 20 to 22 and there may be some who have scored points between eleven and thirteen.
RatioOfTheDecision	It cannot reasonably be denied that there is no difference between these two sets of castes/groups/classes.
Precedent	To give an illustration, take two occupational groups viz., gold-smiths and vaddes (traditional stone-cutters in Andhra Pradesh) both included within Other Backward Classes.
Precedent	None can deny that gold-smiths are far less backward than vaddes.
Precedent	If both of them are grouped together and reservation provided, the inevitably result would be that gold-smiths would take away all the reserved posts leaving none for vaddes.
Precedent	In such a situation, a <ORG> may think it advisable to make a categorisation even among other back ward classes so as to ensure that the more backward among the backward classes obtain the benefits intended for them.
Precedent	Where to draw the line and how to effect the sub-classification is, however, a matter for the <ORG> and the <ORG> - and so long as it is reasonably done, the <ORG> may not intervene.
Precedent	In this connection, reference may be made to the categorisation obtaining in Andhra Pradesh.
Precedent	The Backward Classes have been divided into four categories.
Precedent	Group-A comprises of "Aboriginal tribes.
Precedent	Vimukta jatis.
Precedent	Nomadic and semi-nomadic tribes etc.".
Precedent	Group-B comprises professional group like tappers, weavers, carpenters, ironsmiths, goldsmiths, kamsalins etc.
Precedent	Group-C pertains to "Scheduled Castes converts to Christianity and their progency", while Group-D comprises of all other classes/communities/groups, which are not included in groups A, B and C. The 25% vacancies reserved for backward classes are sub-divided between them in proportion to their respective population.
Precedent	This categorisation was justified in Balr am [1972] 3 S.C.R.
Precedent	247 AT 286.
Precedent	This is merely to show that even among backward classes, there can be a sub-classification on a reasonable basis.
Precedent	There is another way of looking at this issue.
Precedent	Article 16(4) recognises only one class viz., "backward class of citizens".
Precedent	It does speak separately of Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes, as does Article 15(4).
Precedent	Even so, it is beyond controversy that Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes are also included in the expression "backward class of citizens" and that separate reservations can be provided in their favour.
Precedent	It is a well-accepted phenomenon throughout the country.
Precedent	What is the logic behind it?
Precedent	It is that if Scheduled Tribes, Scheduled Castes and Other Backward Classes are lumped together, O.B.Cs.
Precedent	will take away all the vacancies leaving Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes high and dry.
Precedent	The same logic also warrants categorisation as between more backward and backward.
RatioOfTheDecision	We do not mean to say - we may reiterate - that this should be done.
RatioOfTheDecision	We are only saying that  if a <ORG> chooses to do it, it is not impermissible in law.
Fact	PART - V (QUESTION NOS.
Fact	6, 7 AND 8) Question 6: To what extent can the reservation be made?
Fact	(a) Whether the 50% rule enunciated in Balaji a binding rule or only a rule of caution or rule of prudence?
Fact	(b) Whether the 50% rule, if any, is confined to reservations made under Clause (4) of Article 16 or whether it takes in all types of reservations that can be provided under Article 16?
Fact	(c) Further while applying 50% rule, if any, whether an year should be taken as a unit or whether the total strength of the cadre should be looked to ?
Precedent	93.
Precedent	In Balaji, <ORG> of this Court rejected the argument that in the absence of a limitation contained in Article 15(4 ), no limitation can be prescribed by the court on the extent of reservation.
Precedent	It observed that a provision under Article 15(4) being a "special provision" must be within reasonable limits.
Precedent	It may be appropriate to quote the relevant holding from the judgment:  When Article 15(4) refe rs to the special provision for the advancement of certain classes or Scheduled Castes or Scheduled Tribes, it must not be ignored that the provision which is authorised to be made is a special provision; it is not a provision which is exhaustive in character, so that in looking after the advancement of those classes, the <ORG> would be justified in ignoring altogether the advancement of the rest of the society.
Precedent	It is because the interests of the society at large would be served by promoting the advancement of the weaker elements in the society that Article 15(4) authorises special provision to be made.
Precedent	But if a provision which is in the nature of an exception completely excludes the rest of the society, that clearly is outside the scope of Article 15(4).
Precedent	It would be extremely unreasonable to assume that in enacting Article 15(4) the <ORG> intended to provide that where the advancement of the Backward Classes or the Scheduled Castes and Tribes was concerned, the fundamental rights of the citizens constit uting the rest of the society were to be completely and absolutely ignored....A Special provision contemplated by Article 15(4) like reservation for posts and appointments contemplated by Article 16(4) must be within reasonable limits.
RatioOfTheDecision	The interests of weaker sections of society which are a first charge on the <ORG> and the center have to be adjusted with the interests of the community as a whole.
RatioOfTheDecision	The adjustment of these competing claims is undoubtedly a difficult matter, but if under the guise of making a special provision, a <ORG> reserves practically all the seats available in all the colleges, that clearly would be adverting the object of Article 15(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	In this matter again, we are reluctant to say definitely what would be a proper provision to make.
RatioOfTheDecision	Speaking generally and in a broad way a special provision should be less than 50%; how much less than 50% would depend upon the relevant prevailing circumstances in each case.
RatioOfTheDecision	In Devadasan this rule of 50% was applied to a case arising under Article 16(4) an d on that basis the carry-forward rule was struck down.
RatioOfTheDecision	In <NAME>, however the correctness of this principle was questioned.
RatioOfTheDecision	<NAME> observed:  This means that the reservation should be within the permissible limits and should not be a cloak to fill all the posts belonging to a particular class of citizens and thus violate Article 16(1) of the Constitution indirectly.
RatioOfTheDecision	At the same time Clause (4) of Article 16 does not fix any limit on the power of the government to make reservation.
RatioOfTheDecision	Since Clause (4) is a part of Article 16 of the Constitution it is manifest that the <ORG> cannot be allowed to indulge in excessive reservation so as to defeat the policy contained in Article 16(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	As to what would be a suitable reservation within permissible limits will depend upon the facts and circumstances of each case and no hard and fast rule can be laid down, nor can this matter be reduced to a mathematical formula so as to be adhered to in all cases.
RatioOfTheDecision	Decided cases of this <ORG> have no doubt laid down that the perc entage of reservation should not exceed 50%.
RatioOfTheDecision	As I read the authorities, this is however, a rule of caution and does not exhaust all categories.
RatioOfTheDecision	Suppose for instance a <ORG> has a large number of backward class of citizens which constitute 80% of the population and the <ORG>, in order to give them proper representation, reserves 80% of the jobs for them can it be said that the percentage of reservation is bad and violates the permissible limits of Clause (4) of Article 16?
RatioOfTheDecision	The answer must necessarily be in the negative.
RatioOfTheDecision	The dominant object to this provision is to take steps to make inadequate representation adequate.
RatioOfTheDecision	<NAME>, J. agreed with the view taken by <NAME>, J. in the following words:  I agree with my learned brother <NAME>, J. in the view that the arithmatical limit of 50% in any one year set by some earlier rulings cannot perhaps be pressed too far.
RatioOfTheDecision	Overall representation in a department does not depend on recruitment in a particular year, but the total strength of a cadre.
RatioOfTheDecision	I agree w ith his construction of Article 16(4) and his view about the carry forward' rule.
RatioOfTheDecision	<NAME>, <NAME> did not specifically deal with this aspect but from the principles of 'proportional equality' and 'equality of results' espoused by the learned Judge, it is argued that he did not accept the 50% rule.
Precedent	<NAME>, <NAME> also did not refer to this rule but the following sentence occurs in his judgment at pages 962 and 963:  If a reservation of posts under Article 16(4) for employees of backward classes could include complete reservation of higher posts to which they could be promoted, about which there could be no doubt now, I fail to see why it cannot be partial or for a part of the duration of service and hedged round with the condition that a temporary promotion would operate as a complete and confirmed promotion only if the temporary promotee satisfies some tests within a given time.
Precedent	<NAME>, C.<NAME>, did not dispute the correctness of the 50% rule but at the same time he pointed out that this percentage should be applied to the e ntire service as a whole.
Precedent	After the decision in <NAME>, controversy arose whether the 50% rule enunciated in <NAME> stands overruled by <NAME> or does it continue to be valid.
Precedent	In <NAME>, two learned judges came to precisely opposite conclusions on this question.
Precedent	<NAME> held that <NAME> has the effect of undoing the 50% rule in <NAME> whereas <NAME>, J. held that it does not.
Precedent	94.
Precedent	It is argued before us that the observations on the said question in <NAME> were obiter and do not constitute a decision so as to have the effect of overruling <NAME>.
Precedent	Reliance is also placed upon the speech of Dr. <NAME> in <ORG>, where he said that reservation must be confined to a minority of seats (See para 28).
Precedent	It is also pointed out that <NAME>, J. who agreed with <NAME>, J. in <NAME> on this aspect, came back to, and affirmed, the 50% rule in <ORG> (at pp.
Precedent	241 and 242).
Precedent	On the other hand, it is argued for the respondents that when the population of the other b ackward classes is more than 50% of the total population, the reservation in their favour (excluding Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes) can also be 50%.
Precedent	94A.
Precedent	We must, however, point out that Clause (4) speaks of adequate representation and not proportionate representation.
Precedent	Adequate representation cannot be read as proportionate representation.
Precedent	Principle of proportionate representation is accepted only in Articles 330 and 332 of the Constitution and that too for a limited period.
Precedent	These articles speak of reservation of seats in <ORG> and the State <ORG> in favour of Scheduled Tribes and Scheduled Castes proportionate to their population, but they are only temporary and special provisions.
Precedent	It is therefore not possible to accept the theory of proportionate representation though the proportion of population of backward classes to the total population would certainly be relevant.
Precedent	Just as every power must be exercised reasonably and fairly, the power conferred by Clause (4) of Article 16 should also  be exercised in a fair manner and within reasonably limits - and what is more reasonable than to say that reservation under Clause (4) shall not exceed 50% of the appointments or posts, barring certain extra-ordinary situations as explained hereinafter.
Precedent	From this point of view, the 27% reservation provided by the impugned Memorandums in favour of backward classes is well within the reasonable limits.
Precedent	Together with reservation in favour of Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes, it comes to a total of 49.5%.
Precedent	In this connection, reference may be had to the <ORG> decision of <ORG> in <CITATION_1830078> 1987 A.P.
Precedent	53, striking down the enhancement of reservation from 25% to 44% for O.B.Cs.
Precedent	The said enhancement had the effect of taking the total reservation under Article 16(4) to 65%.
Precedent	It needs no emphasis to say that the principle aim of Article 14 and 16 is equality and equality of opportunity and that Clause (4) of Article 16 is but a means of achieving the very same objective.
Precedent	Clause  (4) is a special provision - though not an exception to Clause (1).
Precedent	Both the provisions have to be harmonised keeping in mind the fact that both are but the restatements of the principle of equality enshrined in Article 14.
Precedent	The provision under Article 16(4) - conceived in the interest of certain sections of society - should be balanced against the guarantee of equality enshrined in Clause (1) of Article 16 which is a guarantee held out to every citizen and to the entire society.
Precedent	It is relevant to point out that Dr. <NAME> himself contemplated reservation being "confined to a minority of seats" (See his speech in <ORG>, set out in para 28).
RatioOfTheDecision	No other member of the <ORG> suggested otherwise.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is, thus clear that reservation of a majority of seats was never envisaged by the founding fathers.
RatioOfTheDecision	Nor are we satisfied that the present context requires us to depart from that concept.
RatioOfTheDecision	From the above discussion, the irresistible conclusion that follows is that the reservations contempla ted in Clause (4) of Article 16 should not exceed 50%.
RatioOfTheDecision	While 50% shall be the rule, it is necessary not to put out of consideration certain extraordinary situations inherent in the great diversity of this country and the people.
Precedent	It might happen that in far-flung and remote areas the population inhabiting those areas might, on account of their being out of the main stream of national life and in view of conditions peculiar to and characteristical to them, need to be treated in a different way, some relaxation in this strict rule may become imperative.
Precedent	In doing so, extreme caution is to be exercised and a special case made out.
Precedent	In this connection it is well to remember that the reservations under Article 16(4) do not operate like a communal reservation.
Precedent	It may well happen that some members belonging to, say Scheduled Castes get selected in the open competition field on the basis of their own merit; they will not be counted against the quota reserved for Scheduled Castes; they will be treated as open competiti on candidates.
Precedent	95.
Precedent	We are also of the opinion that this rule of 50% applies only to reservations in favour of backward classes made under Article 16(4).
Precedent	A little clarification is in order at this juncture: all reservations are not of the same nature.
Precedent	There are two types of reservations, which may, for the sake of convenience, be referred to as 'vertical reservations' and 'horizontal reservations'.
Precedent	The reservations in favour of Scheduled Castes, Scheduled Tribes and other backward classes [under Article 16(4)] may be called vertical reservations whereas reservations in favour of physically handicapped [under Clause (1) of Article 16] can be referred to as horizontal reservations.
Precedent	Horizontal reservations cut across the vertical reservations that is called inter-locking reservations.
Precedent	To be more precise, suppose 3% of the vacancies are reserved in favour of physically handicapped persons; this would be a reservation relatable to Clause (1) of Article 16.
Precedent	The persons selected against this quota will be placed in  the appropriate category; if he belongs to S.C. category he will be placed in that quota by making necessary adjustments; similarly, if he belongs to open competition (O.C.)
Precedent	category, he will be placed in that category by making necessary adjustments.
Precedent	Even after providing for these horizontal reservations, the percentage of reservations in favour of backward class of citizens remains - and should remain - the same.
Precedent	This is how these reservations are worked out in several States and there is no reason not to continue that procedure.
Precedent	It is, however, made clear that the rule of 50% shall be applicable only to reservations proper; they shall not be - indeed cannot be - applicable to exemptions, concessions or relaxations, if any provided to 'Backward Class of Citizens' under Article 16(4).
Precedent	96.
Precedent	The next aspect of this question is whether an year should be taken as the unit or the total strength of the cadre, for the purpose of applying the 50% rule.
Precedent	<ORG> does not deal with this aspect but Devadasan (majority  opinion) does.
Precedent	<NAME>, J. speaking for the majority says:  We would like to emphasise that the guarantee contained in Article 16(1) is for ensuring equality of opportunity for all citizens relating to employment, and to appointments to any office under the <ORG>.
Precedent	This means that on every occasion for recruitment the <ORG> should see that all citizens are treated equally.
Precedent	The guarantee is to each individual citizen and, therefore, every citizen who is seeking employment or appointment to an office under the <ORG> is entitled to be afforded an opportunity for seeking such employment or appointment whenever it is intended to be filled.
Precedent	In order to effectuate the guarantee each year of recruitment will have to be considered by itself and the reservation for backward communities should not be so excessive as to create a monopoly or to disturb unduly the legitimate claims of other communities.
Precedent	On the other hand is the approach adopted by <NAME>, C.J.
Precedent	in Thomas.
Precedent	While not disputing the correctness of the 50% rule h e seems to apply it to the entire service as such.
Precedent	In our opinion, the approach adopted by <NAME>, C.J.
Precedent	would not be consistent with Article 16.
Precedent	True it is that the backward classes, who are victims of historical social injustice, which has not ceased fully as yet, are not properly represented in the services under the <ORG> but it may not be possible to redress this imbalance in one go, i.e., in a year or two.
Precedent	The position can be better explained by taking an illustration.
Precedent	Take a unit/service/cadre comprising 1000 posts.
Precedent	The reservation in favour of Scheduled Tribes, Scheduled Castes and Other Backward Classes is 50% which means that out of the 1000 posts 500 must be held by the members of these classes i.e., 270 by other backward classes, 150 by Scheduled Castes and 80 by Scheduled Tribes.
RatioOfTheDecision	At a given point of time, let us say, the number of members of O.B.Cs.
RatioOfTheDecision	in the unit/service/category is only 50, a short fall of 220.
RatioOfTheDecision	Similarly the number of members of Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes is only 20 and 5 r espectively, shortfall of 130 and 75.
RatioOfTheDecision	If the entire service/cadre is taken as a unit and the backlog is sought to be made up, then the open competition channel has to be choked altogether for a number of years until the number of members of all backward classes reaches 500, i.e., till the quota meant for each of them is filled up.
RatioOfTheDecision	This may take quite a number of years because the number of vacancies arising each year are not many.
RatioOfTheDecision	Meanwhile, the members of open competition category would become age barred and ineligible.
RatioOfTheDecision	Equality of opportunity in their case would become a mere mirage.
RatioOfTheDecision	It must be remembered that the equality of opportunity guaranteed by Clause (1) is to each individual citizen of the country while Clause (4) contemplates special provision being made in favour of socially disadvantaged classes.
RulingByPresentCourt	Both must be balanced against each other.
RulingByPresentCourt	Neither should be allowed to eclipse the other.
RatioOfTheDecision	For the above reason, we hold that for the purpose of applying the rule of 50% an year should be taken as the un it and not the entire strength of the cadre, service or the unit, as the case may be.
RatioOfTheDecision	(d) Was Devadasan correctly decided?
Precedent	97.
Precedent	The rule (providing for carry forward of unfilled reserved vacancies as modified in 1955) struck down in Devadasan read as follows:  3(a) If a sufficient number of candidate considered suitable by the recruiting authorities, are not available from the communities for whom reservations are made in a particular year, the unfilled vacancies should be treated as unreserved and filled by the best available candidates.
Precedent	The number of reserved vacancies thus treated as unreserved will be added as an additional quota to the number that would be reserved in the following year in the normal course; and to the extent to which approved candidates are not available in that year against this additional quota, a corresponding addition should be made to the number of reserved vacancies in the second following year.
Precedent	The facts of the case relevant for our purpose are the following:  (i) Reservation i n favour of Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes was 12 1/2% and 5% respectively;  (ii) In 1960, <ORG> issued a notification proposing to hold a limited competitive examination for promotion to the category of Assistant Superintendents in <ORG>.
Precedent	48 vacancies were to be filled, out of which 16 were unreserved while 32 were reserved for Scheduled Castes/Scheduled Tribes, because of the operation of the carry forward Rule: 28 vacancies were actually carried forward;  (iii) <ORG> recommended 16 for unreserved and 30 for reserved vacancies - a total of 46;  (iv) the <ORG> however appointed in all 45 persons, out of whom 29 belonged to Scheduled Castes/Scheduled Tribes.
Precedent	The said Rule and the appointments made on that basis were questioned mainly on the ground that they violated the 50% rule enunciated in Balaji.
Precedent	It was submitted that by virtue of the carry forward Rule, 65% of the vacancies for the year in question came to be reserved for Scheduled Castes/Scheduled Tribes.
Precedent	The m ajority, speaking through Mudholkar,J.
Precedent	upheld the contention of the petitioners and struck down the Rule purporting to apply the principle of <NAME>.
Precedent	The vice of the Rule was pointed out in the following wards:  In order to appreciate better the import of this rule on recruitment, let us take an illustration.
Precedent	Supposing in two successive years no candidate from amongst the Scheduled Castes and Tribes is found to be qualified for filling any of the reserved posts.
Precedent	Supposing also that in each of those two years the number of vacancies to be filled in a particular service was 100.
Precedent	The reserved vacancies for each of those years would, according to the <ORG> resolution, be 18 for each year.
Precedent	Now, since these vacancies were not filled in those years a total of 36 vacancies will be carried forward to the third year.
Precedent	Supposing in the third year also the number of vacancies to be filled is 100.
Precedent	Then 18 vacancies out of these will also have to be reserved for members of the Scheduled Castes and Tribes.
Precedent	By operation  of the carry forward rule the vacancies to be filled by persons from amongst the Scheduled Castes and Tribes would be 54 as against 46 by persons from amongst the more advanced classes.
Precedent	The reservation would thus be more than 50%.
Precedent	98.
RulingByPresentCourt	We are of the respectful opinion that on its own reasoning, the decision in so far as it strikes down the Rule is not sustainable.
RulingByPresentCourt	The most that could have been done in that case was to quash the appointments in excess of 50%, inasmuch as, as a matter of fact, more than 50% of the vacancies for the year 1960 came to be reserved by virtue of the said Rule.
RatioOfTheDecision	But it would not be correct to presume that that is the necessary and the only consequence of that rule.
RatioOfTheDecision	Let us take the very illustration given at pp.
RatioOfTheDecision	691-2, - namely 100 vacancies arising in three successive years and 18% being the reservation quota - and examine.
RatioOfTheDecision	Take a case, where in the first year, out of 18 reserved vacancies 9 are filled up and 9 are carried forward.
RatioOfTheDecision	Similarly, in the second year again, 9 are filled up  and another 9 are carried forward.
RatioOfTheDecision	Result would be that in the third year, 9 + 9 + 18 = 36 (out of a total of 100) would be reserved which would be far less than 50%; the rule in Balaji is not violated.
RatioOfTheDecision	But by striking down the Rule itself, carrying forward of vacancies even in such a situation has become impermissible, which appears to us indefensible in principle.
RatioOfTheDecision	We may also point out that the premise made in Balaji and reiterated in <NAME>, to the effect that Clause (4) is an exception to Clause (1) is no longer acceptable, having been given up in <NAME>.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is for this reason that in <ORG>, <NAME>, J. explained <NAME> in the following words:  In <NAME>'s case the court went into the actuals, not into the hypotheticals.
RatioOfTheDecision	This is most important.
RatioOfTheDecision	The <ORG> actually verified the degree of deprivation of the 'equal opportunity' right....  .... What is striking is that the <ORG> did not take an academic view or make a notional evaluation but checked up to satisfy itself about the serio usness of the infraction of the right....Mathematical calculations, departing from realities of the case, may startle us without justification, the apprehension being misplaced.
RatioOfTheDecision	All that we need say is that <ORG> shall take care to issue instructions to see that in no year shall <ORG> candidates be actually appointed to substantially more than 50% of the promotional posts.
RulingByPresentCourt	Some excess will not affect as mathematical precision is different in human affairs, but substantial excess will void the selection.
RulingByPresentCourt	Subject to this rider or condition that the 'carry forward' rule shall not result, in any given year, in the selection of appointments of <ORG> candidates considerably in excess of 50% we uphold Annexure I.
RulingByPresentCourt	We are in respectful agreement with the above statement of law.
RulingByPresentCourt	Accordingly, we over-rule the decision in Devadasan.
RulingByPresentCourt	We have already discussed and explained the 50% rule in paras 93 to 96.
Precedent	The same position would apply in the case of carry forward rule as well.
Precedent	We, however, agree that an year s hould be taken as the unit or basis, as the case may be, for applying the rule of 50% and not the entire cadre strength.
Precedent	99.
Precedent	We may reiterate that a carry forward rule need not necessarily be in the same terms as the one found in Devadasan.
Precedent	A given rule may say that the unfilled reserved vacancies shall not be filled by unreserved category candidates but shall be carried forward as such for a period of three years.
Precedent	In such a case, a contention may be raised that reserved posts remain a separate category altogether.
Precedent	In our opinion, however, the result of application of carry forward rule, in whatever manner it is operated, should not result in breach of 50% rule.
Precedent	Question No, 7: Whether Clause (4) of Article 16 provides reservation only in the matter of initial appointments/direct recruitment or does it contemplate and provide for reservations being made in the matter of promotion as well?
Precedent	100.
Precedent	The petitioner's submission is that the reservation of appointments or posts contemplated by Clause (4) is only at  the stage of entry into <ORG> service, i.e., direct recruitment.
Precedent	It is submitted that providing for reservation thereafter in the matter of promotion amounts to a double reservation and if such a provision is made at each successive stage of promotion it would be a case of reservation being provided that many times.
Precedent	It is also submitted that by providing reservation in the matter of promotion, the member of a reserved category is enabled to frog-leap over his compatriots, which was bound to generate acute heart - burning and may well lead to inefficiency in administration.
RatioOfTheDecision	The members of the open competition category would come to think that whatever be their record and performance, the members of reserved categories would steal a march over them, irrespective of their performance and competence.
RatioOfTheDecision	Examples are given how two persons (A) and (B), one belonging to O.C.
RatioOfTheDecision	category and the other belonging to reserved category, having been appointed at the same time, the member of the reserved category gets promoted  earlier and how even in the promoted category he jumps over the members of the O.C.
RatioOfTheDecision	category already there and gains a further promotion and so on.
RatioOfTheDecision	This would generate, it is submitted, a feeling of dis-heartening which kills the spirit of competition and develops a sense of dis-interestedness among the members of O.C.
RatioOfTheDecision	category.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is pointed out that once persons coming from different sources join a category or class, they must be treated alike thereafter in all matters including promotions and that no distinction is permissible on the basis of their "birth-mark".
RatioOfTheDecision	It is also pointed out that even the <ORG> debates on draft Article 10(3) do not indicate in any manner that it was supposed to extend to promotions as well.
Argument	It is further submitted that if Article 16(4) is construed as warranting reservation even in the matter of promotion it would be contrary to the mandate of Article 335 viz., maintenance of efficiency in administration.
Argument	It is submitted that such a provision would amount to puttin g a premium upon in-efficiency.
RatioOfTheDecision	The members of the reserved category would not work hard since they do not have to compete with all their colleagues but only within the reserved category and further because they are assured of promotion whether they work hard and efficiently or not.
RatioOfTheDecision	Such a course would also militate against the goal of excellence referred to in Clause (J) of Article 51A (Fundamental Duties).
RatioOfTheDecision	101.
RatioOfTheDecision	<NAME>, learned Counsel appearing for <ORG> raised a preliminary objection to the consideration of this question at all.
RatioOfTheDecision	According to him, this question does not arise at present inasmuch as the impugned Memorandums do not provide for reservation in the matter of promotion.
RatioOfTheDecision	They confine the reservation only to direct recruitment.
RatioOfTheDecision	Learned counsel reiterated the well-established principle of Constitutional Law that Constitutional questions should not be decided in vacuum and that they must be decided only if and when they arise properly on the pleadings of a given case and where  it is found necessary to decide them for a proper decision of the case.
RatioOfTheDecision	A large number of decisions of this <ORG> and English courts are relied upon in support of this proposition.
RatioOfTheDecision	If for any reason this <ORG> decides to answer the said question, says the counsel, the answer can only be one - which is already given by this <ORG> in a number of decisions namely, <ORG>, <ORG> and <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	He submits that an appointment to a post is made either by direct recruitment or by promotion or by transfer.
RatioOfTheDecision	In all these cases it is but an appointment.
RatioOfTheDecision	If so, Article 16(4) does undoubtedly take in and warrant making a provision for reservation in the matter of promotion as well.
RatioOfTheDecision	Learned counsel commended to us the further reasoning in <ORG> that adequate representation means not merely quantitative representation but also qualitative representation.
RatioOfTheDecision	He says further that adequacy in representation does not mean representation at the lowest level alone but at all levels in the administration.
RatioOfTheDecision	Regarding  the <ORG> debates, his submission is that those debates do not indicate that the said provision was not supposed to apply to promotions.
RatioOfTheDecision	In such a situation, it is argued, plain words of the Constitution should be given their due meaning and that there is no warrant for cutting down their ambit on the basis of certain suppositions with respect to interpretation of Clauses (1), (2) and (4).
Precedent	This is also the contention of the other counsel for respondents.
Precedent	102.
RatioOfTheDecision	With respect to the preliminary objection of <NAME>, there can hardly be any dispute about the proposition espoused by him.
RatioOfTheDecision	But it must be remembered that reference to this larger <ORG> was made with a view to "finally settle the legal position relating to reservations".
RatioOfTheDecision	The idea was to have a final look at the said question by a larger <ORG> to settle the law in an authoritative way.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is for this reason that we have been persuaded to express ourselves on this question.
RatioOfTheDecision	But before we proceed to express ourselves on the question,  a few clarifications would be in order.
RatioOfTheDecision	103.
RatioOfTheDecision	Reservation in the case of promotion is normally provided only where the promotion is by selection, i.e., on the basis of merit.
RatioOfTheDecision	For, if the promotion is on the basis of seniority, such a rule may not be called for; in such a case the position obtaining in the lower category gets reflected in the higher category (promotion category) also.
RatioOfTheDecision	Where, however, promotion is based on merit, it may happen that members of backward classes may not get selected in the same proportion as is obtaining in the lower category.
RatioOfTheDecision	With a view to ensure similar representation in the higher category also, reservation is thought of even in the matter of promotion based on selection.
RatioOfTheDecision	This is, of course, in addition to the provision for reservation at the entry (direct recruitment) level.
RatioOfTheDecision	This was the position in Rangachari.
RatioOfTheDecision	Secondly, there may be a service/class/category, to which appointment is made partly by direct recruitment and partly by promotion (i.e., promotion on the basis of mer it).
RatioOfTheDecision	If no provision is made for reservation in promotions, the backward class members may not be represented in this category to the extent prescribed.
RatioOfTheDecision	We may give an illustration to explain what we are saying.
RatioOfTheDecision	Take the category of Assistant Engineers in a particular service where 50% of the vacancies arising in a year are filled up by direct recruitment and 50% by promotion (by selection i.e., on merit basis) from among Junior Engineers.
RatioOfTheDecision	If provision for reservation is made only in the matter of direct recruitment but not in promotions, the result may be that members of backward classes (where quota, let us say, is 25%) would get in to that extent only in the 50% direct recruitment quota but may not get in to that extent in the balance 50% promotion quota.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is for this reason that reservation is thought of even in the matter of promotions, particularly where promotions are on the basis of merit.
RatioOfTheDecision	The question for our consideration, however, is whether Article 16(4) contemplates and permits reservation only  in the matter of direct recruitment or whether it also warrants provision being made for reservation in the matter of promotions as well.
Precedent	For answering this question, it would be appropriate, in the first instance, to examine the facts of and dicta in Rangachari, Hiralal and Karamchari Sangh.
Precedent	104.
Precedent	In Rangachari, validity of the circulars issued by the <ORG> administration providing for reservation in favour of Scheduled Castes/Scheduled Tribes in promotions (by selection) was questioned.
Precedent	The contention was that Article 16(4) does not take in or comprehend reservation in the matter of promotions as well and that it is confined to direct recruitment only.
Precedent	<ORG> agreed with this contention.
Precedent	It held that the word "appointments" in Clause (4) did not denote promotion and further that the word "posts" in the said clause referred to posts outside the cadre concerned.
Precedent	On appeal, this Court reversed by a majority of 3:2, <NAME>, <NAME> speaking for the majority enunciated certain propositions,  of which the following are relevant for our discussion:  (a) matters relating to employment [in Clause (1)] must include all matters in relation to employment both prior, and subsequent, to the employment which are incidental to the employment and form part of the terms and conditions of such employment.
Precedent	(b) in regard to employment, like other terms and conditions associated with and incidental to it, the promotion to a selection post is also included in the matters relating to employment, and even in regard to such a promotion to a selection post all that Article 16(1) guarantees is equality of opportunity to all citizens who enter service.
Precedent	(c) The condition precedent for the exercise of the powers conferred by Article 16(4) is that the <ORG> ought to be satisfied that any backward class of citizens is not adequately represented in its services.
Precedent	This condition precedent may refer either to the numerical inadequacy of representation in the services or even to the qualitative inadequacy of representation.
Precedent	Th e advancement of the socially and educationally backward classes requires not only that they should have adequate representation in the lowest rung of services but that they should aspire to secure adequate representation in selection posts in the services as well.
Precedent	In the context the expression 'adequately represented' imports considerations of "size" as well as "values", numbers as well as the nature of appointments held and so it involves not merely the numerical test but also the qualitative one.
Precedent	(b) in providing for the reservation of appointments or posts under Article 16(4 ), the <ORG> has to take into consideration the claims of the members of the backward classes consistently with the maintenance of the efficiency of administration.
Precedent	It must not be forgotten that the efficiency of administration is of such paramount importance that it would be unwise and impermissible to make any reservation at the cost of efficiency of administration.
Precedent	That undoubtedly is the effect of Article 335.
Precedent	Reservation of appo intments or posts may theoretically and conceivably mean some impairment of efficiency; but the risk involved in sacrificing efficiency of administration must always be borne in mind when any <ORG> sets about making a provision for reservation of appointments of posts.
Precedent	105.
Precedent	<CITATION_806288> , validity of an order made by <ORG> providing for reservation in promotion (in addition to initial recruitment) was questioned.
Precedent	Though <ORG> upheld the challenge, this Court (<NAME>, <NAME> and <NAME>, JJ.)
Precedent	reversed and upheld the validity of the Government order following <NAME>.
Precedent	106.
Precedent	Validity of a number of circulars issued by <ORG> was questioned in Karamchari Sangh, a petition under Article 32.
Precedent	The experience gained over the years disclosed that reservation of appointments/posts in favour of SC/STs, though made both at the stage of initial recruitment and promotion was not achieving the intended results, inasmuch as several posts meant for them remained unfilled by  them.
Precedent	Accordingly, the <ORG> issued several circulars from time to time tending further concessions and other measures to ensure that members of these categories avail of the posts reserved for them fully.
Precedent	(The original circular is referred to in the judgment as Ann.-F, whose validity was upheld in <NAME> itself.
Precedent	The other circulars are referred to as Annexures I, H, J and K).
Precedent	These circulars contemplated (i) giving one grade higher to <ORG> candidates than is assignable to an employee (ii) carrying forward vacancies for a period of three years and (iii) provision for in-service training and coaching (after promotion) to raise the level of efficiency of <ORG> employees who were directed to be promoted on a temporary basis for a specified period, even if they did not obtain the requisite places.
Precedent	The contention of the writ petitioners was that these circulars, being inconsistent with the mandate of Article 335 , are bad.
Precedent	<NAME> was sought to be reopened by arguing that Article 16(4) does not ta ke in reservation in the matter of promotion.
Precedent	<ORG> (<NAME>, <NAME> and <NAME>, JJ.)
Precedent	not only refused to re-open Rangachari but also repelled the attack upon the circulars.
Precedent	It was held that no dilution of efficiency in administration resulted from the implementation of the circulars inasmuch as they preserved the criteria of eligibility and minimum efficiency required and also provided for in-service training and coaching to correct the deficiencies, if any.
Precedent	The carry forward rule was also upheld subject to the condition that the operation of the rule shall not result, in any given year, selection/appointment of Scheduled Caste/Scheduled Tribe candidates in excess of 50%.
Precedent	<CITATION_1685522> , it was held:  It is now well settled by decisions of this Court that the reservation in favour of backward classes of citizens including the members of the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes, as contemplated by Article 16(4) can be made not merely in respect of initial recruitment but  also in respect of posts to which promotions are to be made.
Precedent	[See for instance: and <CITATION_1111529> .
Precedent	1 S.C.
Precedent	246.]
Precedent	107.
Precedent	We find it difficult to agree with the view in Rangachari that Article 16(4) contemplates or permits reservation in promotions as well.
Precedent	It is true that the expression "appointment" takes in appointment by direct recruitment, appointment by promotion and appointment by transfer.
Precedent	It may also be that Article 16(4) contemplates not merely quantitative but also qualitative support to backward class of citizens.
Precedent	But this question has not to be answered on a reading of Article 16(4) alone but on a combined reading of Article 16(4) and Article 335.
Precedent	In Rangachari this fact was acknowledged but explained away on a basis which, with great respect to the learned Judges who constituted the majority - does not appear to be acceptable.
Precedent	The propositions emerging from the majority opinion in Rangachari have been set out in Para 104.
Precedent	Under proposition (d) (as set out in para 104), the majority does say t hat "in providing for the reservation of appointments or posts under Article 16(4 ), the <ORG> has to take into consideration the claims of the members of the backward classes consistently with the maintenance of the efficiency of administration.
Precedent	It must not be forgotten that the efficiency of administration is of such paramount importance that it would be unwise and impermissible to make any reservation at the cost of efficiency of administration.
Precedent	That undoubtedly is the effect of Article 335.
Precedent	Reservation of appointments or posts may theoretically and conceivably means some impairment of efficiency;" but then it explains it away by saying "but the risk involved in sacrificing efficiency of administration must always be borne in mind when any <ORG> sets about making a provision for reservation of appointments of posts."
RatioOfTheDecision	We see no justification to multiply 'the risk', which would be the consequence of holding that reservation can be provided even in the matter of promotion.
RatioOfTheDecision	While it is certainly just to say th at a handicap should be given to backward class of citizens at the stage of initial appointment, it would be a serious and unacceptable inroad into the rule of equality of opportunity to say that such a handicap should be provided at every stage of promotion throughout their career.
RatioOfTheDecision	That would mean creation of a permanent separate category apart from the mainstream - a vertical division of the administrative apparatus.
RatioOfTheDecision	The members of reserved categories need not have to compete with others but only among themselves.
RatioOfTheDecision	There would be no will to work, compete and excel among them.
RatioOfTheDecision	Whether they work or not, they tend to think, their promotion is assured.
RatioOfTheDecision	This in turn is bound to generate a feeling of despondence and 'heart-burning' among open competition members.
RatioOfTheDecision	All this is bound to affect the efficiency of administration.
RatioOfTheDecision	Putting the members of backward classes on a fast-track would necessarily result in leap-fogging and the deleterious effects of "leap-fogging" need no illustration at our hands.
RatioOfTheDecision	At the initial  stage of recruitment reservation can be made in favour of backward class of citizens but once they enter the service, efficiency of administration demands that these members too compete with others and earn promotion like all others; no further distinction can be made thereafter with reference to their "birth-mark", as one of the learned Judges of this Court has said in another connection.
RatioOfTheDecision	They are expected to operate on equal footing with others.
RatioOfTheDecision	Crutches cannot be provided throughout one's career.
RatioOfTheDecision	That would not be in the interest of efficiency of administration nor in the larger interest of the nation.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is wrong to think that by holding so, we are confining the backward class of citizens to the lowest cadres.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is well-known that direct recruitment takes place at several higher levels of administration and not merely at the level of Class-IV and Class-Ill.
RatioOfTheDecision	Direct recruitment is provided even at the level of <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Direct recruitment is provided at the level of District Judges, to give an ex ample nearer home.
RatioOfTheDecision	It may also be noted that during the debates in <ORG>, none referred to reservation in promotions; it does not appear to have been within their contemplation.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is true that Rangachari has been the law for more than 30 years and that attempts to re-open the issue were repelled in <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	It may equally be true that on the basis of that decision, reservation may have been provided in the matter of promotion in some of the <ORG> and State services but we are convinced that the majority opinion in Rangachari, to the extent it holds, that Article 16(4) permits reservation even in the matter of promotion, is not sustainable in principle and ought to be departed from.
RulingByPresentCourt	However, taking into consideration all the circumstances, we direct that our decision on this question shall operate only prospectively and shall not affect promotions already made, whether on temporary, officiating or regular/permanent basis.
Statute	It is further directed that wherever reservations are alr eady provided in the matter of promotion - be it <ORG> or <ORG>, or for that matter services under any corporation, authority or body falling under the definition of 'State' in Article 12- such reservations shall continue in operation for a period of five years from this day.
RatioOfTheDecision	Within this period, it would be open to the appropriate authorities to revise modify or reissue the relevant <ORG> to ensure the achievement of the objective of Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	If any authority thinks that for ensuring adequate representation of 'backward class of citizens' in any service, class or category, it is necessary to provide for direct recruitment therein, it shall be open to it do so.
RatioOfTheDecision	A purist or a legal theoretician may find this direction a little illogical.
RatioOfTheDecision	We can only answer them in the words of Lord <NAME>.
Precedent	In his presidential address to <ORG> at <ORG> on February 29, 1984 on the subject "Law Lords, Reactionaries or Reformers?
Precedent	", the learned Law Lord said:  Legal polic y now stands enthroned and will I hope remain one of the foremost considerations governing the development by <ORG> of the common law.
Precedent	What direction should this development now take?
Precedent	I can think of several occasions upon which we have all said to ourselves "this case requires a policy decision - what is the right policy decision?"
RatioOfTheDecision	The answer is, and I hope will hereafter be, to follow that route which is most consonant with the current needs of the society, and which will be seen to be sensible and will pragmatically thereafter be easy to apply.
RatioOfTheDecision	No doubt the Law Lords will continue to be the targets for those academic lawyers who will seek intellectual perfection rather than imperfect pragmatism.
RatioOfTheDecision	But much of the common law and virtually all criminal law, distasteful as it may be to some to have to acknowledge it, is a blunt instrument by means of which human beings, whether they like it or not, are governed and subject to which they are required to live, and blunt instruments are rarely perfect  intellectually or otherwise.
RatioOfTheDecision	By definition they operate bluntly and not sharply.
RatioOfTheDecision	We must also make it clear that it would not be impermissible for the <ORG> to extend concessions and relaxations to members of reserved categories in the matter of promotion without compromising the efficiency of the administration.
RatioOfTheDecision	The relaxation concerned in <NAME> and the concessions namely carrying forward of vacancies and provisions for in-service coaching/training in <ORG> are instances of such concessions and relaxations.
RatioOfTheDecision	However, it would not be permissible to prescribe lower qualifying marks or a lesser level of evaluation for the members of reserved categories since that would compromise the efficiency of administration.
RatioOfTheDecision	We reiterate that while it may be permissible to prescribe a reasonably lesser qualifying marks or evaluation for the O.B.Cs., S.Cs.
Precedent	and S.Ts.
Precedent	consistent with the efficiency of administration and the nature of duties attaching to the office concerned - in the matter of direct recruitment, s uch a course would not be permissible in the matter of promotions for the reasons recorded hereinabove.
Precedent	Question No.
Precedent	8: Whether Reservations are anti-meritarian?
Precedent	108.
Precedent	In <NAME> and other cases, it was assumed that reservations are necessarily anti-meritarian.
RatioOfTheDecision	For example, in <NAME> it was observed, "it is implicit in the idea of reservation that a less meritorious person be preferred to another who is more meritorious."
RatioOfTheDecision	To the same effect is the opinion of <NAME>, J. in <NAME>, though it is a minority opinion.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even <NAME>, J. who did not agree with this view did recognize some force in it.
RatioOfTheDecision	In his dissenting opinion in Devadasan, While holding that there is no conflict between Article 16(4) and Article 335 , he did say, "it is inevitable in the nature of reservation that there will be a lowering of standards to some extent", but, he said, on that account the provision cannot be said to be bad, inasmuch as in that case, the <ORG> had, as a matter of fact, prescribed minimum qualifications, a nd only those possessing such minimum qualifications were appointed.
RatioOfTheDecision	This view was, however, not accepted by <NAME>, J. in <NAME>.
RatioOfTheDecision	He said "efficiency means, in terms of good government, not marks in examinations only, but responsible and responsive service to the people.
RatioOfTheDecision	A chaotic genius is a grave danger to public administration.
RatioOfTheDecision	The inputs of efficiency rule include a sense of belonging and of accountability (not pejoratively used) if its composition takes in also the weaker segments of "We, the people of India".
RatioOfTheDecision	No other understanding can reconcile the claim of a radical present and the hangover of the unjust past."
Argument	A similar view was expressed in Vasant Kumer by <NAME>, J.
Argument	The learned judge said "the mere securing of high marks at an examination may not necessarily mark out a good administrator.
Argument	An efficient administrator, one takes it, must be one who possesses among other qualities the capacity to understand with sympathy and, therefore, to tackle bravely the problems of a large segment  of population constituting the weaker sections of the people.
Argument	And, who better than the ones belonging to those very sections?
Precedent	Why not ask ourselves why 35 years after Independence, the position of the Scheduled Castes etc.
Precedent	has not greatly improved?
Precedent	Is it not a legitimate question to ask whether things might have been different, had the district administrators and the <ORG> and Central Bureaucrats been drawn in larger numbers from these classes?
Precedent	Courts are not equipped to answer these questions, but the courts may not interfere with the honest endeavours of the Government to find answers and solutions.
Precedent	We do not mean to say that efficiency in the civil service is unnecessary or that it is a myth.
Precedent	All that we mean to say is that one need not make a fastidious fetish of it."
Precedent	109.
Argument	It is submitted by the learned Counsel for petitioners that reservation necessarily means appointment of less meritorious persons, which in turn leads to lowering of efficiency of administration.
Argument	The submission, therefore, is that rese rvation should be confined to a small minority of appointments/posts, - in any event, to not more than 30%, the figure referred to in the speech of Dr. <NAME> in <ORG>.
Argument	The mandate of Article 335 , it is argued, implies that reservations should be so operated as not to affect the efficiency of administration.
Precedent	Even Article 16 and the directive of Article 46 , it is said, should be read subject to the aforesaid mandate of Article 335.
Precedent	110.
Precedent	The respondents, on the other hand, contend that the marks obtained at the examination/test/interview at the stage of entry into service is not an indicia of the inherent merit of a candidate.
Precedent	They rely upon the opinion of <NAME>,J.
Precedent	in Defunis where the learned Judge illustrates the said aspect by giving example of a candidate coming from disadvantaged sections of society and yet obtaining reasonably good scores - thus manifesting his "promise and potential" - vis-a-vis a candidate from a higher strata obtaining higher scores.
Precedent	(His opinion is referred  to in para 44).
Precedent	On account of the disadvantages suffered by them and the lack of opportunities, - the Respondents say - members of backward classes of citizens may not score equally with the members of socially advanced classes at the inception but in course of time, they would.
Precedent	It would be fallacious to presume that nature has endowed intelligence only to the members of the forward classes.
Precedent	It is to be found everywhere.
Precedent	It only requires an opportunity to prove itself.
Precedent	The directive in Article 46 must be understood and implemented keeping in view these aspects, say the Respondents.
Precedent	111.
RatioOfTheDecision	We do not think it necessary to express ourselves at any length on the correctness or otherwise of the opposing points of view referred to above.
RatioOfTheDecision	(It is, however, necessary to point out that the mandate - if it can be called that - of Article 335 is to take the claims of members of SC/ST into consideration, consistent with the maintenance of efficiency of administration.
RatioOfTheDecision	It would be a misreading of Article to say that the man date is maintenance of efficiency of administration.)
RatioOfTheDecision	May be, efficiency, competence and merit are not synonymous concepts; May be, it is wrong to treat merit as synonymous with efficiency in administration and that merit is but a component of the efficiency of an administrator.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even so, the relevance and significance of merit at the stage of initial recruitment cannot be ignored.
RatioOfTheDecision	It cannot also be ignored that the very idea of reservation implies selection of a less meritorious person.
RatioOfTheDecision	At the same time, we recognise that this much cost has to be paid, if the constitutional promise of social justice is to be redeemed.
RatioOfTheDecision	We also firmly believe that given an opportunity, members of these classes are bound to overcome their initial disadvantages and would compete with - and may, in some cases, excel members of open competitor candidates.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is undeniable that nature has endowed merit upon members of backward classes as much as it has endowed upon members of other classes and that what is required is an opportunity  to prove it.
RatioOfTheDecision	It may not, therefore, be said that reservations are anti meritian.
RatioOfTheDecision	Merit there is even among the reserved candidates and the small difference, that may be allowed at the stage of initial recruitment is bound to disappear in course of time.
RatioOfTheDecision	These members too will compete with and improve their efficiency alongwith others.
RatioOfTheDecision	Having said this, we must append a note of clarification.
Precedent	In some cases arising under Article 15 , this <ORG> has upheld the removal of minimum qualifying marks, in the case of Scheduled Caste/Scheduled Tribe candidates, in the matter of admission to medical courses.
Precedent	For example, in <CITATION_842859> admission to medical course was regulated by an entrance test (called Pre-Medical Test).
Precedent	For general candidates, the minimum qualifying marks were 50% in the aggregate and 33% in each subject.
Precedent	For Scheduled Caste/Scheduled Tribe candidates, however, it was 40% and 30% respectively.
Precedent	On finding that Scheduled Cast/Schedule Tribe candidates equal to the number of the seats reserved f or them did not qualify on the above standard, the <ORG> did away with the said minimum standard altogether.
Precedent	The <ORG>'s action was challenged in this Court but was upheld.
Precedent	Since it was a case under Article 15 , Article 335 had no relevance and was not applied.
Precedent	But in the case of Article 16 , Article 335 would be relevant and any order on the lines of the order of <ORG> (in Nivedita Jain) would not be permissible, being inconsistent with the efficiency of administration.
Precedent	To wit, in the matter of appointment of Medical Officers, the <ORG> or <ORG> cannot say that there shall be no minimum qualifying marks for Scheduled Castes/Scheduled Tribes candidates, while prescribing a minimum for others.
Precedent	It may be permissible for the <ORG> to prescribe a reasonably lower standard for Scheduled Castes/Scheduled Tribes/Backward Classes - consistent with the requirements of efficiency of administration - it would not be permissible not to prescribe any such minimu m standard at all.
Precedent	While prescribing the lower minimum standard for reserved category, the nature of duties attached to the post and the interest of the general public should also be kept in mind.
Precedent	112.
Precedent	While on Article 335 , we are of the opinion that there are certain services and positions where either on account of the nature of duties attached to them or the level (in the hierarchy) at which they obtain, merit as explained hereinabove, alone counts.
Precedent	In such situations.
Precedent	It may not be advisable to provide for reservations.
Precedent	For example, technical posts in research and development organisations/departments/institutions, in specialities and super-specialties in medicine, engineering and other such courses in physical sciences and mathematics, in defence services and in the establishments connected therewith.
Precedent	Similarly, in the case of posts at the higher echelons e.g., Professors (in Education), Pilots in <ORG> and <ORG>, Scientists and Technicians in nuclear and space application, provision for  reservation would not be advisable.
Precedent	As a matter of fact, the impugned Memorandum dated 13th August, 1990 applies the rule of reservation to "civil posts and services under <ORG>" only, which means that defence forces are excluded from the operation of the rule of reservation though it may yet apply to civil posts in defence services.
Precedent	Be that as it may, we are of the opinion that in certain services and in respect of certain posts, application of the rule of reservation may not be advisable for the reason indicated hereinbefore.
Precedent	Some of them are: (1) Defence Services including all technical posts therein but excluding civil posts.
Precedent	(2) All technical posts in establishments engaged in Research and Development including those connected with atomic energy and space and establishments engaged in production of defence equipment; (3) Teaching posts of Professors - and above, if any.
Precedent	(4) Posts in super-specialities in Medicine, engineering and other scientific and technical subjects.
Precedent	(5) Posts of pi lots (and co-pilots) in <ORG> and <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	The list given above is merely illustrative and not exhaustive.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is for <ORG> to consider and specify the service and posts to which the Rule of reservation shall not apply but on that account the implementation of the impugned Office Memorandum dated 13th August, 1990 cannot be stayed or withheld.
RatioOfTheDecision	We may point out that the services/posts enumerated above, on account of their nature and duties attached, are such as call for highest level of intelligence, shill and excellence, some of them are second level and third level posts in the ascending order.
RatioOfTheDecision	Hence, they form a category apart.
RatioOfTheDecision	Reservation therein may not be consistent with "efficiency of administration" contemplated by Article 335.
RatioOfTheDecision	We may add that we see no particular relevance of Article 38(2) in this context.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 16(4) is also a measure to ensure equality of status besides equality of opportunity.
Precedent	PART - VI (QUESTIONS 9, 10 & 11 AND OTHER MISCELLANEOUS QUESTIONS).
Precedent	Qu estion No.
Precedent	9: Will the extent of judicial review be limited or restricted in regard to the identification of Backward Classes and the percentage of reservations made for such classes, to a demonstrably perverse identification or a demonstrably unreasonable percentage?
Precedent	113.
Precedent	It is enough to say on this question that there is no particular or special standard of judicial scrutiny in matters arising under Article 16(4) or for that matter, under Article 15(4).
Precedent	The extent and scope of judicial scrutiny depends upon the nature of the subject matter, the nature of the right affected, the character of the legal and constitutional provisions applicable and so on.
Precedent	The acts and orders of the <ORG> made under Article 16(4) do not enjoy any particular kind of immunity.
Precedent	At the same time, we must say that court would normally extend due deference to the judgment and discretion of the <ORG> - a co-equal wing - in these matters.
Precedent	The political executive, drawn as it is from the people and represent as it does the majority  will of the people, is presumed to know the conditions and the needs of the people and hence its judgment in matters within its judgment and discretion will be entitled to due weight.
Precedent	More than this, it is neither possible nor desirable to say.
Precedent	It is not necessary to answer the question as framed.
Precedent	Question No.
Precedent	10: Whether the distinction made in the second Memorandum between 'poorer sections' of the backward classes and others permissible under Article 16?
Precedent	114.
Precedent	While dealing with Question No.
Precedent	3(d), we held that that exclusion of 'creamy layer' must be no the basis of social advancement (such advancement as renders them misfits in the backward classes) and not on the basis of mere economic criteria.
Precedent	At the same time, we held that income or the extent of property held by a person can be taken as a measure of social advancement and on that basis 'creamy layer' of a given caste/community/occupational group can be excluded to arrive at a true backward class.
Precedent	Under Question No.
Precedent	5, we held that it is not impermis sible for the <ORG> to categories backward classes into backward and more backward on the basis of their relative social backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	We had also given the illustration of two occupational groups, viz., gold-smiths and vaddes (traditional stone-cutters in Andhra Pradesh); both are included within 'other backward classes'.
RatioOfTheDecision	If these two groups are lumped together and a common reservation is made, the gold-smiths would walk away with all the vacancies leaving none for vaddes.
RatioOfTheDecision	From the said point of view, it was observed, such classification among the designated backward classes may indeed serve to help the more backward among them to get their due.
RatioOfTheDecision	But the question now is whether Clause (i) of the Office Memorandum dated 25th September, 1991 is sustainable in law.
RatioOfTheDecision	The said clause provides for a preference in favour of "poorer sections" of the backward classes over other members of the backward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	On first impression, it may appear that backward classes are classified into two sub-groups on the basis of ec onomic criteria alone and a preference provided in favour of the poorer sections of the backward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	In our considered opinion, however, such an interpretation would not be consistent with the context in which the said expression is used and the spirit underlying the clause nor would it further the objective it seeks to achieve.
RatioOfTheDecision	The object of the clause is to provide a preference in favour of more backward among the "socially and educationally backward classes".
RatioOfTheDecision	In other words, the expression 'poorer sections' was meant to refer to those who are socially and economically more backward.
