RatioOfTheDecision	The use of the word 'poorer', in the context, is meant only as a measure of social backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Of course, the <ORG> is yet to notify which classes among the designated backward classes are more socially backward, i.e., 'poorer sections').
RatioOfTheDecision	Understood in this sense, the said classification is not and cannot be termed as invalid either constitutionally speaking or in law.
RatioOfTheDecision	The next question that arises is: what is the  meaning and context of the expression 'preference'?
RatioOfTheDecision	Having regard to the fact the backward classes are sought to be divided into two sub-categories, viz., backward and more backward, the expression 'preference' must be read down to mean an equitable apportionment of the vacancies reserved (for backward classes) among them.
RatioOfTheDecision	The object evidently could not have been to deprive the 'backward' altogether from benefit of reservation, which could be the result if word 'preference' is read literally - if the 'more backward' take away all the available vacancies/posts reserved for O.B.Cs., none would remain for 'backward' among the O.B.Cs.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is for this reason that we are inclined to read down the expression to mean an equitable apportionment.
RatioOfTheDecision	This, in our opinion, is the proper and reasonable way of understanding the expression preference in the context in which it occurs.
RatioOfTheDecision	By giving the above interpretation, we would be effectuating the underlying purpose and the true insertion behind the clause.
RatioOfTheDecision	It shall be open t o the Government to notify which classes among the several designated other backward classes are more backward for the purposes of this clause and the apportionment of reserved vacancies/posts among 'backward' and "more backward".
RatioOfTheDecision	On such notification the clause will become operational.
Fact	Question No.
Fact	11: Whether the reservation of 10% of the posts in favour of 'other economically backward sections of the people who are not covered by any of the existing schemes of the reservations' made by the Office Memorandum dated 25.9.1991 permissible under Article 16?
RatioOfTheDecision	115.
RatioOfTheDecision	This clause provides for a 10% reservation (in appointments/posts) in favour of economically backward sections among the open competition (non-reserved) category.
RatioOfTheDecision	Though the criteria is not yet evolved by <ORG>, it is obvious that the basis is either the income of a person and/or the extent of property held by him.
RatioOfTheDecision	The impugned Memorandum does not say whether this classification is made under Clause (4) or Clause (1) of Article 16.
RatioOfTheDecision	Evidently, this classification among a category outside Clause (4) of Article 16 is not and cannot be related to Clause (4) of Article 16.
RatioOfTheDecision	If at all, it is relatable to Clause (1).
RatioOfTheDecision	Even so, we find it difficult to sustain.
RatioOfTheDecision	Reservation of 10% of the vacancies among open competition candidates on the basis of income/property-holding means exclusion of those above the demarcating line from those 10% seats.
RatioOfTheDecision	The question is whether this is constitutionally permissible?
RatioOfTheDecision	We think not.
RatioOfTheDecision	It may not be permissible to debar a citizen from being considered for appointment to an office under the <ORG> solely on the basis of his income or property-holding.
RatioOfTheDecision	Since the employment under the <ORG> is really conceived to serve the people (that it may also be a source of Livelihood is secondary) no such bar can be created.
RatioOfTheDecision	Any such bar would be inconsistent with the guarantee of equal opportunity held out by Clause (1) of Article 16.
Precedent	On this ground alone, the said clause in the Office Memorandum dated 25.5.1991 fails and is accord ingly declared as such.
Precedent	THE CONCEPT OF POSITIVE ACTION AND POSITIVE DISCRIMINATION  116.
Precedent	Dr. <NAME> describes Article 15(4) as a provision envisaging programmes of positive action and Article 16(4) as a provision warranting programmes of positive discrimination.
Precedent	We are afraid we may not be able to fit these provisions into this kind of compartmentalisation in the context and scheme of our constitutional provisions.
Precedent	By now, it is well settled that reservations in educational institutions and other walks of life can be provided under Article 15(4) just as reservations can be provided in services under Article 16(4).
Precedent	If so, it would not be correct to confine Article 15(4) to programmes of positive action alone.
Precedent	Article 15(4) is wider than Article 16(4) inasmuch as several kinds of positive action programmes can also be evolved and implemented thereunder (in addition to reservations) to improve the conditions of SEBCs., Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes, whereas Article 16(4) speaks only of one type of  remedial measure, namely, reservation of appointments/posts.
Precedent	But it may not be entirely right to say that Article 15(4) is a provision envisaging programmes of positive action.
Precedent	Indeed, even programmes of positive action may sometimes involve a degree of discrimination.
Precedent	For example, if a special residential school is established for Scheduled Tribes or Scheduled Castes at <ORG> expense, it is a discrimination against other students, upon whose education a far lesser amount is being spent by the <ORG>.
Precedent	Or for that matter, take the very American cases - <ORG> or <ORG> Can it be said that they do not involve any discrimination?
Precedent	They do.
Precedent	It is another matter that such discrimination is not unconstitutional for the reason that it is designed to achieve an important governmental objective.
Precedent	DESIRABILITY OF A PERMANENT STATUTORY BODY TO EXAMINE COMPLAINTS OF OVER INCLUSION/UNDER INCLUSION.
Precedent	117.
Precedent	We are of the considered view that there ought to be a permanent body, in the nature of a <ORG> or T ribunal, to which complaints of wrong inclusion or non-inclusion of groups, classes and sections in the lists of Other Backward Classes can be made.
Precedent	Such body must be empowered to examine complaints of the said nature and pass appropriate orders.
Precedent	Its advice/opinion should ordinarily be binding upon the <ORG>.
Precedent	Where, however, the <ORG> does not agree with its recommendation, it must record its reasons therefor.
Precedent	Even it any new class/group is proposed to be included among the other backward classes, such matter must also be referred to the said body in the first instance and action taken on the basis of its recommendation.
Precedent	The body must be composed of experts in the field, both official and non-official, and must be vested with the necessary powers to make a proper and effective inquirey.
Precedent	It is equally desirable that each State constitutes such a body, which step would go a long way in redressing genuine grievances.
Precedent	Such a body can be created under Clause (4) of Article 16 itself - or under Article 16 (4) read with Article 340 - as a concomitant of the power to identify and specify backward class of citizens, in whose favour reservations are to be provided.
Precedent	We direct that such a body be constituted both at Central level and at the level of the States within four months from today.
Precedent	They should become immediately operational and be in a position to entertain and examine forthwith complaints and matters of the nature aforementioned, if any, received.
Precedent	It should be open to <ORG> and the respective State Governments to devise the procedure to be followed by such body.
Precedent	The body or bodies so created can also be consulted in the matter of periodic revision of lists of O.B.Cs.
Precedent	As suggested by <NAME>, CJ.
Precedent	in Vasant Kumar, there should be a periodic revision of these lists to exclude those who have ceased to be backward or for inclusion of new classes, as the case may be.
Precedent	SHOULD THE MATTER GO BACK TO Constitution BENCH TO GO INTO THE DEFECTS OF THE MANDAL COMMISSION REPORT.
Precedent	118.
RatioOfTheDecision	Now that we ha ve answered all the questions raised for our consideration, question new arises, whether in view of the answers given and directions being given by us, is it necessary to send back the matter to <ORG> to consider whether the investigation and survey done, and conclusions arrived at, by <ORG> are contrary to law and if so, whether the impugned Office Memorandums, based as they are on the report of the said <ORG>, can be sustained?
RatioOfTheDecision	We think not.
RatioOfTheDecision	This is not a case where <ORG> framed certain questions and referred them to this <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	All the matters as such were placed before this <ORG> for disposal.
RatioOfTheDecision	During the course of hearing, however, when some counsel wanted to take us into details of castes/groups/classes which, according to them, have been wrongly included or excluded, as the case may be, we refused to go into those details saying that those details can be gone into before <ORG> later.
RatioOfTheDecision	Otherwise, we heard the counsel fully on the alleged il legalities in the approach and methodology adopted by the <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	The written arguments bear them out.
RatioOfTheDecision	We shall notice the criticism first and then answer the question posed at the inception of this para.
RatioOfTheDecision	118A.
RatioOfTheDecision	The first and foremost criticism levelled against the approach and the procedure adopted by Mandal <ORG> in that the Mandal <ORG> has adopted caste and caste alone as the basis of its approach throughout.
RatioOfTheDecision	On this count alone, it is argued, the entire report of the <ORG> is vitiated.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is pointed out that in its very first letter dated 25th April, 1979 (Appendix VII at page 91-Vol.
RatioOfTheDecision	2) addressed to all the Ministries and Departments of <ORG>, the <ORG> has prescribed the following test for determining the socially and educationally backward classes:  (a) In respect of employees belonging to the Hindu communities  (i) an employee will be deemed to be socially backward if he does not belong to any of the three twice-born (Dvij) 'Varnas' i.e., he is neither a Brahm in, nor a Kshatriya/nor a Vaishya; and  (ii) he will be deemed to be educationally backward if neither his <NAME> nor his grant <NAME> has studied beyond the primary level.
RatioOfTheDecision	(b) Regarding the non-Hindu Communities  (i) an employee will be deemed to be socially backward if either (1) he is a convert from those Hindu communities which have been defined as socially backward as per para 4(a)(i) above, or (2) in case he is not such a convert, his parental income is below the prevalent poverty line, i.e., Rs.
RatioOfTheDecision	71 per head per month.
RulingByPresentCourt	(ii) he will be deemed to be educationally backward if neither his <NAME> nor his grand <NAME> had studied beyond the primary level.
RulingByPresentCourt	Serious objection is taken to the above criteria.
RatioOfTheDecision	Treating all the Hindus not belonging to three upper castes as socially and educationally backward classes, it is submitted, is faulty to the core.
RatioOfTheDecision	In the case of non-Hindus, the prescription of income limit is said to be arbitrary.
RatioOfTheDecision	The criteria for identifying backward classes must be uniform for the enti re population; it cannot vary from religion to religion.
RatioOfTheDecision	This shows, says the counsel, the impropriety and impermissibility of adopting the caste as the basis of identification, since castes exist only in the Hindu religion and not in others.
RatioOfTheDecision	On the basis of the statements made in Chapters IV and V, it is submitted that the <ORG> was obsessed by caste and was blind to all other determinants.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is also pointed out that the Survey done by the <ORG> is cursory, totally inadequate and faulty.
RatioOfTheDecision	According to the petitioners, the survey must be an exhaustive one like the one done by Venkataswamy <ORG> in Karnataka, which also forms the basis of Justice <NAME> <ORG> Report.
RatioOfTheDecision	Carrying out the Survey to cover merely two villages and one urban block in each District is not likely to disclose a true picture since it does not represent survey of even one percent of the population.
RatioOfTheDecision	Objection is also taken to use of personal knowledge and also to reliance upon lists of backward classes prepared b y State Governments.
RulingByLowerCourt	It is repeatedly urged that the survey done by the <ORG> cannot be called a scientific one, which has led to discovery of as many as 3,743 castes and their identification as socially and educationally backward classes.
RulingByLowerCourt	This is a steep increase over Kaka Kalelkar <ORG>, according to which, the number of S.E.B.Cs.
RulingByLowerCourt	was only 2,733.
RulingByLowerCourt	It is pointed out further that certain castes which obtained less than 11 points on being tested against the criteria evolved by the <ORG> are included among the backward classes.
RulingByLowerCourt	Conversely, certain castes which obtained 11 or more points are yet excluded from the list of backward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is urged that the caste based approach adopted by the <ORG> has practically divided the nation into a forward section and a backward section.
RatioOfTheDecision	If Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes are also added to the Other Backward Classes, more than 81 per cent of the population gets designated as backward.
RatioOfTheDecision	But for the decision in Balaji, it is submitted, the <ORG> ion would certainly have recommended reservation of 52 per cent of the appointments/posts in favour of the backward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	The <ORG> was actuated by malice towards upper castes and has submitted an unbalanced, unjust and unconstitutional report, it is argued.
RatioOfTheDecision	Respondent's counsel, on the other hand, have refuted each and every contention of the petitioners.
RatioOfTheDecision	According to them, the criteria evolved, the methodology adopted, identification made and lists prepared are all perfectly valid and legal.
RatioOfTheDecision	<ORG>, while justifying the Report, has taken the stand that even if there are any errors or inadequacies in the work and report of the <ORG>, it is no ground for throwing out the report altogether, more particularly when the <ORG> of India has taken care by 'marrying' the <ORG> lists with the <ORG> lists.
RatioOfTheDecision	If any errors are brought to the notice of the <ORG>, <NAME> says, the <ORG> will certainly look into them and rectify them, if satisfied about the error.
RatioOfTheDecision	119.

RatioOfTheDecision	In addition to the above, the following factors must also be kept in mind:  (a) The Mandal Commission <ORG> has not been accepted by <ORG> in its fullness, nor has the Government accepted the list of Other Backward Classes Prepared by it in its entirety.
RatioOfTheDecision	What is now in issue is not the validity of the <ORG> but the validity of the impugned Office Memorandums issued on the basis of the <ORG>.

RatioOfTheDecision	Even if in one or two cases (e.g., Goa), the list is prepared without appointing a <ORG>, it cannot be said to be bad on that account.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Government, which drew up the list, must be presumed to be aware of the conditions obtaining in their <ORG>/area.
RatioOfTheDecision	Unless so held by any competent court - or the permanent mechanism (in the nature of a <ORG>) directed to be created herewith holds otherwise - the lists must be deemed to be valid and enforceable.
RatioOfTheDecision	At the same time, we think it necessary to make the following clarification: It is true that the Government of India has adopted the <ORG> lists obtaining as on 13th August, 1990 for its own purposes but that does not mean that those lists are meant to be sacrosanct and unalterable.
RulingByPresentCourt	There may be cases where commissions appointees by the <ORG> Government may have, in their reports, recommended modification of such lists by deletion or addition of certain castes, communities and classes.
RulingByPresentCourt	Wherever such commission reports  are available, <ORG> is bound to look into them and take action on that basis with reasonable promptitude.
RulingByPresentCourt	If <ORG> effects any modification or alteration by way of deletions or additions, the same shall be intimated to <ORG> forthwith which shall take appropriate action on that basis and make necessary changes in its own list relating to that <ORG>.
RulingByPresentCourt	Further, it shall be equally open to, indeed the duty of, <ORG> - since it has adopted the existing <ORG> lists - to look into the reports of such commission, if any, and pass its own orders, independent of any action by <ORG>, thereon with reasonable promptitude by way of modification or alteration.
RulingByPresentCourt	It shall be open to <ORG> to make such modification/alteration in the lists adopted by way of additions or deletions, as it thinks appropriate on the basis of the Reports of the Commission(s).
RulingByLowerCourt	This direction, in our opinion, safe guards against perpetuation of any erro rs in the <ORG> lists and ensures rectification of those lists with reasonable promptitude on the basis of the reports of the <ORG> already submitted, if any.
RulingByLowerCourt	This course may be adopted de hors the reference to or advice of the permanent mechanism (by way of <ORG>) which we have directed to be created at both central and state level and with respect to which we have made appropriate directions elsewhere.
RulingByLowerCourt	(b) Strictly speaking, appointment of a <ORG> under Article 340 is not necessary to identify the other backward classes.
RulingByLowerCourt	Article 340 does not say so.
RulingByLowerCourt	According to it, the <ORG> is to be constituted "to investigate the conditions of socially and educationally backward classes...and the difficulties under which they labour and to make recommendations as to the steps that should be taken of the <ORG> or any <ORG> to remove such difficulties...." The Government could have, even without appointing a <ORG>, specified the O.B.Cs., on the basis of such material as it may have had before it ( e.g., the lists prepared by various <ORG> Governments) and than appointed the <ORG> to investigate their conditions and to make appropriate recommendations.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is true that <ORG> <ORG> was constituted "to determine the criteria for defining the socially and educationaly backward classes" and the <ORG> did determine the same.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even so, it is necessary to keep the above constitutional position in mind, - more particularly in view of the veto given to <ORG> lists over the <ORG> lists as explained in the preceding sub-para.
RatioOfTheDecision	The criteria evolved by <ORG> <ORG> for defining/identifying the Other Backward Classes cannot be said to be irrelevant.
RatioOfTheDecision	May be there are certain errors in actual exercise of identification, in the nature of over-inclusion or under- inclusion, as the case may be.
RatioOfTheDecision	But in an exercise of such magnitude and complexity, such errors are not uncommon.
RatioOfTheDecision	These errors cannot be made a basis for rejecting either the relevance of the criteria evolved by the <ORG> or the entire ex ercise of identification, It is one thing to say that these errors must be rectified by <ORG> by evolving an appropriate mechanism and an altogether different thing to say that on that account, the entire exercise becomes futile.
RatioOfTheDecision	There can never be a perfect report.
RatioOfTheDecision	In human affairs, such as this, perfection is only an ideal - not an attainable goal.
RatioOfTheDecision	More than forty years have passed by.
RatioOfTheDecision	So far, no reservations could be made in favour of O.B.Cs.
RatioOfTheDecision	for one or the other reason in Central services though in many States, such reservations are in force.
RatioOfTheDecision	Reservations in favour of O.B.Cs.
RatioOfTheDecision	are in force in the States of Kerala, Tamil Nadu, Karnataka, Andhra Pradesh, Maharashtra, Orissa, Bihar, Gujarat, Goa, Uttar Pradesh, Punjab, Haryana and Himachal Pradesh among others.
RatioOfTheDecision	In Madhya Pradesh, a list of O.B.Cs.
RatioOfTheDecision	was prepared on the basis of <ORG> but it appears to have been stayed by <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	(c) The direction made herein for Constitution of a permanent Commission to examine com plaints of over-inclusion or under-inclusion obviates the need of any such scrutiny by this Court.
RatioOfTheDecision	We have directed Constitution of such <ORG> both at Central and <ORG> level.
RatioOfTheDecision	Persons aggrieved can always approach them for appropriate redress.
RatioOfTheDecision	Such <ORG>, which will have the power to receive evidence and enquire into disputed questions of fact, can more appropriately decide such complaints than this Court under Article 32.
RatioOfTheDecision	120.
RatioOfTheDecision	In this view of the matter, it is unnecessary for us to express any opinion on the correctness or adequacy of the exercise done by the <ORG> <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	(If and when <ORG> notifies any caste/community/group/class from out of the <ORG> list, which caste etc., is not included in the appropriate <ORG> list, would the said question fall for consideration.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is then that it would be necessary to deal with the criticism against the <ORG> <ORG>).
RatioOfTheDecision	For the same reason, it is unnecessary to refer or deal with the arguments of the counsel for <ORG>  and the Respondents in justification of the <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Before parting with this aspect, we must say that identifying the impugned Office Memorandums with the <ORG> report is basically erroneous.
RatioOfTheDecision	Such an identification is bound to lead one into confusion.
RatioOfTheDecision	He would be missing the wood for the trees.
RatioOfTheDecision	Instead of concentrating on the real issues, he would deviate into irrelevance and imbalance.
RatioOfTheDecision	<ORG> report may have led to the passing of the impugned Office Memorandum dated 13th August, 1990; it may have acted as the catalytic agent in bringing into existence the reservation in favour of O.B.Cs.
RatioOfTheDecision	(loosely referred to as SEBCs.
RatioOfTheDecision	in the O.M.)
RatioOfTheDecision	but the Office Memorandum dated 13th August, 1990 doesn't incorporate the <ORG> lists of O.B.Cs.
RatioOfTheDecision	as such.
RatioOfTheDecision	It incorporates, in truth and effect, the <ORG> lists as explained hereinabove.
RatioOfTheDecision	In a social measure like the impugned one, the court must give due regard to the judgment of the <ORG>, a co-equal wing of the <ORG> and approach the m easure in the spirit in which it is conceived.
RatioOfTheDecision	This very idea is put forcefully by <NAME> (Fellow of <ORG>, Oxford) in his article "The Rule of Law and its virtue" (1977) 93 Law Quarterly Review 195 at 211 in the following words:  ... one should be wary of disqualifying the legal pursuit of major social goals in the name of the rule of law.
RatioOfTheDecision	After all the rule of law is meant to enable the law to promote social good, and should not be lightly used to show that it should not do so.
RatioOfTheDecision	Sacrificing too many social goals on the altar of the rule of law may make the law barren and empty.
RatioOfTheDecision	A note of clarification may be appended at this stage.
RatioOfTheDecision	We are told that in the State of Madhya Pradesh a list of Other Backward Classes has been prepared but it has been stayed by <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	The said stay, in our opinion, does not affect the operation of the Office Memorandum dated 13th August, 1992 even with respect to the other backward classes in Madhya Pradesh.
RatioOfTheDecision	What the said Office Memorandum does is to import  and adopt the said list for its own purposes i.e., for the purpose of making reservations in central services in favour of other backward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	In such a situation, the stay of the operation of the said list by the <ORG> of Madhya Pradesh does have no relevance to the importation and adoption of the said list into Office Memorandum dated 13th August, 1990.
RatioOfTheDecision	PART - VII  121.
RatioOfTheDecision	We may summarise our answers to the various questions dealt with and answered hereinabove:  (1)(a) It is not necessary that the 'provision' under Article 16(4) should necessarily be made by the <ORG>/Legislature.
RatioOfTheDecision	Such a provision can be made by the Executive also.
RatioOfTheDecision	Local bodies, Statutory Corporations and other instrumentalities of the <ORG> falling under Article 12 of the Constitution are themselves competent to make such a provision, if so advised.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 55)  (b) An executive order making a provision under Article 16(4) is enforceable the moment it is made and issued.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 56) (2)(a) Clause (4) of Article 16 is not an exception t o Clause (1).
RatioOfTheDecision	It is an instance and an illustration of the classification inherent in Clause (1).
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 57)  (b) Article 16(4) is exhaustive of the subject of reservation in favour of backward class of citizens, as explained in this judgment.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 58)  (c) Reservations can also be provided under Clause (1) of Article 16.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is not confined to extending of preferences, concessions or exemptions alone.
RatioOfTheDecision	These reservations, if any, made under Clause (1) have to be so adjusted and implemented as not to exceed the level of representation prescribed for 'backward class of citizens' - as explained in this Judgment.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 60) (3)(a) A caste can be and quite often is a social class in India.
RatioOfTheDecision	If it is backward socially, it would be a backward class for the purposes of Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	Among non-Hindus, there are several occupational groups, sects and denominations, which for historical reasons, are socially backward.
RatioOfTheDecision	They too represent backward social collectives for the purposes of Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	(Paras 61 to 82)  (b) N either the Constitution nor the law prescribes the procedure or method of identification of backward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	Nor is it possible or advisable for the court to lay down any such procedure or method.
RatioOfTheDecision	It must be left to the authority appointed to identify.
RatioOfTheDecision	It can adopt such method/procedure as it thinks convenient and so long as its survey covers the entire populace, no objection can be taken to it.
RatioOfTheDecision	Identification of the backward classes can certainly be done with reference to castes among, and along with, other occupational groups, classes and sections of people.
RatioOfTheDecision	One can start the process either with the occupational groups or with castes or with some other groups.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus one can start the process with the castes, wherever they are found, apply the criteria (evolved for determining backwardness) and find out whether it satisfies the criteria.
RatioOfTheDecision	If it does - what emerges is a "backward class of citizens" within the meaning of and for the purposes of Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	Similar process can be adopted in the case of other  occupational groups, communities and classes, so as to cover the entire populace.
RatioOfTheDecision	The central idea and overall objective should be to consider all available groups, sections and classes in society.
RatioOfTheDecision	Since caste represents an existing, identifiable social group/class encompassing an overwhelming majority of the country's population, one can well begin with it and then go to other groups, sections and classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Paras 83 and 84)  (c) It is not necessary for a class to be designated as a backward class that it is situated similarly to the Scheduled Castes/Scheduled Tribes.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Paras 87 and 88)  (d) 'Creamy layer' can be, and must be excluded.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 86)  (e) It is not correct to say that the backward class of citizens contemplated in Article 16(4) is the same as the socially and educationally backward classes referred to in Article 15(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	It is much wider.
RatioOfTheDecision	The accent in Article 16(4) is on social backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	Of course, social, educational and economic backwardness are closely inter-twined in the Indian context.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Par a 85)  (f) The adequacy of representation of a particular class in the services under the <ORG> is a matter within the subjective satisfaction of the appropriate <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	The judicial scrutiny in that behalf is the same as in other matters within the subjective satisfaction of an authority.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 89) (4)(a) A backward class of citizens cannot be identified only and exclusively with reference to economic criteria.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 90)  (b) It is, of course, permissible for the <ORG> or other authority to identify a backward class of citizens on the basis of occupation-cum-income, without reference to caste, if it is so advised.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 91).
RatioOfTheDecision	(5) There is no constitutional bar to classify the backward classes of citizens into backward and more backward categories.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 92) (6)(a)&(b) The reservations contemplated in Clause (4) of Article 16 should not exceed 50%.
RatioOfTheDecision	While 50% shall be the rule, it is necessary not to put out of consideration certain extraordinary situations inherent in the great diversity of this coun try and the people.
RatioOfTheDecision	It might happen that in far-flung and remote areas the population inhabiting those areas might, on account of their being out of the main-stream of national life and in view of the conditions peculiar to and characteristic of them need to be treated in a different way, some relaxation in this strict rule may become imperative.
RatioOfTheDecision	In doing so, extreme caution is to be exercised and a special case made out.
RatioOfTheDecision	(c) The rule of 50% should be applied to each year.
RatioOfTheDecision	It cannot be related to the total strength of the class, category, service or cadre, as the case may be.
RulingByPresentCourt	(Para 96)  (d) Devadasan was wrongly decided and is accordingly over-ruled to the extent it is inconsistent with this judgment.
RulingByPresentCourt	(Paras 97 to 99) (7) Article 16(4) does not permit provision for reservations in the matter of promotion.
RulingByPresentCourt	This rule shall, however, have only prospective operation and shall not affect the promotions already made, whether made on regular basis or on any other basis.
RulingByPresentCourt	We direct that our decision on this question  shall operate only prospectively and shall not affect promotions already made, whether on temporary, officiating or regular/permanent basis.
RulingByPresentCourt	If is further directed that wherever reservations are already provided in the matter of promotion - be it <ORG> or <ORG>, or for that matter services under any Corporation, authority or body falling under the definition of 'State' in Article 12 - such reservations may continue in operation for a period of five years from this day.
RulingByPresentCourt	Within this period, it would be open to the appropriate authorities to revise, modify or re-issue the relevant rules to ensure the achievement of the objective of Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	If any authority thinks that for ensuring adequate representation of backward class of citizens in any service, class or category, it is necessary to provide for direct recruitment therein, it shall be open to it do so.
RatioOfTheDecision	(<NAME>, J. expresses no opinion on this question upholding the preliminary objection of <ORG>).
RatioOfTheDecision	It would not be impermissi ble for the <ORG> to extent concessions and relaxations to members of reserved categories in the matter of promotion without compromising the efficiency of the administration.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Paras 100 to 107).
RatioOfTheDecision	(8) While the rule of reservation cannot be called anti-meritarion, there are certain services and posts to which it may not be advisable to apply the rule of reservation.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Paras 108 to 112) (9) The distinction made in the impugned Office Memorandum dated 25th September, 1991 between 'poorer sections' and others among the backward classes is not invalid, if the classification is understood and operated as based upon relative backwardness among the several classes identified as other Backward classes, as explained in para 114 of this Judgment (Para 114).
RatioOfTheDecision	(11) The reservation of 10% of the posts in favour of 'other economically backward sections of the people who are not covered by any of the existing schemes of the reservation' made in the impugned office memorandum dated 25.9.1991 is constitutionally invalid and is  accordingly struck down.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 115) (12) There is no particular or special standard of judicial scrutiny applicable to matters arising under Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 113) (13) The <ORG> of India and the State <ORG>s have the power to, and ought to, create a permanent mechanism - in the nature of a <ORG> - for examining requests of inclusion and complaints of over-inclusion or non-inclusion in the list of O.B.Cs.
RatioOfTheDecision	and to advise the <ORG>, which advice shall ordinarily be binding upon the <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Where, however, the <ORG> does not accept the advice, it must record its reasons therefor.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Para 117) (14) In view of the answers given by us herein and the directions issued herewith, it is not necessary to express any opinion on the correctness and adequacy of the exercise done by the Mandal <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is equally unnecessary to send the matters back to <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	(Paras 118 to 119) 122.
RatioOfTheDecision	For the sake of ready reference, we also record our answers to questions as  framed by the counsel for the parties and set out in para 26.
RatioOfTheDecision	Our answers question-wise are:  (1) Article 16(4) is not an exception to Article 16(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	It is an instance of classification inherent in Article 16(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 16(4) is exhaustive of the subject of reservation in favour of backward classes, though it may not be exhaustive of the very concept of reservation.
RatioOfTheDecision	Reservations for other classes can be provided under Clause (1) of Article 16.
RatioOfTheDecision	(2) The expression 'backward class' in Article 16(4) takes in 'Other Backward Classes', S.Cs., S.Ts.
RatioOfTheDecision	and may be some other backward classes as well.
RatioOfTheDecision	The accent in Article 16(4) is upon social backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	Social backwardness leads to educational backwardness and economic backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	They are mutually contributory to each other and are inter-twined with low occupations in the Indian society.
RatioOfTheDecision	A caste can be and quite often is a social class in India.
RatioOfTheDecision	Economic criterion cannot be the sole basis for determining the backward class of citizens contemplated by Article 1 6(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	The weaker sections referred to Article 46 do include S.E.B.Cs.
RatioOfTheDecision	referred to in Article 340 and covered by Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	(3) Even under Article 16(1 ), reservations cannot bo made on the basis of economic criteria alone.
RatioOfTheDecision	(4) The reservations contemplated in Clause (4) of Article 16 should not exceed 50%.
RatioOfTheDecision	While 50% shall be the rule, it is necessary not to put out of consideration certain extraordinary situations inherent in the great diversity of this country and the people.
RatioOfTheDecision	It might happen that in far-flung and remote areas the population inhabiting those areas might, on account of their being out of the main-stream of national life and in view of the conditions peculiar to and characteristic of them need to be treated in a different way, some relaxation in this strict rule may become imperative.
RatioOfTheDecision	In doing so, extreme caution is to be exercised and a special case made out.
RatioOfTheDecision	For applying this rule, the reservations should not exceed 50% of the appointments in a grade, cadre or service in any given yea r. Reservation can be made in a service or category only when the <ORG> is satisfied that representation of backward class of citizens therein is not adequate.
RatioOfTheDecision	To the extent, Devadasan is inconsistent herewith, it is over-ruled.
RatioOfTheDecision	(5) There is no constitutional bar to classification of backward classes into more backward and backward classes for the purposes of Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	The distinction should be on the basis of degrees of social backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	In case of such classification, however, it would be advisable - nay, necessary - to ensure equitable distribution amongst the various backward classes to avoid lumping so that one or two such classes do not eat away the entire quota leaving the other backward classes high and dry.
RatioOfTheDecision	For excluding 'creamy layer', an economic criterion can be adopted as an indicium or measure of social advancement.
RatioOfTheDecision	(6) A 'provision' under Article 16(4) can be made by an executive order.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is not necessary that it should be made by <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	(7) No special standard of  judicial scrutiny can be predicated in matters arising under Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	It is not possible or necessary to say more than this under this question.
RatioOfTheDecision	(8) Reservation of appointments or posts under Article 16(4) is confined to initial appointment only and cannot extend to providing reservation in the matter of promotion.
RulingByPresentCourt	We direct that our decision on this question shall operate only prospectively and shall not affect promotions already made, whether on temporary, officiating or regular/permanent basis.
Statute	It is further directed that wherever reservations are already provided in the matter of promotion - be it <ORG> or <ORG>, or for that matter services under any Corporation, authority or body falling under the definition of 'State' in Article 12 - such reservations may continue in operation for a period of five years from this day.
Statute	Within this period, it would be open to the appropriate authorities to revise, modify or re-issue the relevant rules to ensure the achievement of the objective  of Article 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	If any authority thinks that for ensuring adequate representation of 'backward class of citizens' in any service, class or category, it is necessary to provide for direct recruitment therein, it shall be open to it do so.
RatioOfTheDecision	(As pointed out at the end of the paragraph 101 of this judgment, <NAME>, J. having upheld the preliminary objection raised by <NAME> and others has not associated himself with the discussion on the question whether reservation in promotion is permissible.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, the views expressed in this judgment on the said point are not the views of <NAME>.
Precedent	J.)
Precedent	THE FOLLOWING DIRECTIONS ARE GIVEN TO THE GOVERNMENT OF INDIA.
Precedent	THE STATE GOVTS.
Precedent	AND THE ADMINISTRATION OF UNION TERRITORIES.
Precedent	123.
Precedent	(A).
Precedent	The Government of India, each of the State Governments and <ORG> shall, within four months from today, constitute a permanent body for entertaining, examining and recommending upon requests for inclusion and complaints of over-inclusion and under-in clusion in the lists of other backward classes of citizens.
Precedent	The advice tendered by such body shall ordinarily be binding upon the Government.
Precedent	(B) Within four months from today <ORG> shall specify the bases, applying the relevant and requisite socio-economic criteria to exclude socially advanced persons/sections ('creamy layer') from 'Other Backward Classes'.
Precedent	The implementation of the impugned O.M.
RulingByPresentCourt	dated 13th September, 1990 shall be subject to exclusion of such socially advanced persons ('creamy layer').
RulingByPresentCourt	This direction shall not however apply to States where the reservations in favour of backward classes are already in operation.
RulingByPresentCourt	They can continue to operate them.
RulingByPresentCourt	Such States shall however evolve the said criteria within six months from today and apply the same to exclude the socially advanced persons/sections from the designated 'Other Backward Classes.
RulingByPresentCourt	(C) It is clarified and directed that any and all objections to the criteria that may be evolved by <ORG> and the Stat e Governments in pursuance of the direction contained in Clause (B) of Para 123 as well as to the classification among backward classes and equitable distribution of the benefits of reservations among them that may be made in terms of and as contemplated by Clause (1) of the Office Memorandum dated 25th September 1991, as explained herein, shall be preferred only before this <ORG> and not before or in any other High <ORG> or other <ORG> or <ORG>.
RulingByPresentCourt	Similarly, and petition or proceeding questioning the validity, operation or implementation of the two impugned Office Memorandums, on any grounds whatsoever, shall be be filed or instituted only before this <ORG> and not before any High <ORG> or other <ORG> or <ORG>.
Precedent	124.
Precedent	The Office Memoranda dated August 13, 1990 impugned in these writ petitions is accordingly held valid and enforceable subject to the exclusion of the socially advanced members/sections from the notified 'Other Backward Classes', as explained in para 123(B).
Precedent	Clause (i) of the Office Memorand um dated September 25, 1991 requires - to uphold its validity - to be read, interpreted and understood as intending a distinction between backward and more backward classes on the basis of degrees of social backwardness and a rational and equitable distribution of the benefits of the reservations amongst them.
Precedent	To be valid, the said clause will have to be read, understood and implemented accordingly.
Precedent	Clause (ii) of the Office Memorandum dated September 25, 1991 is held invalid and inoperative.
RulingByPresentCourt	The writ Petitions and Transferred Cases are disposed of in the light of the principles, directions, clarifications and orders contained in this Judgment.
RulingByPresentCourt	No costs.
Precedent	<NAME>, J.
Precedent	125.
Precedent	Equality of status and of opportunity...' the rubric chiselled in the luminous preamble of our vibrating and pulsating Constitution radiates one of the avowed objectives in our Sovereign, Socialist and Secular Democratic Republic.
Precedent	In every free country which has adopted a system of governance through democratic principles, th e people have their fundamental inalienable rights and enjoy the recognition of inherent dignity and of equality analogous to the rights proclaimed in the 'Bill of Rights' in U.S.A., the 'Rights of Man' in the French Constitution of 1971 and 'Declaration of Human Rights' etc.
Precedent	Our Constitution is unquestionably unique in its character and assimilation having its notable aspirations contained in 'Fundamental Rights' (in Part HI) through which the illumination of Constitutional rights comes to us not through an artless window glass but refracted with the enhanced intensity and beauty by prismatic interpretation of the Constitutional provisions dealing with equal distribution of justice in the social, political and economic spheres.
Precedent	126.
Precedent	Though forty-five years from the commencement of the Indian independence after the end of British paramountcy and forty-two years from the advent of our Constitution have marched on, the tormenting enigma that often nags the people of India is whether the principle of 'equality  of status and of opportunity' to be equally provided to all the citizens of our country from cradle to grave is satisfactorily consummated and whether the clarion of 'equality of opportunity in matters of public employment' enshrined in Article 16(4) of the Constitution of India has been called into action?
Precedent	With a broken heart one has to answer these questions in the negative.
Precedent	127.
Precedent	The founding fathers of our Constitution have designedly couched Articles 14, 15 and 16 in comprehensive phraseology so that the frail and emaciated section of the people living in proverty, rearing in obscurity, possessing no wealth or influence, having no education, much less higher education and suffering from social repression and oppression should not be denied of equality before the law and equal protection of the laws and equal opportunity in the matters of public employment or subjected to any prohibition of discrimination on grounds of religion, race, caste, sex or place of birth.
Precedent	128.
Precedent	To achieve the above objectives, th e Government have enacted innumerable social welfare legislations and geared up social reformative measures for uplifting the social and economic development of the disadvantaged section of people.
Precedent	True, a rapid societal transformation and profusion of other progressive changes are taking place, yet a major section of the people living below the poverty line and suffering from social ostracism still stand far behind and lack in every respect to keep pace with the advanced section of the people.
Precedent	The undignified social status and sub-human living conditions leave an indelible impression that their forlorn hopes for equality in every sphere of life are only a myth rather than a reality.
Precedent	It is verily believed - rightly too - that the one and only peerless way and indeed a most important and promising way to achieve the equal status and equal opportunity is only by means of constitutional justice so that all the citizens of this country irrespective of their religion, race, caste, sex, place of birth or any of the m may achieve the goal of an egalitarian society.
Precedent	129.
Precedent	This <ORG> has laid down a series of landmark judgments in relation to social justice by interpreting the constitutional provisions upholding the cherished values of the Constitution and thereby often has shaped the course of our national life.
Precedent	Notwithstanding a catena of expository decisions with interpretive semantics, the naked truth is that no streak of light or no ray of hope of attaining the equality of status and equality of opportunity is visible.
Precedent	130.
Precedent	Confining to the issue involved in this case as regards the equal opportunity in the matters of public employment, I venture to articulate without any reservation, even on the possibility of any refutation that it is highly deplorable and heart-rending to note that the constitutional provision, namely, namely, Clause (4) of Article 16 proclaiming a "Fundamental Right" enacted about 42 years ago for providing equality of opportunity in matters of public employment to people belonging to any backwar d class has still not been given effect to in services under <ORG> and many more States.
Precedent	A number of <ORG> have been appointed in some of the States, the recommendations of which have been repeatedly subjected to judicial scrutiny.
Precedent	Though the President of India appointed the second <ORG> under the chairmanship of <NAME> as far back as 1at January, 1979 and the Report was submitted in December, 1980, no effective steps were taken for its implementation till the issuance of the two impugned OMs.
Precedent	Having regard to this appalling situation and the pathetic condition of the backward classes, for the first time <ORG> has issued the Office Memorandum (hereinafter called the 'O.M.')
Precedent	in August 1991 and thereafter an amended O.M.
Precedent	in September 1991 on the basis of the recommendations of <ORG>.
Precedent	131.
Precedent	Immediately after the announcement of the acceptance of the Report of <ORG>, as pointed out in Writ Petition No.
Precedent	930/90 and the Annexures I & II enclosed thereto, there were unabated pro as well as anti reservation agitations and violent societal disturbances virtually paralysing the normal life.
Precedent	It was unfortunate and painful to note that some youths who are intransigent to recognise the doctrine of equality in matters of public employment and who under the mistaken impression that 'wrinkles and gray hairs' could not do any thing in this matter, actively participated in the agitation.
Precedent	Similarly, another section of people suffering from a fear psychosis that the <ORG> recommendations may not at all be implemented entered the fray of the agitation.
