Precedent	The Nav.
Precedent	Budhists, and Neo Budhists the majority of whom are converts from Scheduled Castes enjoy the reservation on the ground that their low status in that community have not become advanced equal to the status of others and their social backwardness is not changed in spite of change of their religion.
Precedent	227.
Precedent	Sikhism, no doubt, strictly believes in social equality and justice, denounces all sorts of social discrimination between man and man, strongly advocates the equality and  parity in all humanity and propagates that caste, birth or colour cannot make one superior or inferior.
Precedent	All the Gurus of <ORG> have advocated and articulated the concept of equality of man as the basis of egalitarian society.
Precedent	Notwithstanding <ORG> is violently against casteism, some converts to <ORG> from <ORG> still retain their caste label.
Precedent	228.
Precedent	Thus even among non-Hindus, there are occupational organisations or social groups or sects which are having historical backward/evolution.
Precedent	They too constitute social collectives and form separate classes for the purposes of Article 16(4).
Precedent	229.
Precedent	Though in India, caste evil originated from Hindu religion that evil has taken its root so deep in the social structure of all the Indian communities and spread its tentacles far and wide thereby leaving no community from being influenced by the caste factor.
Precedent	In other words, it cannot be authoritatively said the some of the communities belonging to any particular religion are absolutely free from caste ism or at least from its shadow.
Precedent	The only difference being that the rigour of caste varies from religion to religion and from region to region.
Precedent	Of course, in some of the communities, the influence of the caste factor may be minimal.
Precedent	So far as the Hindu society is concerned, it is most distressing to note that it receives sanction from the Hindu religion itself and perpetuated all through.
Precedent	230.
Precedent	Reference may be made to paragraphs 12.11 to 12.16 of Chapter XII of the Report.
Precedent	231.
Precedent	After identifying in paragraph 12.18, the <ORG> has laid down the following tests for identifying non-Hindu OBCs:  12.18 After giving a good deal of thought to these difficulties, the <ORG> has evolved the following rough and ready criteria for identifying non-Hindu OBCs:-  (i) All untouchables converted to any non-Hindu religion; and  (ii) Such occupational communities which are known by the name of their traditional hereditary occupation and whose Hindu counterparts have been included in the list of Hindu OBCs.
Precedent	(Examples:  Dhobi, Teli, Dheemar, Nai, Gujar, Kumhar, Lohar, Darji, Badhai, etc.)
Precedent	232.
Precedent	Even assuming that the caste factor would not furnish a reliable yardstick to identify 'socially and educationally backward groups' in the communities other than Hindu community as there is no commonness since all sections of people among Budhists, Muslims, Sikhs and Christians etc.
Precedent	and as the respective religion of those communities do not recognise the caste system, yet on the principle of the other agreed criteria such as traditional occupation, trade, place of residence, poverty lack of education or economic backwardness etc.
Precedent	the social and economic backwardness of those communities could be identified independently of the caste criterion.
Precedent	Once these 'casteless societies' are tested on the anvil of the established relevant criteria de hors the caste criterion, there may not be any difficulty in identifying the social and educational backwardness of the section of the people of that community and classifying them as 'backward clas s of citizens' within the meaning of Article 16(4).
Precedent	233.
Precedent	In this connection, reference may be made to the observation of this Court in Chitralekha (supra) that "...if in a given situation caste is excluded in ascertaining a class within the meaning of Article 15(4) of the Constitution, it does not vitiate the classification if it satisfied other tests."
RatioOfTheDecision	234.
RatioOfTheDecision	More often than not, a question that is put forth is should the caste label be accepted as a criterion in ascertaining the social and educational backwardness of a group of persons or community.
RatioOfTheDecision	No doubt, it is felt that in identifying and classifying a group of persons or community as 'socially and educationally backward class', it should be done de hors the caste label.
RatioOfTheDecision	But all those who address such a question turn a blind eye to the existing stark reality that in the Hindu society ever since the caste system was introduced, till today, the social status of Hindu is so woven or inextricably intertwined and fused with the caste system to such an exte nt that no one in such a situation can say that the caste is not a primary indicator of social backwardness and that social backwardness is not identifiable with reference to the caste of an individual or group of persons or community.
RatioOfTheDecision	However, painful and distasteful, it may be, we have to face the reality that under the hydraulic pressure of caste system in Hindu society, a major section of the Hindus under multiple caste labels are made to suffer socially, educationally and economically.
RatioOfTheDecision	There appears no symptoms of early demise of this dangerous disease of caste system or getting away from the caste factor in spite of the fact that many reformative measures have been taken by the <ORG>.
Precedent	Unless this caste system, unknown to other parts of the world is completely eradicated and all the socially and educationally backward classes to whichever religion they belong inclusive of Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes are brought up and placed on par with the advanced section of the people, the caste label a mong Hindus will continue to serve as a primary indicator of its social backwardness.
Precedent	235.
Precedent	Though I am not inclined to exhaustively elaborate the untold agony and immeasurable sufferings undergone by the people in the lower strata under the label of their respective caste, I cannot avoid but citing a jarring piece of information appearing in the <ORG>.
Precedent	The noted and renowned Sociologist <NAME> in Rise & Awakening of Depressed Classes in India published by <ORG>, New Delhi has quoted a passage from the issue of 'Hindu' dated 24.12.1932 as an example of visual pollution existing in Tinnevelli (Tamil Nadu) which <ORG> has extracted in Chapter IV vide para 4.13 of its report:  4.13.
Precedent	...
Precedent	In this (Tinnevelly) district there is a class of unseeables called purada vannans.
Precedent	They are not allowed to come out during day time because their sight is considered to be pollution.
Precedent	Some of these people who wash the clothes of other exterior castes working between midnight and day- break, were with difficulty persuaded to leave their houses to interview.
Precedent	236.
Precedent	Does not the very mention of the caste named 'purada vannans' indicate that the people belonging to that community were so backward, both socially, economically as well as educationally beyond comprehension?
Precedent	Would the children of those people who were not allowed to come out during day time have gone to any school?
Precedent	Does not the very fact that those people were treated with contempt and disgrace as if they were vermin in the human form freeze our blood?
Precedent	Alas!
Precedent	What a terrible and traumatic experience it was for them living in their hide-outs having occasional pot-luck under pangs of misery, all through mourning over their perilous predicament on account of this social ostracism.
Precedent	When people placed at the base level in the hierarchical caste system are living like mutes, licking their wounds - caused by the deadening weight of social customs and mourning their fate for having been born in lower castes - can it be said by any stretch  of imagination that caste can never be the primary criterion in identifying the social, economic and educational backwardness?
Precedent	Are not the social and economic activities of Shudras and Panchamas (untouchables) severely influenced by their low caste status?
Precedent	237.
Precedent	There is no denying that many of the castes are identified even by their traditional occupation.
Precedent	This is so because numerous castes arranged in a hierarchical order in the Hindu social structure are tied up with their respective particular traditional occupation consequent upon the creation of four Varnas on the concept of divine origin of caste system based on the Vedic principles.
Precedent	Can it be said that the propagation and practice on the caste - based discrimination; the marked dividing line between upper caste Hindus and Shudras, and the practice of untouchability in spite of the Constitutional declaration of abolition of untouchability under Article 17 are completely eradicated and erased?
Precedent	Can it be said that the social backwardness has no relation  to caste status?
Precedent	The unchallengeable answer for the first question would be in the negative and for the second question, the answer would be that social backwardness does have a relation with the caste status.
Precedent	238.
Precedent	It is not germane for my purpose to enter into a lengthy deliberation as to how religion and mythology were used for founding the social institution in Hindu society containing so much of inequalities and discrimination among the people professing the same Hinduism.
Precedent	239.
Precedent	<ORG> in Chapter IV of its report under the heading "Social Backwardness and Caste" has concluded its view, with a query under paragraph 4.33 of its Report (Volume I) thus:  In view of the foregoing will it be too much to say that in the traditional Indian society social backwardness was a direct consequence of caste status....  240.
Precedent	Though the <ORG> both on the Central and State level have taken and are taking positive steps through law and other reformative measures to eradicate this social evil, it is hear t- rending to note that in many circumstances, the caste system is being perpetuated instead of being banished for the reasons best known to those perpetratOrs.
Precedent	241.
Precedent	It is common knowledge that in Hindu society, if a person merely mentions the name of a traditional occupation, another by his empirical knowledge can immediately identify the caste by the said traditional occupation.
Precedent	To illustrate, the traditional occupation of washing clothes is identified with washerman (Dhobi), caste, traditional occupation of haircutting is identified with <NAME> (Nai) - caste, traditional occupation of pottery is identified with <NAME> (Kumhar's caste), and so on.
Precedent	Of course in modern times, persons belonging to any particular caste might have shifted over to other occupation leaving their traditional occupation but generally speaking, the occupation is identified with the caste and vice-versa.
Precedent	Many backward castes have taken 'agricultrure' as their profession.
Precedent	In such an unquestionable situation, in my opinion, there can b e no justification in saying that caste in Hindu society cannot serve as a primary criterion even at the starting point in ascertaining its social, economic and educational backwardness.
Precedent	To say that in the effort of ascertaining social backwardness, caste should be considered only at the end point, is a misnomer and fallacious.
Precedent	Because after identifying and classifying a group of persons belonging to a particular caste by testing with the application of the relevant criteria other than the caste criterian, the identification of the caste of that class of persons is no more required as in the case of identification of casteless society as a backward class.
Precedent	In fact, this <ORG> in a number of decisions has held that a caste may become a 'backward class' provided that caste satisfies the test of backwardness.
Precedent	242.
Precedent	It is apposite, in this context, to make reference of the views expressed by <ORG> stating that there is "a close linkage between caste ranking of a person and his social educational an d economic status....In India, therefore, the low ritual caste status of a person has a direct bearing on his social backwardness".
Precedent	243.
Precedent	<NAME>, J.
Precedent	In <NAME> points out that the social investigator "... may freely perceive those pursuing certain 'lowly' occupation as socially and educationally backward classes."
Precedent	244.
Precedent	In passing, I would like to make reference to the pith and substance of the report of <NAME>, according to which the relevant factors to cosider in classifying 'backward class' would be their traditional occupation or profession, the percentage of literary or the general educational advancement made by them; the estimated population of the conmmunity, and the distribution of the various communities throughout the State or their concentration in certain areas.
Precedent	245.
Precedent	What the Expression "Backward Class" means?
Precedent	246.
Precedent	In Minor P. Rajendran (supra), <NAME>, C.J.
Precedent	speaking for <ORG> has stated that" a caste is also a 'class of citizens' and that reservation can  be made in such a case provided if that caste as a whole is socially and educationally backward within the meaning of Article 15(4)".
Precedent	247.
Precedent	Reference may also be made to <NAME> (11) (supra) and <NAME>.
Precedent	248.
Precedent	The facts in <NAME> (cited above) disclose that for the admission to the integrated <ORG> in the government medical colleges in Andhra Pradesh, the Government issued a G.O.
Precedent	making a reservation of 25% of seats in favour of 'backward classes' as recommended by <ORG> besides other reservations inclusive of reservation for Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes.
Precedent	The reservation for the 'backward classes' was challenged on the ground that the Government Order violated Article 15(1) read with Article 29 and that the reservation was not saved by Article 15(4).
Precedent	<ORG> held that the <ORG> had merely enumerated the various persons belonging to a particular caste as 'backward classes' which was contrary to the decision of this Court and violati ve of the constitutional provisions and consequently struck down the G.O.
Precedent	The Government preferred an appeal before this Court.
Precedent	<NAME>, J. speaking for the <ORG> has observed:  In the determination of a class to be grouped as backward, a test solely based upon caste or community cannot be valid.
Precedent	But, in our opinion, though Directive Principles contained in Article 46 cannot be enforced by <ORG>, Article 15(4) will have to be given effect to in order to assist the weaker sections of the citizens, as the <ORG> has been charged with such a duty.
Precedent	No doubt, we are aware that any provision made under this clause must be within the well defined limits and should not be on the basis of caste alone.
Precedent	But it should not also be missed that a caste is also a class of citizens and that a caste as such may be socially and educationally backward.
Precedent	If after collecting the necessary data, it is found that the caste as a whole is socially and educationally backward, in our opinion, the reservation made of such persons wil l have to be upheld notwithstanding the fact that a few individuals in that group may be both socially and educationally above the general average.
Precedent	There is no gainsaying the fact that there are numerous castes in the country, which are socially and educationally backward and, therefore, a suitable provision will have to be made by the <ORG> as charged in Article 15(4) to safeguard their interest.
Precedent	(emphasis supplied)  249.
Precedent	The decisions which we have referred to above support the view that a caste is also a class of citizens and that if that caste satisfies the requisite tests of backwardness, then the classification of that caste as a backward class is not opposed to Article 16(4) notwithstanding that a few individuals of that caste are socially and educationally above the general average.
Precedent	I am in full agreement with the above view.
Precedent	250.
Precedent	The composition and terms of reference of <ORG> show that the <ORG> was appointed to investigate the conditions of socially and educa tionally backward classes within the territory of India but not the socially, economically and educationally backward classes.
Precedent	The earlier O.M.
RulingByLowerCourt	issued on 13.8.90 reads that with a view to providing certain weightage to socially and educationally backward classes in the services of the <ORG> and their Public Undertakings, as recommended by the <ORG>, the orders are issued in the terms mentioned therein.
RulingByLowerCourt	The said O.M.
RulingByLowerCourt	also explains that "the <ORG> would comprise in the first phase the castes and communities which are common to both the lists, in the report of the <ORG> and <ORG> list".
RulingByLowerCourt	In addition it is said that list of such castes/communities is being issued seperately.
RulingByLowerCourt	The subsequent amended O.M.
RulingByLowerCourt	dated 25.9.91 states that in order to enable the 'poorer sections' of the <ORG>s to receive the benefits of reservation on a preferential basis and to provide reservation for other economically backward sections of the people not covered by any of the existing schemes of reservation, the Gove <ORG> have decided to amend the earlier Memorandum.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus this amended O.M.
RatioOfTheDecision	firstly speaks of the 'poorer sections' of the <ORG> and secondly about the economically backward sections of the people not covered by any of the existing schemes of reservation.
RatioOfTheDecision	However, both the O.M.s while referring to the <ORG>, do not include the 'economic backwardness' of that class along with 'social and educational backwardness'.
RatioOfTheDecision	By the amended O.M., the Gove<ORG> while providing reservation for the backward sections of the people not covered by the existing schemes of reservation meant for <ORG>, classifies that section of the people as 'economically backward', that is to say that those backward sections of the people are to be identified only by their economic backwardness and not by the test of social and educational backwardness, evidently for the reason that they are all socially and educationally well advanced.
RatioOfTheDecision	251.
RatioOfTheDecision	Coming to Article 16(4) the words 'backward class' are used with a wider connotation and without any qu alification or explanation.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, it must be construed in the wider perspective.
RatioOfTheDecision	Though the OMs speak of social and educational backwardness of a class, the primary consideration in identifying a class and in ascertaining the inadequate representation of that class in the services under the <ORG> under Article 16(4) is the social backwardness which results in educational backwardness, both of which culminate in economic backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	The degree of importance to be attached to social backwardness is much more than the importance to be given to the educational backwardness and the economic backwardness, because in identifying and classifying a section of people as a backward class within the meaning of Article 16(4) for the reservation of appointments or posts, the 'social backwardness' plays a predominant role.
RatioOfTheDecision	252.
RatioOfTheDecision	<NAME>, <NAME> in Jayashree is of the view that "Social backwardness can contribute to educational backwardness and educational backwardness may perpetuate social backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	Both are often no m ore than the inevitable corollaries of the extremes of poverty and the deadening weight of custom and tradition."
RatioOfTheDecision	253.
Precedent	The very fact that the <ORG> itself has given a weightage of 12 points to 'social backwardness' and 6 points to 'educational backwardness' and 4 points to 'economic backwardness' (vide paragraph 11.24 of Chapter XI) shows in very clear terms that 'social backwardness' is taken as a predominant factor in ascertaining the backwardness of a class under Article 16(4).
Precedent	254.
Precedent	<CITATION_599701>  Suppl.
Precedent	1 SCR 439 at page 454 <NAME>, J. observed that "economic backwardness might have contributed to social backwardness...." This observation tends to show that <NAME>, J. was of the view that economic backwardness may contribute to social backwardness.
Precedent	With respect to the learned Judge, I am unable to agree with his view.
Precedent	255.
Precedent	<NAME>, J. in <NAME> has expressed a similar view that if economic criterion for compensatory discrimination or affirmative action is accepted, it wou ld strike at the root cause of "social and educational backwardness...." thereby holding that only criterion which can be devised is the 'economic backwardness' for identifying 'socially and educationally backward classes' ignoring the predominance of social backwardness.
Precedent	I am unable to share this above view.
Precedent	256.
Precedent	How far the <ORG> would be competent to identify the 'Backward class' is explained by <NAME>, J. in <NAME> in the following words:  We are afraid <ORG> are not necessarily the most competent to identify backward classes or to lay down guidelines for their identification except in broad and very general way.
RatioOfTheDecision	We are equipped for; that we have no legal barometers to measure social backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	We are truly removed from the people, particularly those of the backward classes, by layer upon layer of gradation and degradation.
RatioOfTheDecision	257.
RatioOfTheDecision	Let us have a glance over the Report in identifying the 'backward classes' by testing the same on the touchstone of various established criteria.
RatioOfTheDecision	258.
RatioOfTheDecision	In C hapter XI of the Report (Volume I part I) under the caption 'Socio-Educational Field Survey and Criteria of Backwardness' it is categorically stated that after most comprehensive enquiries and survey in the socio-educational fields with the association and help of top social scientists and specialists in the country as well as experts from a number of disciplines, the <ORG> had prepared the "Indicators (Criteria) for Social and Educational Backwardness" on the analysis of data and submitted its report.
RatioOfTheDecision	The relevant paragraphs 11.23, 11.24 and 11.25 showing the criteria for identification of backwardness are as follows:  Indicators (Criteria) for Social and Educational Backwardness 11.23 As a result of the above exercise, the <ORG> evolved eleven 'Indicators' or 'criteria' for determining social and educational backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	These 11 'Indicators' were grouped under three broad heads, i.e.
RatioOfTheDecision	Social, Educational and Economic.
Precedent	They are:-  A.
Precedent	Social  (i) Castes/Classes considered as socially backward by ot hers.
Precedent	(ii) Castes/Classes which mainly depend on manual labour for their livelihood.
Precedent	(iii) Castes/Classes where at least 25% females and 10% males above the <ORG> average get married at an age below 17 years in rural areas and at least 10% females and 5% males do so in urban areas.
Precedent	(iv) Castes/Classes where participation of females in work is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
Fact	B.
Fact	Educational  (v) Castes/Classes where the number of children in the age group of 5-15 years who never attended school is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
Fact	(vi) Castes/Classes where the rate of student drop-out in the age group of 5-15 years is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
Fact	(vii) Castes/Classes amongst whom the proportion of matriculates is at least 25% below the <ORG> average.
Fact	C. Economic  (viii) Castes/Classes where the average value of family assets is at least 25% below the <ORG> average.
Fact	(ix) Castes/Classes where the number of families living in Kuccha houses is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
Fact	(x) Ca stes/Classes where the source of drinking water is beyond half a kilometer for more than 50% of the households.
Fact	(xi) Castes/Classes where the number of households having taken consumption loan is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
Fact	11.24 As the above three groups are not of equal importance for our purpose, separate weightage was given to 'Indicators' in each group.
Fact	All the social 'Indicators' were given a weightage of 3 points each, Educational 'Indicators' a weightage of 2 points each and Economic 'Indicators' a wightage of one point each.
RulingByLowerCourt	Economic, in addition to Social and Educational Indicators, were considered important as they directly flowed from social and educational backwardness.
RulingByLowerCourt	This also helped to highlight the fact that socially and educationally backward classes are economically backward also.
RulingByLowerCourt	11.25 It will be seen that from the values given to each Indicator, the total score adds upto 22.
RulingByLowerCourt	All these 11 Indicators were applied to all the castes covered by the survey for a particular <ORG>.
RulingByLowerCourt	As a result of this application, all castes which had a score of 50 per cent (i.e.
RulingByLowerCourt	11 points) or above were listed as socially and educationally backward and the rest were treated as 'advanced'.
RulingByLowerCourt	(It is a sheer coincidence that the number of indicators and minimum point score for backwardness, both happen to be eleven).
RulingByLowerCourt	Further, in case the number of households covered by the survey for any particular caste were below 20, it was left out of consideration, as the sample was considered too small for any dependable inference.
Precedent	259.
Precedent	It is crystal clear that the <ORG> only on the basis of the galaxy of facts unearthed and massive statistics collected it, has made its recommendations on a very scientific basis of course taking 'caste' as the primary criterion in identifying the backward class in Hindu society and the occupation as the basis for identifying all those in whose societies, the caste system is not prevalent.
Precedent	260.
Precedent	It is not necessary for a class to be designated as a backward class that it should be  situated similarly to the Scheduled Castes and scheduled Tribes.
Precedent	261.
Precedent	<NAME>, J. in Balaram while examining a similar issue after making reference to the cases of <NAME>, <NAME> and <NAME> stated, "None of the above decisions lay down that socially and educationally backward class must be exactly similar in all respects to that of Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes."
Precedent	262.
Precedent	<NAME>, J. in <NAME> while dealing with the observations made in <NAME> "that the backward classes for whose improvement special provision is contemplated by Article 15(4) are in the matter of their backwardness comparable to Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes" observed thus:  There is no point in attempting to determine the social backwardness of other classes by applying the test of nearness to the conditions of existence of the Scheduled Castes.
Precedent	Such a test would practically nullify the provision for reservation for socially and educationally Backward Classes other than Scheduled Castes and Tribes.
Precedent	2 63.
Precedent	Criticism levelled against <ORG> <ORG>  264.
Argument	The learned senior counsel, Mr. <NAME>, Mr. <NAME>, Smt.
Argument	<NAME> and Mr. <NAME> assisted by a battery of layers appearing for the petitioners condemn the recommendations of the <ORG> on the various grounds.
Fact	Therefore, it has become unavoidable to meet their challenges, it may not be necessary otherwise to express any opinion on the correctness and adequacy of the exercise done by the <ORG>.
Fact	265.
Argument	Taking pot-shots at the Mandal <ORG> recommending exclusive reservation for SEBCs, the belligerent anti-reservationists denigrate the report by making scathing criticism and indiscriminately trigger off a volley of bullets against the <ORG>.
Argument	The first attack against the <ORG> is that it is perpetuating the evils of caste system and accentuating caste consciousness besides impeding the doctrine of secularism, the net effect of which would be dangerous and disastrous for the rapid development of the Indian socie ty as a whole marching towards the goal of the welfare state.
Argument	According to them, the identification of SEBCs by the <ORG> on the basis of caste system is bizarre and barren of force, much less exposing hollowness.
Argument	Therefore, the OMs issued on the strength of the Mandal Report which is solely based on the caste criterion are violative of Article 16(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	266.
RatioOfTheDecision	The above criticism, in my considered view, is very uncharitable and bereft of the factual position.
RatioOfTheDecision	Hence it has to be straightaway rejected as unmeritorious since that Report is not actually based solely on caste criteria but on the anvil of various factors grouped under three heads i.e.
RatioOfTheDecision	social, educational and economic backwardness but giving more importance - rightly too - to the social backwardness as having a direct consequence of caste status.
RatioOfTheDecision	267.
RatioOfTheDecision	Adopting the policy of 'Running with the hare and hunting with the hounds', a conciliatory argument was advanced saying that although it is necessary to make provisions for providing equality of op portunity in matters of public employment 'in favour of any backward class' in terms of Article 16(4 ), the present <ORG> based on 1931 census can never serve a correct basis for identifying the 'backward class', that therefore, a fresh <ORG> under Article 340(1) of the Constitution is required to be appointed to make a fresh wide survey sumey through out the length and breadth of the country and submit a new list of OBCs (other backward classes) on the basis of the present day <ORG> and that there are million ways of guaranteeing progress of backward classes and ensuring that it percolates down the social scale, but <ORG> is the one.
RatioOfTheDecision	268.
RatioOfTheDecision	Firstly, in my view if the above argument is accepted it will result in negation of the just claim of the <ORG> to avail the benefit of Article 16(4) which is a fundamental right.
RatioOfTheDecision	269.
RatioOfTheDecision	Secondly, this attack is based on a misconception.
RatioOfTheDecision	A perusal of the <ORG> would indicate that the 1931 census does not have been even a remote connection with the id entification of OBCs.
RatioOfTheDecision	But on the other hand, they are identified only on the basis on the country-wide socio-educational field survey and the census report of 1961 particularly for the identification of primitive tribes, aboriginal tribes, hill tribes, forest tribes and indigenous tribes personal knowledge gained through extensive touring and receipt of voluminous public evidence and lists of OBCs notified by various States.
RatioOfTheDecision	It was only after the identification of OBCs, the <ORG> was faced with the task of determining their population percentage and at that stage 1931 census become relevant.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is to be further noted after 1931 census, no caste-wise statistics had been collected.
RatioOfTheDecision	In fact, the identification of classes by the <ORG> was based on the realities prevailing in 1980 and not in 1931.
Precedent	It is brought to our notice that the same method had already been adopted in Section 5 of the Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes Order (Amendment) Act , 1976.
Precedent	270.
Precedent	Thirdly, the <ORG> cannot be said to  have ignored this factual position and found fault with for relying on 1931 census.
Precedent	In fact, this position is made clear by the <ORG> itself in Chapter XII of its Report, the relevant paragraphs of which read thus:  12.19 Systematic caste-wise enumeration of population was introduced by <ORG> in 1881 and discontinued in 1931.
Precedent	In view of this, figures of caste-wise population beyond 1931 are not available.
Precedent	But assuming that the inter se rate of growth of population of various castes, communities, and religious groups over the last half a century has remained more or less the same, it is possible to work out the percentage that all these groups constitute of the total population of the country.
Precedent	12.10 Working on the above basis, the <ORG> culled out caste/community-wise population figures from the census records of 1931 and, then grouped them into broad caste-clusters and religious groups.
Precedent	These collectivities were subsequently aggregated under five major heads i.e.
Precedent	(i) Schedu led Castes and Scheduled Tribes; (ii) Non-Hindu communities, Religious Groups, etc.
Precedent	; (iii) Forward Hindu Castes and Communities; (iv) Backward Hindu Caste and Communities; and (v) Backward Non-Hindu Communities....  271.
Precedent	In Balaram, wherein a similar argument was addressed, this Court after going through the Report of <ORG> of the State of Andhra Pradesh, felt the difficulty of the non-availability of the Caste-wise statistics after 1931 census and pointed out that in Andhra, the figures of 1921 census were available and in Telangana area, 1931 census of caste-wise statistics was available.
Precedent	272.
Precedent	In the background of the above discussion, the anti-reservationists cannot have any legitimate grievance and justifiably demand this Court to throw the Report over-board on the mere ground that 1931 census had been taken into consideration by the <ORG>.
Precedent	273.
Precedent	As pointed out by this Court in Balaram that no conclusions can always be scientifically accurate in such matters.
Precedent	If at all the  attack perpetrated on the <ORG> renders any remedy to the anti-reservationists, it would be only for the purpose of putting the <ORG> in cold storage as has happened to the <ORG> of the First Backward Classes <ORG>.
Precedent	274.
Fact	Therefore, for the aforementioned reasons, I hold that the above submission made against the <ORG> with reference to the consideration of <ORG> of 1931 cannot be conuntenanced.
Fact	275.
Fact	After having gone through the <ORG>'s <ORG> very assiduously and punctiliously, I am of the firm view that the <ORG> only after deeply considering the social, educational and economic backwardness of various classes of citizens of our country in the light of the various propositions and tests laid down by this <ORG> had submitted its <ORG> enumerating various classes of persons who are to be treated as OBCs.
Fact	The recommendations made in the present <ORG> after a long lull since the submission of the <ORG> by the First Backward Classes <ORG> are supportive of affirmative action program mes holding the members of the historically disadvantaged groups for centuries to catch up with the standards of competition set up by a well advanced society.
Fact	276.
Fact	As a matter of fact, the <ORG> wanted to reserve 52% of all the posts in <ORG> for OBCs commensurate with their ratio in the population.
Fact	However, in deference to legal limitation it has recommended a reservation of 27% only even though the population of OBCs is almost twice this figure.
Fact	277.
Fact	Yet another argument on behalf of the anti-reservationsits was addressed contending that if the recommendations of the <ORG> are implemented, it would result in the sub-standard replacing the standard and the reins of power passing from meritocracy to mediocrity; that the upshot will be in demoralization and discontent and that it would revitalize caste system, and cleave the nation into two - forward and backward - and open up new vistas for internecine conflict and fissiparous forces, and make backwardness a vested interest.
Fact	278.
RatioOfTheDecision	Th e above tortuous line of reasoning, in my view is not only illogical, inconceivable, unreasonable and unjustified but also utterly overlooks the stark grim reality of the SEBCs suffering from social stigma and ostracism in the present day scenario of hierarchical caste system.
RatioOfTheDecision	The very object of Article 16(4) is to ensure equality of opportunity in matters of public employment and give adequate representation to those who have been placed in a very discontent position from time immemorial on account of sociological reasons.
RatioOfTheDecision	To put it differently, the purpose of Clause (4) is to ensure the benefits flowing from the fountain of this clause on the beneficiaries - namely the Backward Classes - who in the opinion of the Constitution makers, would have otherwise found it difficult to enter into public services, competing with advanced classes and who could not be kept in limbo until they are benefited by the positive action schemes and who have suffered and are still suffering from historic disabilities arising fro m past discrimination or disadvantage or both.
RatioOfTheDecision	However, unfortunately all of them had been kept at bay on account of various factors, operating against them inclusive of poverty.
RatioOfTheDecision	They continue to be deprived of enjoyment of equal opportunity in matters of public employment despite there being sufficient statistical evidence in proof of manifest imbalance in <ORG> jobs which evidence is sufficient to support an affirmative action plan.
RatioOfTheDecision	If candidates belonging to <ORG> (characterised as mediocre by anti-reservationists), are required to enter the open field competition, along with the candidates belonging to advanced communities without any preferential treatment in public Services in their favour and go through a rigid test mechanism being the highly intelligence test and professional ability test as conditions of employment, certainly those conditions would operate as "built-in headwinds" for <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is, therefore, in order to achieve equality of employment opportunity, Clause 4 of Article 16 empowers  the <ORG> to provide permissible reservation to SEBCs in the matters of appointments or posts as a remedy so as to set right the manifest imbalance in the field of public employment.
RatioOfTheDecision	279.
RatioOfTheDecision	The argument that the implementation of the recommendations of the <ORG> would result in demoralisation and discontent has no merit because conversely can it not be said that the non-implementation of the recommendations would result in demoralisation and discontent among the SEBCs.
RatioOfTheDecision	280.
RatioOfTheDecision	Though 'equal protection' clause prohibits the <ORG> from making unreasonable discrimination in providing preferences and facilities for any section of its people, nonetheless it requires the <ORG> to afford substantially equal opportunities to those, placed unequally.
RatioOfTheDecision	281.
RatioOfTheDecision	The basic policy of reservation is to off-set the inequality and remove the manifest imbalance, the victims of which for bygone generations lag far behind and demand equality by special preferences and their strategies.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, a comprehensive methodological ap proach encompassing jurisprudential, comparative, historical and anthropological conditions is necessary.
RatioOfTheDecision	Such considerations raise controversial issues transcending the routine legal exercise because certain social groups who are inherently unequal and who have fallen victims of societal discrimination require compensatory treatment.
RatioOfTheDecision	Needless to emphasise that equality in fact or substantive equality involves the necessity of beneficial treatment in order to attain the result which establishes an equilibrium between two sections placed unequally.
Precedent	282.
Precedent	It is more appropriate to recall that "There is equality only among equals and to equate unequals is to perpetuate inequality."
Precedent	283.
Precedent	Therefore, the submission that the implementation of the recommendations of the <ORG> will curtail concept of equality as enshrined under Article 14 of the Constitution and destroy the basic structure of the Constitution, cannot be countenanced.
Precedent	284.
Argument	One of the arguments criticising the <ORG> is that the said <ORG> virtually  rewrites the Constitution and in effect buries 50 fathoms deep the ideal of equality and that if the recommendations are given effect to and implemented, the efficiency of administration will come to a grinding halt.
Argument	This submission is tantamount to saying that the reservation of 27% to <ORG> as per the impugned OMs is opposed to the concept of equality.
Argument	285.
Argument	There is no question of rewriting the Constitution, because the <ORG> has acted only under the authority of the notification issued by the President.
Precedent	It has after laying down the parameters in the light of the various pronouncements of this <ORG> has ultimately submitted its Report recommending the reservation in tune with the spirit of Article 16(4).
Precedent	286.
Precedent	The question whether the candidates, belonging to the <ORG> should be given a preferential treatment in matters of public employment to such time as it is necessary, receives a fitting reply in Devadasan wherein <NAME>, J.
Precedent	(as the learned Chief Justice then was) has observed, by citing an i llustration as to how the manifest imbalance and inequality will occur otherwise, thus:  To make my point clear, take the illustration of a horse race.
RatioOfTheDecision	Two horses are set down to run a race - one is a first class race horse and the other an ordinary one.
RatioOfTheDecision	Both are made to run from the same starting point.
RatioOfTheDecision	Though theoretically they are given equal opportunity to run the race, in practice the ordinary horse is not given an equal opportunity to compete with the race horse.
RatioOfTheDecision	Indeed that is denied to it.
RatioOfTheDecision	So a handicap may be given either in the nature of extra weight or a start from a longer distance.
RatioOfTheDecision	By doing so, what would otherwise have been a farce of a competition would be made a real one.
RatioOfTheDecision	The same difficulty had confronted the makers of the Constitution at the time it was made.
RatioOfTheDecision	Centuries of calculated oppression and habitual submission reduced a considerable section of our community to a life of serfdom.
RatioOfTheDecision	It would be well nigh impossible to raise their standards if the doctrine of equal opportunity was strictly  enforced in their case.
RatioOfTheDecision	They would not have any chance if they were made to enter the open field of competition without adventitious aids till such time when they could stand on their own legs.
RatioOfTheDecision	That is why the makers of the Constitution introduced Clause (4) in Article 16.
Precedent	287.
Precedent	It will be befitting, in my opinion, to extract a passage from the book, Bakke, Defunis and Minority Admissions (The Quest for Equal Opportunity) by <NAME> wherein at page 9, the unequal competition is explained by an analogy which is as follows:  A good way to appreciate the "something more" quandary is to consider the metaphor of the shackled runner, an analogy frequently advanced by spokesmen for minorities:  'Imagine two runners at the starting line, readying for the 100-yeard dash.
Precedent	One has his legs shackled, the other not.
Fact	The gun goes off and the race begins.
RatioOfTheDecision	Not surprisingly, the unfettered runner immediately takes the lead and then rapidly increases the distance between himself and his shackled competition.
RatioOfTheDecision	Before  the finish line is crossed, over the judging official blows his whistle, calls off the contest on the grounds that the unequal conditions between the runners made it an unfair competition, and orders removal of the shackles.'
RatioOfTheDecision	Surely few would deny that pitting a shackled runner against an unshackled one is inequitable and does not provide equality of opportunity.
RatioOfTheDecision	Hence, cancelling the race and freeing the disadvantaged runner of his shackles seem altogether apporpriate.
RatioOfTheDecision	Once beyond this point, however, agreement fades rapidly.
Fact	The key question becomes: what should be done so that the two runners can resume the contest on a basis of fair competition?
Fact	Is it enough after removing the shackles, to place both runners back at the starting point?
Fact	Or is "something more" needed, and if so, what?
Fact	Should the rules of the running be altered, and if so, how?
Fact	Should the previously shackled runner be given a compensatory edge, or should the other runner be handicapped in some way?
Fact	How much edge or handicap?
Precedent	288.
Precedent	To one of  the queries posed by the author of the above analogy, the proper reply would be that even if the shackles whether of iron chains or silken cord, are removed and the shackled person has become unfettered, he must be given a compensatory edge until he realises that there is no more shackle on his legs because even after the removal of shackles he does not have sufficient courage to compete with the runner who has been all along unfettered.
Precedent	289.
Precedent	Mr. <NAME>, an intervener demonstrably explained that as unwatered seeds do not germinate, unprotected backward class citizens will wither away.
Precedent	290.
Precedent	The above illustration and analogies would lead to a conclusion that there is an ocean of difference between a well advanced class and a backward class in a race of open competition in the matters of public employment and they, having been placed unequally, cannot be measured by the same yardstick.
Precedent	As repeatedly pointed out, it is only in order to make the unequals equal, this constitutional provision, namely,  Clause (4) of Article 16 has been designed and purposely introduced providing some preferential treatment to the backward class.
Precedent	It is only in case of denial of such preferential treatment, the very concept of equality as enshrined in the Constitution, will get buried 50 fathoms deep.
Precedent	291.
Precedent	A programme of reservation may sacrifice merit but does not in any way sacrifice competence because the beneficiaries under Article 16(4) have to possess the requisite basic qualifications and eligibility and have to compete among themselves though not with the mainstream candidates.
Precedent	292.
Precedent	As <NAME>, J. in <NAME> has rightly observed, "Always one hears the word 'efficiency' as if it is sacrosanct and the sanctorum has to be fiercely guarded.
Precedent	'Efficiency' is not a mantra which is whispered by the Guru in the <NAME>'s ear."
Precedent	293.
Precedent	In yet another context, in the same decision, the learned Judge at page 394 has firmly and irrefutably put the merit argument at rest stating thus:  The real conflict is between the  class of people, who have never been in or who have already moved out of the desert of poverty, illiteracy and backwardness and are entrenched in the oasis of convenient living and those who are still in the desert and want to reach the oasis.
Precedent	There is no enough fruit in the garden and so those who are in, want to keep out those who are out.
Precedent	The disastrous consequences of the so-called meritarian principle to the vast majority of the under-nourished, poverty-stricken, barely literate and vulnerable people of our country are too obvious to be stated.
Precedent	And, what is merit?
Precedent	There is no merit in a system which brings about such consequences.
Precedent	294.
Precedent	Be that as it may, the intelligence, merit, ability, competence, meritocracy, administrative efficiency and achievement cannot be measured by skin-pigmentation or by the surname of an individual indicating his caste.
Precedent	295.
Precedent	In this regard, the observation of <NAME>, J. in Devadasan at page 706 may be recapitulated, which to some extent answers the doubt raised by a sect ion of anti-reservationists that reservation will result in deterioration in the standard of service.
Precedent	The said observation reads as follows:  If the provision deals with reservation - which I hold it does - I do not see how it will be bad because there will be some deterioration in the standard of service.
Precedent	It is inevitable in the nature of reservation that there will be lowering of standards to some extent; but on that account the provision cannot be said to be bad.
Precedent	Indeed, the <ORG> laid down the minimum qualifications and all the appointments were made from those who had the said qualifications.
Precedent	How far the efficiency of the administrations suffers by this provision is not for me to say, but it is for the <ORG>, which is certainly interested in the maintenance of standards of Us administration.
Precedent	Submission on the theory of past discrimination based on the decisions of the Supreme Court of United <ORG>s  296.
Precedent	Based on certain American decisions, it has been urged that only that group or section of people suf fering from the lingering effects of past discrimination can be classified as 'backward classes' and not others.
RatioOfTheDecision	This submission has to be mentioned for being simply rejected for more than one reason.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even today, the caste discrimination is very much prevalent in India particularly in the rural areas.
RatioOfTheDecision	Secondly, even among the Judges of <ORG>, there is a division of opinion on the theory of lingering effects of past discrimination.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thirdly, this theory cannot be imported to the Indian conditions where the Hindu society even today is suffering from the firm grip of discrimination based on caste system.
RatioOfTheDecision	The vastness and richness of the materials unearthed by the various <ORG> inclusive of <ORG>s' <ORG> unambiguously and pellucidly reveal that in our country, representation of the SEBCs in the services under the <ORG> is grossly inadequate when compared to the representation of the advanced class of citizens, leave apart the complete absence of reservation for SEBCs in the  Central Services.
Precedent	This inadequate representation is not confined to any specific section of the people, but all those who fall under the group of social backwardness whether they are Shudras of Hindu community or similarly situated other backward classes of people in other communities, namely, Muslims, Sikhs, Christians etc.
Precedent	297.
Precedent	Drawing strength on the opinion of <NAME>, J in Regents of <ORG> v. <NAME> 57 L Ed 2d 750, an argument has been advanced that Article 16(1) permits only preferences but not reservations.
Precedent	In the above <NAME>'s case, a white male who had been denied admission to the medical school at <ORG> at Davis for two consecutive years, instituted an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against the Regents of the University in <ORG> Yolo County, California alleging the invalidity under the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, a provision of the California Constitution, and the prescription in racial discrim ination in any programme receiving federal financial assistance of the medical school's special admissions programme.
Precedent	<ORG> announced its decision amid confusion and controversy.
Precedent	There was no clear majority, but a three-way split namely four Judges took one view and four other Judges took a different view, leaving Justice <NAME> straddling the middle.
Precedent	In their joint opinion partially concurring and partially dissenting, Justices <NAME>, <NAME>, <NAME> and <NAME> took issue with <NAME>l's conclusion that the <NAME> programme was unconstitutional and said, "We cannot...let color blindness become myopia which masks the reality that many 'created equal' have been treated within our lifetimes as inferior both by the law and by their fellow citizens."
Precedent	298.
Precedent	Attention was also drawn to <NAME> v. <NAME> [1974] 40 L. Ed.
Precedent	2nd 164.
Precedent	299.
Precedent	The analytical study of American cases shows that the American-style justification of positive discrimination is on the ground of utility whereas the Indian-styl e justification is on the ground of constitutional rights.
Precedent	Therefore, the decision in relation to a racial discrimination relating to an admission to the medical school cannot be of much assistance in the matter of identification of 'backward classes' falling under Article 16(4).
Precedent	The dicta in Bakke and Defunis is one akin to the principle covered under Article 15(4) and not under Article 16(1) or 16(4).
Precedent	300.
Precedent	Whether Article 16(4) is an exception to Articles 16(1) and (2)?
Precedent	301.
Precedent	Mr <NAME>, the learned senior counsel, appearing on behalf of <ORG> articulated that Articles 16(4) and 335 are so worded as to give a wide latitude to the <ORG> in the matter of reservation and that Article 16(4) having no-obstinate clause reading "Nothing in this Article shall prevent the <ORG> from making any provision...." has an over-riding effect on Article 16(2).

Precedent	303.
Precedent	Yet another argument placing reliance on <NAME> case (I) (supra) was advanced contending that Article 16(4) is an enabling provision conferring a discretionary power on the <ORG> to make a reservation of appointments in favour of backward class of citizens.
Precedent	Placing reliance on the view expressed by <NAME>, <NAME> (as the learned Chief Justice then was) in <CITATION_1074353> it was further urged that Article 16(4) which is in the nature of an exception or proviso to Article 16(1) cannot nullify equality of opportunity guaranteed to all citizens by that article.
Precedent	304.
Precedent	In my view, that Clause (4) of Article 16 is not an exception to Article 16(1) and (2) but it is an enabling provision and permissive in character overriding Article 16(1) and (2); that it is a source of reservation for appointments or posts in the <ORG> so far as  the backward class of citizens is concerned and that under Clause (1) of Article 16 reservation for appointments or posts can be made to other sections of the society such as physically handicapped etc.
Precedent	305.
Precedent	There is complete unanimity of judicial opinion of this <ORG> that under Article 16(4) the <ORG> can make adequate provisions for reservations of appointments of posts in favour of any backward class of citizens, if in the opinion of the <ORG> such 'backward class' is not adequately represented in the <ORG>.
Precedent	In fact in <CITATION_575853> AIR 1951 SC 229 a seven Judges Bench of this <ORG> held that "reservation of posts in favour of any backward class of citizens cannot, therefore, be regarded as unconstitutional".
RatioOfTheDecision	Not a single decision of this <ORG> has cast slightest shadow of doubt on the constitutional validity of reservation.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, in view of the above position of law.
Precedent	I am not inclined to embark upon an elaborate discussion on this question any further.
Precedent	306.
Precedent	Whether Reservation under Article 1 6(4) can be made by Executive Order?
Precedent	307.
Precedent	The next submission that the provision for reservation of appointments or posts under Article 16(4) can be made only by a legislation and not by an executive order is unsustainable.
Precedent	This contention as a matter of fact has already been answered in (1) <NAME> (supra) and (2), <CITATION_1395006> .
