Precedent	418.
Precedent	What is sought to be identified is not caste, religion and the like, but social and educational backwardness, generally manifested by disabilities such as illiteracy, humiliating isolation, poverty, physical and mental degeneration, incurable diseases, etc.
Precedent	Living in abject poverty and squalor, engaged in demeaning occupations to keep body and soul together, and bereft of sanitation, medical aid and other facilities, these unfortunate classes of citizens bearing the badges of historical discrimination and naked exploitation are generally traceable in the midst of the lowest of the low classes euphemistically described as Harijans and in fact treated as un touchables.
Precedent	To deny them the constitutional protection of reservation solely by reason of change of faith or religion is to endanger the very concept of secularism and the raison d'etre of reservation.
Precedent	419.
Precedent	No class of citizens can be classified as backward solely by reason of religion, race, caste, sex, descent, place of birth, residence or any of them.
Precedent	But any one or all of these factors mentioned in Article 15(1) or Article 16(2) can be taken into account along with other relevant factors in identifying classes of citizens who are socially and educationally backward.
Precedent	What is significant is that such identification should not be made solely with reference to the criteria specified in Article 15(1) or Article 16(2 ), but with reference to the social and educational backwardness of classes of citizens.
Precedent	Referring to the words "socially and educationally backward classes of citizens" appearing in Article 15(4 ), this <ORG> stated in <CITATION_1734464> .
Precedent	:  The expression 'classes of citizens' indicates a homog eneous section of the people who are grouped together because of certain likeliness and common traits and who are identifiable by some common attributes.
Precedent	The homogeneity of the class of citizens is social and educational backwardness.
Precedent	Neither caste nor religion nor place or birth will be the uniform element of common attributes to make them a class of citizens.
Precedent	It may, however, be true that backwardness is associated specially with people of a particular religion or race or caste or place of birth or residence or any other category mentioned in Article 15(1) or Article 16(2).
Precedent	In that event, any one or more of such criteria along with other relevant factors, may be taken into consideration to reach the conclusion as to social and educational backwardness.
Precedent	Hard and primitive living conditions in remote and inaccessible areas, where the inhabitants have neither the means of livelihood nor facilities for education, health service or other civic amenities, are some such relevant criteria, <CITATION_579569> and Or s. ; <CITATION_27045> .
Precedent	420.
Precedent	The city slum dwellers, the inhabitants of the pavements, afflicted and disfigured in many cases by diseases like leprosy, caught in the vicious grip of grinding penury, and making a meagre living by begging besides the towering mansions of affluence, transcend all barriers of religion, caste, race, etc.
Precedent	in their degradation, suffering and humiliation.
Precedent	They are the living monument of backwardness and a shameful reminder of our national indifference, a cruel betrayal of what the preamble to the Constitution proclaims.
Precedent	No matter what caste or religion they may claim, their present plight of animal like existence, living on crumbs picked from garbage cans or coins flung from moving cars - a common painful sight in our metropolis - entitles them to every kind of affirmative action to redeem themselves from the in equities of past and continuing discrimination.
Precedent	Rehabilitation and resettlement of these unfortunate victims of societal indifference and Governmental neglect and appropriat e and urgent measures for <ORG> aided health care, education and special technical training for their progeny with a view to their employment in public services are the primary responsibility of a welfare <ORG>.
Precedent	These are the classes of people specially chosen by the law for prompt and effective affirmative action, not by reason of their caste or religion, but solely by reason of their backwardness in tracing which any relevant criterion is a useful tool.
Precedent	421.
Precedent	In identifying backwardness, caste, religion, residence etc.
Precedent	are of course relevant factors, but none of them is a dominant or much less an indispensable factor.
Precedent	What is of ultimate relevance is the social and educational backwardness of a class of citiznes, whatever be their caste, religion, etc.
Precedent	422.
Precedent	Identification of the backward classes for the purpose of reservation must be with reference to their social and educational backwardness resulting from the continuing ill effects of prior discrimination or exploitation; and not solely with reference to  any one or more of the prohibited criteria mentioned in Article 15(1) or Article 16(2 ), although any one or more of such criteria may have been the ultimate cause of such discrimination or exploitation and the resultant poverty and backwardness.

Precedent	What chains them, what incapacitates them, what distinguishes them, what qualifies them for favoured treatment of the law is their backwardness: their badges of proverty, disease, misery, ignorance and humiliation.
Precedent	It is conceivable that the entire caste is a backward class.
Precedent	In that event, they form a class of people for the special protection of Articles 15(4) and 16(4), not by reason of their caste, which is merely incidental, but by reason of their social and educational, backwardness which is identified to be the result of prior or continuing discrimination and its ill effects and which is comparable to that of the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes.

Precedent	But to avoid any risk of keeping ours a divided society, the Constitution makers provided ample safeguards for Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes (SC/ST) the only category of backward class which could be compared to the Negroes in America.
Precedent	American philosophy developed by courts that discrimination having  arisen due to race consciousness the remedy too should be race based, appears to have been inspired by our constitutional provisions which takes every precaution to remedy the caste related evil of <ORG> by caste based reservation.
Precedent	But the same can not be adopted for other backward classes as it would be distortion of constitutional interpretation by importing a concept which was deliberately and purposely avoided.
Precedent	Insistence, for claiming reservation for the remaining or for all others who were in so-called broader category of Sudras not because they Were really backward without any regard to social and economic conditions, would be unfair to history and unjust to society.
Precedent	What is constitutionally provided has to be adhered to in spirit but not on assumption that all amongst Hindus who fell in the broader category of Sudras were subjected to same treatment as untouchables in India or Negroes in America.
Precedent	History, social or political, does not bear it out.
Precedent	Reservation for other backward class is no doubt const itutionally permisible, on social and economic conditions which prevailed in the country and are still prevailing and not on benign steps for Negroes upheld by foreign courts.
Precedent	Judicial activism has no doubt in America been remarkable in absence of any constitutional protection for the Negroes but our courts are not required to undertake the exercise as our constitutional statesmanship has no parallel in the world where to achieve egalitatian society truly and really it devised mechanism of treating the backward class of citizens, 'differently' by Articles 16(4) and 15(4) to bring them at par with others so that they could be treated equally.
Precedent	The policy of official discrimination is, unique in the world both in the range of benefits involved and in the magnitude of the groups eligible for them.
Precedent	(8)  642.
Precedent	Caste has never been accepted by this Court as exclusive or sole criteria for determination or identification of backward class.
Precedent	That is why the communal Government Order in Champakam and reservation, except  for SC/ST and Hindu backward, in S. Venkatramana v. State of Madras, AIR 1951 SC 229, were invalidated.
Precedent	Caste based evil was so repugnant that even when communal Government Order issued by the State of Madras a legacy of caste based reservation practised in Madras since thirties and forties was struck down and the Constitution was amended and Article 15(4) was added the basic philosophy against the caste was neither eroded nor mitigated and ameliorative steps were made state-responsibility for socially and educationally backward castes.
Precedent	<NAME> adopted test of, comparability of backward classes with Scheduled Caste and Scheduled Tribe as a result of combined reading of Article 340(1) and Article 338(3).
Precedent	Two major drawbacks were noticed in identifying backward class with caste, one, 'it may not always be legal and may perhaps contain the vice of perpetuating the caste', and other 'if the caste of the group of citizens was made the sole basis for determining the social backwardness of the social group, the test  would inevitably break down in relation to many sections of Indian society which do not recognise caste in the conventional sense known to Hindu society'.
Precedent	In Chitralekha the <ORG> observed that 'caste is only a relevant circumstance in ascertaining the backwardness of a class and there is nothing in the judgment of this <ORG> (<NAME>) which precludes the authority concerned from determining the social backwardness of a group of citizens if it can do so without reference to caste'.
Precedent	<NAME> too did not differ with <NAME> nor it carved out any new path.
Precedent	The <ORG> accepted the determination of backward class as, the explanation given by the State of Madras had not been controverted by any rejoinder affidavit.
Precedent	The <ORG> observed, 'that though the list shows certain caste the member of those castes are classes of educationally and socially backward citizens'.
Precedent	In Sagar the <ORG> was concerned with a list where backwardness was determined amongst others on caste taking it as one of the relevant test for determin ation of backwardness.
Precedent	Therefore, the <ORG> agreeing with <NAME> observed, 'in determining whether a particular section forms a class caste cannot be excluded altogether.
Precedent	But in the determination of a class a test solely based upon caste or a community cannot also be accepted'.
Precedent	In <ORG> it was observed that, 'a caste has always been recognised as a class'.
Precedent	Support for this was sought {torn <NAME> and it was observed that it was authority 'for the proposition that the classification of backward classes on the basis of caste is within the purview of Article 15(4) if those castes are shown to be socially and educationally backward.
Precedent	But <NAME> was decided as the caste included in the list were in fact socially and educationally backward.
Precedent	<NAME>, too, followed the same and relying on <NAME>, <NAME> and <ORG> upheld the test as entire caste was found to be socially and economically backward.
Precedent	'Caste, ipso facto, is not class in secular state' was said in Soshit Karamchari.
Precedent	In Jayshree it wa s held that caste could not be made the sole basis for reservation.
Precedent	Ratio in <ORG>, <NAME>, <NAME> and Peeriakaruppan are wrongly understood and erroneously applied.
Precedent	All these decisions turned on facts as the <ORG> in each case upheld the classification not because it was done on caste but those included in the list deserved the protection.
Precedent	Different streams of thought may appear from various decisions but none has accepted caste as the sole criteria for determination of backwardness.
Precedent	(9)  643.
Precedent	'Backward class' in Article 16(4) thus cannot be read as backward caste.
RatioOfTheDecision	What is the scope then?
RatioOfTheDecision	Is it social backwardness, educational backwardness, economic backwardness, social and economic backwardness, natural backwardness etc.?
RatioOfTheDecision	In absence of any indication expressly or impliedly any group or collectivity which can be legitimately considered as, 'backward' for purposes of representation in service would be included in the expression 'backward class'.
RatioOfTheDecision	Word 'any' is indicative of that the backward class was not  visualised in singular.
RatioOfTheDecision	When Constitution was framed the anxiety was to undo the historical backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	Yet a word of wider import was used to avoid any close-door policy.
RatioOfTheDecision	For instance, backwardness arising out of natural reasons was never contemplated.
RatioOfTheDecision	But today with developments of human rights effort is being made to encourage those to whom nature has not been so kind.
Precedent	Do such persons not form a class?
Precedent	Are they not backward?
Precedent	They cannot, obviously compete on equal level with others.
Precedent	Backwardness which the Constitution makers had to tackle by making special provision, due to social and economic condition, was different but that does not exclude backwardness arising due to different reasons in new set up.
Precedent	644.
Precedent	Although dictionarily the word 'any' may mean one or few and even all yet the meaning of a word has to be understood in the context it has been used.
Precedent	In Article 16(4) it cannot mean all as it would render the whole Article unworkable.
Precedent	The only, reasonable, meaning that can be attributed to it is tha t it should be the States' discretion to pick out one or more than one from amongst numerous groups or collectivity identified or accepted as backward class for purposes of reservation.
Precedent	Whether such picking is reasonable and satisfies the test of judicial review is another matter.
Precedent	That explains the rationale for the non-obstante clause being discretionary and not mandatory.
Precedent	A State is not bound to grant reservation to every backward class.
Precedent	In one State or at one place or at one point of time it may be historical and social backwardness or geographical and habitational backwardness and at another it may be social and educational or backwardness arising out of natural cause.
Precedent	(10)  645.
Precedent	From out of various backward class of citizens who could be provided protection under Article 16(4) the President has been empowered by Article 340 to appoint a Commission to investigate the conditions of socially and educationally backward classes within the territory of India.
Precedent	What does the expression 'socially and educational ly backward classes' connote?
Precedent	How it should be understood?
Precedent	Is it social backwardness only?
Precedent	Is the educational backwardness surplus-age?.
Precedent	Article 340(1) of the Constitution reads as under:  The President may by order appoint a <ORG> consisting of such persons as he thinks fit to investigate the conditions of socially and and educationally backward classes within the territory of India and the difficulties under which they labour and to make recommendations as to the steps that should be taken by the <ORG> or any <ORG> to remove such difficulties and to improve their condition and as to the grants that should be made for the purpose by the <ORG> or any <ORG> and the conditions subject to which such grants should be made, and the order appointing such <ORG> shall define the procedure to be followed by the <ORG>.
Precedent	A bare reading of the Article indicates that the avowed objective of this provision is to empower the President to appoint a <ORG> to ascertain the difficulties and the problems of t he socially and educationally backward classes and to make recommendations so that steps may be taken by the Union and the States to solve their problems, remove their difficulties and improve their conditions.
Precedent	Since backwardness has been qualified by the words 'social and educational' the ambit of the expression is not as wide as backward class in Article 16(4).
Precedent	What does it mean then?
Precedent	A social class, 'is an aggregate of persons within a society possessing about the same status'.
Precedent	How to determine backwardness of such a class.
Precedent	The yardstick of backwardness in any society is, primarily, economic.
Precedent	But Indian society, 'has made caste as the sole hierarchy of social ranking and uses the caste system as the basic frame of reference'.
Precedent	<ORG> described it as ascribed status, that is, status of a person determined by his birth.
Precedent	The social backwardness in pre-independence period, no doubt, arose because of caste stratification.
Precedent	Members of castes other than Brahmans, Thakurs and Vaishyas were  socially backward.
Precedent	But with foreign domination, enlightened movements both social and religious, acquisition of wealth and power a gradual caste mobility took place not only to consolidate but even to assert a higher social status.
Precedent	'The struggle launched by these backward castes as a subaltern in the pre-independence period, changed its course in the post independence period' due to vested interest in reservation, 'It is well known that up to year 1931, the last census year for which castes are recorded, there were several castes applying for changing their names to those indicative of higher caste status.
Precedent	In that period name indicated status.
Precedent	The trend now is to claim backwardness both among the Hindus and Muslims by claiming the same caste status by various devices as those who are legally considered as backward caste, are the beneficiaries of reservation.
Precedent	While determining social backwardness, therefore, one cannot loose sight of the type of society, the social mobility, the economic conditions, the polit ical power.
Precedent	Even the Expert Panel noticed few of these but then it got lost in ascribed status.
Precedent	The social backwardness in 1990 for purposes of employment in services cannot be status by birth but backwardness arising out of other elements such as class, power etc.
Precedent	Dr. <NAME> in his book [The Caste System in India] after an elaborate study has concluded,  1.
Precedent	Class, independent of caste, determines social ranking in Indian Society in certain domains;  2.
Precedent	Analysis of caste alone is not sufficient to provide the real picture of stratification in India to-day;  3.
Precedent	A proper study of stratification in modern India must concern with other dimensions, viz., class, status and power.
Precedent	While explaining power he has observed in, 'past power was located in the dominant caste'.
Precedent	But it is now changing in two senses, 'first, power is shifting from one caste (or group of castes) to another.
Precedent	Secondly, power is shifting from caste itself and comes to be located in more differentiated political organs and institutions.
Precedent	This has  been empirically found by <NAME>, and others on the basis of his studies of Kammas and Reddis of Andhra Pradesh.
Precedent	<NAME> writes: "This picture of political competition between the two caste groups is only a modern recurrence of an historic pattern dating back to the fourteenth century.
Precedent	<NAME>' analysis of politics in Mysore gives a central place to rivalries between the dominant castes: "As in Andhra, the <ORG> is dominated by two leading peasant castes, one of which is Lingayat and the other Okkaliga.
Precedent	Lingayat Okkaliga rivalry is colouring every issue, whether it be appointment to government posts or reservation of seats in colleges, or election to local bodies and legislatures."
Precedent	Both - <ORG>'s study in Andhra Pradesh and <NAME> 'in Mysore depict the rise to power of the two pairs of non-Brahman dominant castes followed by the decline of the Brahmans".'
Precedent	Any determination of social backwardness, therefore, cannot be valid unless these important aspects are taken into consideration.
Precedent	646.
Precedent	Educati onal backwardness too was not added just for recitation.
Precedent	No word in Statute, more so in a Constitution, can be read as surplus-age.
Precedent	In none of the decisions of this <ORG> under Article 16(4) it has been held that educational backwardness was irrelevant.
Precedent	In <NAME> declaration of minor community as educationally backward was not accepted as correct since the student community of 5 per thousand was not below the <ORG> average.
Precedent	In <NAME> the <ORG> approved acceptance by the government of criteria adopted by the <ORG> for determining social and edcuational backwardness of the citizen, namely,  (i) the general poverty of the class or community as a whole;  (ii) Occupations pursued by the classes of citizens, the nature of which must be inferior or unclean or undignified and unremunerative or one which does not carry influence or power;  (iii) Caste in relation to Hindus; and  (iv) Educational backwardness.
Precedent	In the hoary past the education amongst Hindus was confined to a particular class, that is, the Brahmins , but with advent of Muslim rule and British regime this barricading fell down, considerably, and the education spread amongst other classes as well.
Precedent	But even in those times there was a section of society which was kept away, deliberately, from education as they were not permitted to enter the schools and colleges.
Precedent	That has been done away with by the Constitution.
Precedent	Yet the educational with all efforts has not filtered to certain classes particularly in rural areas and many traditionally educationally backward still suffer from it.
Precedent	At the same time many groups or collectivity did not opt for education for various reasons, personal or otherwise.
Precedent	Therefore, a <ORG> appointed under Article 340 cannot determine only social backwardness.
Precedent	Any class to be backward under Article 340 must be both socially and educationally backward.
Precedent	647.
Precedent	Two things emerge from it, one, that the backward class in Article 16(4) and socially and educationally in Article 340 , being expressions with different connotations they cannot  be understood in one and same sense.
Precedent	The one is wider and includes the other.
Precedent	A socially and educationally backward class may be backward class but not vice versa.
Precedent	Other is that such investigation cannot be caste based.
Precedent	Meaning of expression 'socially and educationally backward' class of citizens was explained in <NAME> as under:  The expression 'classes of citizens' indicates a homogenous section of the people who are grouped together because of (a) certain likeness and common traits and who are identified by some common attributes.
Precedent	The homogeneity of the class of citizen is social and educational backwardness.
Precedent	Neither caste nor religion nor place of birth will be uniform element or common attributes to make them a class of citizens.
Precedent	648.
Precedent	Even when the report of <ORG> was submitted to <ORG> the memorandum prepared by it, and presented to the <ORG>, emphasised that, efforts should be made, 'to discover some criteria other than caste, which could be of  practical application in determining the backward classes'.
Precedent	Three of the members of the <ORG>, 'were opposed to one of the most crucial recommendations of the <ORG>, that is, the acceptance of caste as a criteria for social backwardness and reservations of posts in government service on that basis'.
Precedent	One of the reasons given for it by the Chairman in his letter was that adopting of caste criteria was, 'going to have a most unhealthy effect on the Muslim and Christian sections of the nation'.
Precedent	649.
Precedent	When Second Backward Class <ORG> was appointed by the President under Article 340 it was required, 'to determine the criteria for determining the socially and educationally backward classes' and, to examine the desirability or otherwise of making provision for the reservation of appointments or posts in favour of such backward classes of citizens which are not adequately represented in public services and posts in connection with the affairs of the <ORG> or of any <ORG>.
Precedent	The order further outlined the pro cedure to be followed by the <ORG> as required by Article 340 by directing it to examine the recommendations of the Backward Classes <ORG> appointed earlier and the considerations which stood in the way of the acceptance of its recommendations by <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	The <ORG> thus was required to undertake the exercise so as to avoid repetition of those failings of due to which the report of first <ORG> could not be implemented.
RatioOfTheDecision	The <ORG> was not oblivious of it as in paragraph 1.17 of the report it observed, Though the above failings are serious, yet the real weakness of the <ORG> lies in its internal contradictions.
RatioOfTheDecision	As stated in para 1.5 of this Chapter, three of the Members were opposed to one of the most crucial recommendations of the <ORG>, that is, the acceptance of caste as a criterion for social backwardness and the reservation of posts in <ORG> services on that basis.
RatioOfTheDecision	Yet the <ORG> undertook extensive exercise for ascertaining social system and opined that, 12.4 In fact , caste being the basic unit of social organisation of Hindu society, castes are the only readily and clearly "recognisable and persistent collectivities.
RatioOfTheDecision	Having done so it determined social and educational backwardness in paragraph 11.23 as under :  11.23 As a result of the above exercise, the <ORG> evolved eleven 'Indicators' or 'criteria' for determining social and educational backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	These 11 'Indicators' were grouped under three broad heads, i.e., Social, Educational and Economic.
RatioOfTheDecision	They are:  A.
RatioOfTheDecision	Social  (i) Castes/Classes considered as socially backward by others.
RatioOfTheDecision	(ii) Castes/Classes which mainly depend on manual labour for their livelihood.
RatioOfTheDecision	(iii) Castes/Classes where at least 25% females and 10% males above the <ORG> average get married at an age below 17 years in rural areas and at least 10% females and 5% males do so in urban areas.
RatioOfTheDecision	(iv) Castes/Classes where participation of females in work is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
Precedent	B.
Precedent	Educational  (v) Castes/Classes where the number of c hildren in the age group of 5-15 years who never attended school is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
Precedent	(vi) Castes/Classes where the rate of student drop-out in the age group of 5-15 years is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
Precedent	(vii) Castes/Classes amongst whom the proportion of matriculates is at least 25% below the <ORG> average.
Precedent	C. Economic  (viii) Castes/Classes where the average value of family assets is at least 25% below the <ORG> average.
Precedent	(ix) Castes/Classes where the number of families living in Kuccha houses is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
Precedent	(x) Castes/Classes where the source of drinking water is beyond half a kilometer for more than 50% of the households.
Precedent	(xi) Castes/Classes where the number of households having taken consumption loan is at least 25% above the <ORG> average.
RatioOfTheDecision	11.24 As the above three groups are not of equal importance for our purpose separate weightage was given to 'Indicators' in each group.
RatioOfTheDecision	All the Social 'Indicators' were given a weightage of 3 points each, <NAME> ucational 'Indicators' a weightage of 2 points each and Economic 'Indicators' a weightage of one point each.
RatioOfTheDecision	Economic, in addition to Social and Educational Indicators, were considered important as they directly flowed from social and educational backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	This also helped to highlight one fact that socially and educationally backward classes are economically backward also.
RatioOfTheDecision	11.25 It well be seen that from the values given to each Indicator, the total score adds up to 22.
RatioOfTheDecision	All these 11 Indicators were applied to all the castes covered by the survey for a particular State.
RatioOfTheDecision	As a result of this aplication, all castes which had a score of 50 per cent (i.e., 11 points) or above were listed as socially and educationally backward and the rest were treated as 'advanced'.
Precedent	(Emphasised supplied) In paragraph 12.2 of the Report the <ORG> observed, As the unit of identification in the above survey is caste, and caste is a peculiar feature of Hindu society only, the results of the survey cannot have much validity  for non-Hindu communities.
Precedent	Criteria for their identification have been given separately.
Precedent	The <ORG>, thus, on own showing identified socially and educationally backward class amongst Hindus on caste.
Precedent	The criteria for identifying non-Hindus backward classes was stated in paragraph 12.18:  (i) All untouchables converted to any non-Hindu religion; and  (ii) Such occupational communities which are known by the name of their traditional hereditary occupation and whose Hindu counterparts have been included in the list of Hindu OBCs.
Precedent	(Examples : Dhobi, Teli, Dheemar, Nai, Gujar, Kumhar, Lohar, Darji, Badhai, etc.)
Precedent	650.
Precedent	Caste was thus adopted as the sole criteria for determining social and educational backwardness of Hindus.
Precedent	For members of other communities test of conversion from Hinduism was adopted.
Precedent	The <ORG>, even, though noticed that the first <ORG> suffered from inherent defect of identifying on caste proceeded, itself, to do the same.
Precedent	651.
Precedent	In preceding discussion it has been examined, in detai l, as to why caste cannot be the basis of identification of backward class.
Precedent	The constitutional constraint in such identification does not undergo any change because different groups or collectivity identified on caste are huddled together and described as backward class.
Precedent	By grouping together, the cluster of castes does not loose its basic characteristic and continues to be caste.
Precedent	652.
Precedent	No further need be said as whether the <ORG> acted in terms of its reference and whether the identification was constitutionally permissible and legally sound, before it could furnish for any exercise, legislative or executive, was to be undertaken by the government.
Precedent	653.
Precedent	Use of expression, 'nothing in this Article shall prevent <ORG>' in Article 16(4) cannot be read as empowering the <ORG> to make reservation under Article 16(4) on race, religion or caste.
Precedent	It would result in regenerating the communal representation in services infused by Britishers by different orders issued from 1924 to 1946.
Precedent	How such an expression  should be interpreted need not be elaborated.
Precedent	Both the text books and judicial decisions are full of it.
Precedent	To comprehend the real meaning the provision itself, the setting or context in which it has been used, the purpose and background of its enactment should be examined, and interpretational exercise may be resorted to only if there is a compelling necessity for it.
Precedent	In earlier decisions rendered by the <ORG> till sixties Article 16(4) was held to be exception to Article 16(1).
Precedent	But from 1976 onwards it has been understood differently.
Precedent	Today Article 16(1) and 16(4) are understood as part of one and same scheme directed towards promoting equality.
Precedent	Therefore what is destructive of equality for Article 16(1) would apply equally to Article 16(4).
Precedent	The non-obstante clause was to take out absolutism of Article 16(1) and not to destroy the negatism of Article 16(2).
Precedent	654.
Precedent	Rule of statutory construction explained by jurists is to adopt a construction which may not frustrate the objective of enactment and result in neg ation of the objective sought to be achieved.
Precedent	Rigour of its application is even more severe in constitutional interpretation as unlike statute its provisions cannot be amended or repealed easily.
Precedent	Accepting race, religion and caste as the remedy to undo the past evil would be against constitutional spirit, purpose and objectives.
Precedent	As stated earlier this remedy was adopted by the framers of the Constitution for <ORG>.
Precedent	What was not provided for others should be deemed, on principle of interpretation, not to have been approved and accepted.
Precedent	Even if two constructions of the provisions could have been possible, 'the <ORG> must adopt that which will ensure smooth and harmonious working of the Constitution and eschew the other which will lead to absurdity and given rise to practical incovenience'.
Precedent	Since acceptance of caste, race or religion would be destructive of the entire constitutional philosophy and would be contrary to the Preamble of the Constitution it cannot be accepted as a legal method of identification of  backward classes for Article 16(4).
Precedent	655.
Precedent	Would the consequences be different if race, religion or caste etc.
Precedent	are coupled with some other factors?
Precedent	In other words, what is the effect of the word, 'only' in Article 16(2).
Precedent	In the context it has been used it operates, both, as permissive and prohibitive.
Precedent	If is permissive when <ORG> action, legislative or executive, is founded on any ground other than race, religion or caste.
Precedent	Whereas it is prohibitive if it is based exclusively on any of the grounds mentioned in Article 16(2).
Precedent	<CITATION_1695548> .
Precedent	, furnishes best illustration of the former.
Precedent	A notification discriminating between candidates of North Eastern <ORG>s, Tripura, Manipur etc.
Precedent	on the one hand and others for <ORG> examination and exempting them from offering language paper compulsory for everyone was upheld on linguistic concession.
Precedent	When it comes to any <ORG> action on race, religion or caste etc.
Precedent	the word, 'only' mitigates the constitutional prohibition.
Precedent	That is if the action is not founded, exclusively,  or merely, on that which is prohibited then it may not be susceptible to challenge.
Precedent	What does it mean?
Precedent	Can a <ORG> action founded on race, religion, caste etc.
Precedent	be saved under Article 16(2) if it is coupled with any factor relevant or irrelevant.
Precedent	What is to be remembered is that the basic concept pervading the Constitution cannot be permitted to be diluted by taking cover under it.
Precedent	Use of word, 'only' was to avoid any attack on legitimate legislative action by giving it colour of race, religion or caste.
Precedent	At the same time it cannot be utilised by the <ORG> to escape from the prohibition by taking recourse to such measures which are race, religion or caste based by sprinkling it with something other as well.
Precedent	For instance, in <CITATION_173824126> , , where exemption granted to Muslims and Harijans from levy of cost for stationing additional police force was attempted to be defended because the notification was not based, 'only' on caste or religion but because persons belonging to these communities were found by  the <ORG> not to have been guilty of the conduct which necessitated stationing of the police force it was struck down as discriminatory since it could not be shown by the <ORG> that there were no law abiding persons in other communities.
Precedent	Similarly identification of backward class by such factors as dependence of group or collectivity on manual labour, lower age of marriage, poor schooling, living in kuccha house etc.
Precedent	and applying it to caste would be violative of Article 16(2) not only for being caste based but also for violation of Article 14 because it, excludes other communities in which same factors exist only because they are not Hindus.
Precedent	Further the group or collectivity, thus, determined would not be caste coupled with other but on caste and caste alone.
Precedent	656.
Precedent	Today if Article 16(2) is construed as justifying identification of backward class by equalizing them with those castes in which the customary marriage age is lower or majority of whom are living in kuccha houses or a sizeable number is working as  manual labour then tomorrow the identification of backward class amongst other communities where caste does not exist on race or religion coupled with these very considerations cannot be avoided.
Precedent	That would result in making reservation in public services on communal considerations.
Precedent	An interpretation or construction resulting in such catastrophical consequences must be avoided.
Precedent	(12)  657.
Precedent	Backward used in Article 16(4) is wider than socially and educationally used in Article 15(4) and weaker sections used in Article 46.
Precedent	SC/ST are covered in either expression.
Precedent	But same cannot be said for others.
Precedent	Backward, cannot be defined as was, wisely, done by the Constitution makers.
Precedent	It has to emerge as a result of interaction of social and economic forces.
Precedent	It cannot be static.
Precedent	Many of those who were Sudras in 17th and 18th Centuries ceased to be so in 19th and 20th Century due to their educational advancement and social acceptablity.
Precedent	Members of various backward communities, both, in South and North who were moving upward s even before 1950 compare no less in education, status, economic advancement or political achievement with any other class in society.
Precedent	The average lower middle class of Muslims or Christians may not be better educationally or economically and in many cases even socially than the intermediate class of backward class of Sri Paik's list.
Precedent	For instance the bhisties (the water carriers in leather bags) among Muslims.
Precedent	Does Article 340 empowering President to ascertain educational and social backwardness of citizens of this country not include those poor socially degraded and educationally backward.
Precedent	Are they not citizens of this counrty?
Precedent	Could backwardness of Muslims, Christians and Buddhists be recognised for purposes of Article 16(4) only if they were converts from Hinduism or such backwardness for preferential treatment be recognised only if a group or class was Hindu at some time or was occupationally comparable to Hindus.
Precedent	That is if members of other community carry on occupation which is not practised by Hindus , for instance bhisties amongst Muslims, then they cannot be regarded as backward class even if it has been their hereditary occupation and they are socially, educationally and economiclly backward.
Precedent	A Commission appointed under Article 340 by the President is not to identify Hindu, backwards only but the backward class within the territory of India which includes Hindu, Muslim, Sikh or Christian etc.
Precedent	bora and residing in India within meaning of Article 5 of the Constitution.
Precedent	The expression is not only backward class but backward class of citizens.
Precedent	And citizens means all those who are mentioned in Articles 5 and 10 of the Constitution.
Precedent	658.
Precedent	Thus neither from the language of Article 16(4) nor the literal test of interpretation nor from the spirit or purpose of interpretation nor the present - day social setting, warrants construction of the expression backward class as backward caste.
Precedent	Consequently what comes out of the examination from different aspects leads to conclusion that:  (1) Backward class in Article  16(4) cannot be read as backward caste.
Precedent	(2) Expression 'backward class' is of wider import and there being no ambiguity or danger of unintended injustice in giving it its natural meaning it should be understood in its broader and normal sense.
Precedent	(3) Backward class under Article 16(4) is not confined to erstwhile sudras or depressed classes or intermediate backward classes amongst Hindus only.
Precedent	(4) Width of the expression includes in its fold any community Hindu, Muslim, Christian, Sikh, Budha, or Jain etc.
Precedent	as the expression is 'backward class of citizens'.
Precedent	* * * * * 'E'  659.
Precedent	Reason for backwardness or inadequate representation in services of backward Hindus prior to 1950 were caste division, lack of education, poverty, feudalistic frame of society, and occupational helplessness.
Precedent	All these barriers are disappearing.
Precedent	Industrialisation has taken over.
Precedent	Education, through <ORG> effort and due to awareness of its importance, both, statistically and actually has improved.
Precedent	Feudalism died in fifties itself.
Precedent	Even the  <ORG> accepts, this reality .
Precedent	Any identification of backward class for purposes of reservation, therefore, has to be tested keeping in view these factors as the exercise of power is in presenti.
Precedent	Importance of word 'is' in Article 16(4) should not be lost of.
Precedent	Backwardness and inadequacy should exist on the date the reservation is made.
Precedent	Reservation for a group which was educationally, economically and socially backward before 1950 shall not be valid unless the group continues to be backward today.
Precedent	The group should not have suffered only but it should be found to be suffering with such disabilities.
Precedent	If a class or community ceases to be economically and socially backward or even if it is so but is adequately represented then no reservation can be made as it no more continues to be backward even though it may not be adequately represented in service or it may be backward but adequately represented.
Precedent	660.
Precedent	Ethical justification for reverse discrimination or protective benefits or ameliorative measures e manates from the moral of compensating such class or group for the past injustices inflicted on it and for promoting social values.
Precedent	Both these aspects are fully borne out from <ORG>.
Precedent	Anxiety was to uplift the backward classes by enabling them to participate in administration as they had been excluded by few who had monopolised the services.
Precedent	Objective was to change the social face as it shall advance public welfare, by demolishing rigidity of caste, promoting representation of those who till now were kept away thus providing status to them, restoring balance in the society, reducing poverty and increasing distribution of benefits and advantages to one and all.
Precedent	The compensatory principle implies that like an individual a group or class that has remained backward for whatever reason, should be provided every help to overcome the shortcomings but once disadvantage disappears the basis itself must go.
Precedent	For instance there may be four groups of different nature deserving such protection.
Precedent	Some of it may improve and come up in the social stream within short time.
Precedent	Can it be said that since they were kept excluded for hundred years the compensation by way of protective benefits should continue for hundred years.
Precedent	That would be mockery of protective discrimination.
Precedent	The compensation principle, 'makes little sense unless it is involved in connection with assertion that the malignant effects of prior deprivation are still continuing'.
Precedent	The social utility of preferential treatment extended to the disadvantage and weaker too should not be pushed too far on what happened in the past without looking to the present.
Precedent	Such construction of Article 16(4) arises not because of what has been said by some of the American judges but on plain and simple reading of the word, 'is' in the Article.
Precedent	661.
Precedent	An egalitarian society or welfare state wedded to secularism does not and cannot mean a social order in which religion or caste ceases to exist.
Precedent	'India is a seculiar but not an anti-religious state.
Precedent	Article 25 is pride  of our democracy.
Precedent	But that cannot be basis of state activities.
Precedent	May be caste is being exploited for political ends.
Precedent	<NAME> has very graphically described it in Karnataka Third Backward Class Commission Report (1990).
Precedent	And, we have political parties and politicians who, if anything, are realists, fully aware of the deep roots of caste in Indian society and who, far from ignoring it, feed the fire as it were and give caste great importance in the choice of their candidates for election and flaunt the caste of the candidates before the electorate.
Precedent	They preach against caste in public and thrive on it in private.
Precedent	662.
Precedent	Even <ORG> observed that what, 'caste lost on ritual front it gained on political front'.
Precedent	In politics caste may or may not play an important role but politics and constitutional exercise are not the same.
Precedent	A candidate may secure a ticket on caste considerations but if he or his agent or any person with his consent or his agent's consent appeals to vote or refrain from voting  on ground of religion, race or caste then he is guilty of corrupt practice under Section 123(3) of the Representation of People Act and his election is liable to be set aside.
Precedent	Thus caste, race or religion are prohibited even in political process.
Precedent	What cannot furnish basis for exercise of electoral right and is constitutionally prohibited from being exercised by the <ORG> cannot furnish valid basis for constitutional functioning under Article 16(4).
Precedent	Utilization of caste as the basis for purpose of determination of backward class of citizens is thus constitutionally invalid and even ethically and morally not permissible.
Precedent	Existence of caste in the past and present, its continuance in future cannot be denied but insistence that since it is being practised or observed for political purpose even though unfortunately it should be the basis for identification of backwardness in services is not only robbing the Constitution of the fresh look it promised and guaranteed but would result in perpetuating a system under u gly weight of which the society had bent earlier.
Precedent	Thus, (i) backwardness and inadequacy of representation in service must exist on the date the reservation is being made.
Precedent	(ii) Any past injustice which entitles a group for protective discrimination must on principle of compensation or social justice be continuing on the date when reservation is being made.
Precedent	* * * * * 'F'   663.
Precedent	'It is easier to give power but difficult to give wisdom'.
Precedent	Dr. <NAME> quoted this <NAME>'s thought in the Constituent Assembly Debate and exhorted 'let us prove by our conduct that we have not only the power but also the wisdom to carry with us all sectors of the country which is bound to lead us to unity'.
Fact	How to effectuate this wisdom?
Fact	For Article 16(4) how to determine who can be legally considered to be backward class of citizens?
RatioOfTheDecision	The answer is simple.
RatioOfTheDecision	By adopting, constitutionally permissible methodology of identification irrespective of their race, religion or caste.
RatioOfTheDecision	The difficulty, however, arises in finding out the criteria.
RatioOfTheDecision	Although the work should normally be left to be undertaken by the <ORG> as the courts are ill equipped for such exercise due to lack of data, necessary expertise and relevant material but with development of role of courts from mere, 'superintend and supervise' to legitimate constitutional affirmative decision, this <ORG> is not only duty bound but constitutionally obliged to lay down principles for guidance for those who are entrusted with this responsibility, with a sense of duty towards the country as the occasion demands never more than now, but with remotest intention to interfere with legislative, or executive process.
Precedent	What the <ORG> should remember is that the basic values of constitutionalism guaranting judicial independence is to enable the courts to discharge their duty without being guided by any philosophy as judicial interpretation, gives better protection than the political branches to the weak and outnumbered, to minorities and unpopular individuals, to the inadequately represented in the poli tical process.
Precedent	664.
Precedent	Before doing so it is necessary to be stated, at the outset, that identification of backward classes for purposes of different States may not furnish safe and sound basis for including all such groups or collectivities for reservation in services under the <ORG>.
Precedent	Reason is that local conditions play major part in such exercise.
Precedent	For instance habitation in hills of U.P.
Precedent	was upheld as valid basis for identifying backwardness.
Precedent	Same may not be true of residents of hills in other States.
Precedent	Otherwise entire population of Kashmir may have to be treated as backward.
Precedent	In Kerala State most of the Muslims are identified as backward.
Precedent	Can this be valid basis for other States.
Precedent	Even <ORG> noticed that some castes backward in one State are forward in others.
Precedent	If State list of every State is adopted as valid for central services it is bound to create confusion.
Precedent	One of the apparent abuse inherent in such inclusion is that it is apt to encourage paper mobility of citizens from a State where such  class or caste is not backward to the <ORG> where it is so identified.
Precedent	This apart such inclusion may suffer from constitutional infirmity.
Precedent	Many groups or collectivities in different <ORG>s are continuing or have been included in the <ORG> list due to various considerations political or otherwise.
Precedent	<ORG> of Karnataka is its best example.
Precedent	Commission after commission beginning from <ORG>, <ORG> and <ORG> despite having found that some of the castes ceased to be backward they continue in the list due to their political pressure and economic power.
Precedent	<NAME> 'Economic and Political Weekly' Vol.
Precedent	26 (1991) p. 601 in 'Social Backwardness and Politics of Reservations', has pointed out, 'Among the sudras there are peasant castes, artisan castes and nomadic castes.
Precedent	Subjective perception of one's position in the 'varna' system varies and changes from time to time, place to place and context to context.
Precedent	For instance, the Patidars of Gujarat were considered sudras a few decades  ago, but not they call themselves vaishyas, and are acknowledged as such by others.
Precedent	It is significant that they are not have-nots.
Precedent	Similar is the case of Vokkaligas and Lingayats of Karnataka, Reddies and Kammas of Andhra Pradesh, Marathas of Maharashtra and to some extent Yadavas of Bihar.'
Precedent	Yet these castes or group have been identified as backward class in their <ORG>.
Precedent	Whether such inclusion on political, economic and social condition is justified in <ORG> list or not but inclusion of a group or collectivity in list of socially and educationlly backward classes, which is a term narrower and different than backward class for services under the <ORG> without proper identification only on <ORG> list may not be valid.
Precedent	For services under the <ORG>, therefore, some principle may have to be evolved which may be of universal application to members of every community and which may be adopted by <ORG>, as well, after adjusting it with prevalent local conditions.
Precedent	665.
Precedent	Ours is a country comprising of various communit ies.
Precedent	Each community follows different religion.
Precedent	Centuries of historical togetherness has influenced each other.
Precedent	Caste system which is peculiar to Hindus infiltrated even amongst Muslims, Christians, Sikhs or others although it has no place in their religion.
Precedent	The Encyclopedia Americana International Edition describes the development thus, All important communities, including the Muslims., Christians, and Sikhs, have some sort of caste scheme.
Precedent	These schemes are patterned after the Hindu system, since most of these people originally came from Hindu stock.
Precedent	The large-scale conversions that have been going on for centuries have modified Indian caste society.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus traditional Hindu communal and connubial rituals and emphasis on inherited social status or rank though generally rejected in the Islamic or Christian religious ethic, nevertheless operate on social plain in these societies in India.
RatioOfTheDecision	In India social rites and customs very from region to region rather than from religion to religion.
RatioOfTheDecision	Among the Muslims, the S ayids, <NAME>, <NAME>, and Momin, among others, function as exclusive endogamous caste groups.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Christians are divided into a number of groups, including the Chaldean Syrians, Jacobite Syrians, Latin Catholics, Marthom Syrians, Syrian Catholics, and Protestants.
RatioOfTheDecision	Each of these groups practices endogamy.
RatioOfTheDecision	Among the Catholics, the Syrian Romans and the Latin Romans generally do not intermarry.
RatioOfTheDecision	The Christians have not wholly discarded the idea of food restrictions and pollution by lower caste members.
Precedent	When lower caste Hindus were converted to Christianity a generation or two ago, they were not allowed to sit with high caste Christians in <ORG>, and separate churches were erected for them.
Precedent	666.
Precedent	On the social plain therefore there has been lack of mobility from one group to other.
Precedent	Amongst Hindus it has been more marked.
Precedent	Inter-se discrimination has been worse.
RatioOfTheDecision	Untouchables prior to 1950 have been victims of social persecutions not ony by the twice born but even the socalled intermediate backward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	But wha t appears to be common in each community is that the caste divide is more or less occupational based.
RatioOfTheDecision	A washerman or a barber, a milkman or an agriculturist, are all known among Hindus by castes and amongst others by occupation.
RatioOfTheDecision	In fact they are all occupational.
RatioOfTheDecision	Very genesis of <ORG> was occupational.
RatioOfTheDecision	According to <NAME>, castes are special form of social classes, 'which in tendency at least are present in every society.
RatioOfTheDecision	Castes differ from social classes, however, in that they have emerged into social consciousness to the point that custom and law attempt their rigid and permanent separation from one another'.... 'The jatis which developed later and which continued to grow in number have their economic significance; they are for the most part occupational groups and, in the traditional village economy, the caste system largely provides the machinery for the exchange of goods and services.
RatioOfTheDecision	But these rigid stratifications are breaking today.
Fact	The social inter-se barriers are rapidly disappearing.
Fact	<NAME> es are fast changing.
RatioOfTheDecision	In fact many of the backward classes as observed by Sri <NAME> in his separate note to <ORG> 'co-existed since times immemorial with upper castes and had therefore some scope to imbibe better association and what all its connotes'.
RatioOfTheDecision	Take for instance the list of the 'Intermediate Backward Class' where traditional occupation, according to Sri <NAME> has been, 'agriculture, market gardening, betal leaves, grovers, pastoral activities, village industries like artisans, tailors, dyers and weavers, petty business-cum-agricultural activities, heralding, temple service, toddy selling, oil mongering, combating, astrology etc.
RatioOfTheDecision	etc.'.
RatioOfTheDecision	Their backwardness has been primarily economic or educational.
RatioOfTheDecision	Mobility, too, occupational or professional has not been very rigid.
RatioOfTheDecision	An agriculturist or an artisan, a dyer or weaver had the occupational freedom of moving in any direction.
RatioOfTheDecision	Consideration for marriage or social customs may be different.
RatioOfTheDecision	But that prevails in every strata of society.
RatioOfTheDecision	One  sect of a caste or community Hindu or Muslim, or even Christian, forward or backward does not prefer marrying in another sect what to say of caste.
RatioOfTheDecision	But these considerations are not relevant for identifying backward class for public employment.
RatioOfTheDecision	Lack of education, at least among so-called intermediate backward classes, was more due to personal volition than social ostracisation.
RatioOfTheDecision	Historical social backwardness has already been taken care of by providing reservation to <ORG> and empowering President to include any group or collectivity found to be suffering from such disability.
RatioOfTheDecision	Same yardstick cannot be applied for socially and educationally backward class for whom the President has been empowered to appoint a <ORG> and who only after identification are to be deemed to be included as SC and ST by virtue of Article 338(10).
RatioOfTheDecision	From the preceding discussion it is clear that identification of such class cannot be caste based.
RatioOfTheDecision	Nor it can be founded, only, on economic considerations as 'Mere poverty' cannot be the t est of backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	With these two negative considerations stemming out of constitutional constraints two positive considerations, equally important and basic in nature flow from principle of constitutional construction one that the effort should, primarily, be directed towards finding out a criteria which must apply uniformly to citizens of every community, second that the benefit should reach the needy.
Precedent	Various combinations excluding and including caste as relevant consideration have been discussed in different decisions which need not be mentioned as occasion to examine social and educational backwardness in public services and that also in union services never arose.
Precedent	667.
Precedent	In sub-paragraph (ii) of paragraph 12.8 extracted earlier <ORG> recommended occupational identification for non-Hindus if the community was traditionally known to carry on the hereditary occupation of their counterpart amongst Hindus and included in the test of OBC.
Precedent	The <ORG> thus recognised occupational divide amo ng Hindus.
Precedent	If occupation amongst Hindus can be basis for identification of backwardness among non-Hindus then why cannot it furnish basis for identification amongst Hindus itself.
Precedent	668.
Precedent	Ideal and wise method, therefore, would be to mark out various occupations, which on the lower level in many cases amongst Hindus would be the caste itself.
Precedent	Find out their social acceptability and educational standard.
Precedent	Weight them in the balance of economic conditions.
Precedent	Result would be backward class of citizens needing genuine protective umbrella.
Precedent	Group or collectivity which may thus emerge may be members of one or the other community.
Precedent	Advantage of occupational based identification would be that it shall apply uniformly irrespective of race, religion and caste.
Precedent	Reason for accepting occupation based identification is that prior to 1950 Sudras amongst Hindus were all those who were not twice born.
Precedent	Amongst them there was vertical and occupational divisions.
Precedent	No similar to hierarchy existed amongst Muslims.
Precedent	Same is true of other co mmunities.
Precedent	Sri <NAME> narrated a list of, 'intermediate backward classes' and 'depressed backward classes'.
Precedent	It may not be exhaustive.
Precedent	But it is indicative that different categories of persons are, normally, known by occupation they carry.
Precedent	'Castes, therefore, are special form of classes which in tendency are present in every society'.
Precedent	It was said by Lord <NAME> long back for America that classes way not be divided, for political purposes into upper and lower and richer and poorer, 'but according to their respective occupation they follow'.
Precedent	Class according to <NAME> may get formed due to various reasons, 'war, the institution of private property, biological characteristic, the division of labour'.
Precedent	And, 'Even today, indeed though less regularly than in the past class tends to determine occupation rather than occupational class.
Precedent	So is the case in our society.
Precedent	It is immaterial if caste has given rise to occupation or vice versa.
Precedent	In either case occupation can be the best starting point constitutionally permissible and  legally valid for determination of backwardness.
Precedent	669.
Precedent	For instance, priests either in Hindus or Mullahs in Muslims or Bishops or Padris amongst Christians or Granthi in Sikhs are considered to be at the top of hierarchal system.
Precedent	They cannot be considered to be backward in any community not because of their religion but the nature of occupation.
Precedent	Similarly the untouchables became outcaste due to nature of the job they performed.
Precedent	On lower level whether it is barber or tailor, washerman or milkman, agricultural class or artisan they are a group or class who can be identified in any community.
Precedent	Identifying them by caste may mean that a Muslim or Christian who for generations has been carrying on same occupation as his counterpart amongst Hindus cannot be identified as backward class.
Precedent	And if it is done then for Hindus it would be caste based whereas for others occupational.
Precedent	How far that would be legal and constitutional is one matter but if the yardstick of occupation is applied to every community the identificatio n would be uniform without exclusion of any.
Precedent	For instance weavers or washerman.
Precedent	They may be both Hindus and Muslims.
Precedent	It would be unfair to include Hindu washerman and exclude Muslim washerman.
Precedent	670.
Precedent	Having adopted occupation as the starting point next step should be to ascertain the social acceptability.
Precedent	A lawyer, a teaching and a doctor of any community whether he is a teacher of primary school or <ORG>, a Vaid or Hakim practising in the village or a professor in Medical college always commands social respect.
Precedent	Similarly social status amongst those who perform lower job depends on the nature of occupation.
Precedent	A person carrying on scavenging became an untouchable whereas others who were as lower as untouchable in the order became depressed.
Precedent	For instance coboler.
Precedent	Same did not apply to those who carried on better occupation.
Precedent	A person having landed property and carrying on agricultural occupation did not in social hierarchy command lesser respect than the one carrying on same occupation belonging to higher cast e. But backwardness should be traditional.
Precedent	For instance only those washerman or tailor should be considered backward who have been carrying on this occupation for generations and not the modern dry cleaner or fashion tailOrs.
Precedent	If the collectivity satisfies both the tests then apply the test of education.
Precedent	What standard of education should be adopted should be concern of the <ORG>.
Precedent	Existence of, both, that is social and educational backwardness for a group or collectivity is indicated by Article 15(4) itself.
Precedent	Use of such expression was purposive.
Precedent	Mere educational or social backwardness would not have been sufficient as it would have enlarged the field thus frustrating the very purpose of the amendment.
Precedent	That is why it was observed in Balaji that the concept of backwardness was intended, 'to be relative in the sense that any class who is backward in relation to the most advanced classes should be included in it.
Precedent	And the purpose of amendment could be achieved if backwardness under Article 15(4) was understood as co mprising of social and educational backwardness.
Precedent	It is not either social or educational, but it is both social and educational'.
Precedent	Reading the expression disjunctively and permitting inclusion of either socially or educationally backward class of citizens would defeat the very purpose.
Precedent	For instance some of the so-called higher castes who by nature of their occupation or caste have been accepted by society to be socially advanced may enter because of the group or collectivity having been educationally backward.
Precedent	Many agricultural occupationists both in South and North have chosen to remain educationally backward even though by virtue of their landed property they have always been compared to any higher class.
Precedent	Can such persons be permitted to take benefit of such benign measures.
Precedent	Not on the language, purpose and objective of these provisions.
Precedent	671.
Precedent	After applying these tests the economic criteria or the means test should be applied.
Precedent	Poverty is the prime cause of all backwardness.
Precedent	It generates social and educationa l backwardness.
Precedent	But wealth or economic affluence cuts across all.
Precedent	A wealthy man irrespective of caste or community needs no crutches.
Precedent	Not in 1990 when money more than social status and education have become the index.
Precedent	Therefore, even if a group or collectivity is not educated or even socially backward but otherwise rich and affluent then it cannot be considered backward.
Precedent	There is no dearth of class or group who by the nature of the occupation they have been pursuing are economically well off.
Precedent	Including such groups would be doing injustice to others.
Precedent	Thus occupation should furnish the starting point of determination of backward class.
Precedent	And if in ultimate analysis any Hindu caste is found to be occupationally, socially, educationally and economically backward it should be regarded as eligible for benefit under Article 16(4) because it would be within constitutional sanction.
Precedent	(2)  672.
Precedent	Identification alone does not entitle a group or class to be entitled for protective benefits.
Precedent	Such group or collectivity should  be inadequately represented.
Precedent	Use of such words as a equate or inadequate are no doubt wide and vague and their meaning has to be gathered, 'largely on the point of view from which the facts may be proved are reconsidered'.
Precedent	But from the purpose and objective of Article 16(4) a collectivity or group which is found to be backward cannot qualify for being included if it is adequately represented.
Precedent	Word 'any' has great significance.
Precedent	In wider sense it extends to and includes all group or collectivity, which is as much 'any' backward class as any singularity.
Precedent	In the larger sense comprising of entire plurality it continues and may continue but in the limited sense the group may keep on getting in and out depending on continuance of those conditions which entitled it to be determined as backward.
Precedent	A government of a <ORG> or <ORG> may on evaluation after five or ten years direct a group or collectivity to be excluded from the list of backward classes if it finds it adequately represented.
Precedent	What is adequa te representation is of course the primary concern of the government.
Precedent	But the exercise should be objective.
Precedent	For instance in some States it was found by <ORG> appointed by their governments that certain castes were adequately represented.
Precedent	Yet because of extraneous reasons the government had to bow and include them in the list of backward classes.
Precedent	Such inclusion is a fraud of constitutional power.
Precedent	Any citizen has a right to challenge and court has obligation to strike it down by directing exclusion of such group from the backward class.
Precedent	Inadequacy provides jurisdiction not only for exercise of power but its continuance as well.
Precedent	If that itself ceases to exist the power cannot be continued to be exercised.
Precedent	Where power is coupled with duty the condition precedent must exist for valid exercise of power.
Precedent	Mere identification of collectivity or group by a <ORG> cannot clothe the government to exercise the power unless it further undertakes the exercise of determining if such group or collectivity is adequat ely or inadequately represented.
Precedent	The exercise is mandatory not in the larger sense alone but in the narrower sense as well.
Precedent	* * * * * 'G'   673.
Precedent	More important that determination of backward class is the proportion in which reservation can be done as it is not only a social or economic problem or the question of empowering but a constitutional and legal issue which calls for serious deliberation.
Precedent	Although political statesmanship of the framers of the Constitution intended to confine it to 'minority of seats' the judicial pragmatism raised it 'broadly and generally' to less than 50% in Balaji and not beyond that in <CITATION_1466728> .
Precedent	Effect of these two decisions was that the reserved and non-reserved seats both for purposes of admission in educational institution under Article 15(4) and for appointment and posts in Article 16(4) were divided in half and half.
Precedent	But once the reservation climate spread in the country's environment it took over the political set up of different States to provide for reservation  for different groups for different reasons.
Precedent	And legal justification for such reservation was provided for by the courts, either on the touchstone of Article 14 being a reasonable classification or under Article 16(1) as preferential treatment for disadvantaged groups.
Precedent	If in <CITATION_195765> , , the provision for government nominees in medical colleges was upheld, 'as the government which bears the financial burden of running medical colleges' could not be, 'denied the right to decide from what sources the admission will be made' then <CITATION_1276295> , , did not find it unreasonable to extend the principle of preferential treatment, of socially and educationally backward in Article 15(4 ), to children of political sufferers as 'it would not in any way be improper if that principle were to be applied to those who are handicapped but do not fall under Article 15(4)'.
Precedent	The reservation in favour of wards of defence personnel was upheld as a reasonable classification in <CITATION_467233> , AIR 1966 Mysore 40 as  the reservation was in national interest.
Precedent	Result of such extensions and justification was multiplication of categories and withdrawal of more and more seats and posts from open competition.
Precedent	And when observations were made in <NAME> that 50% was, 'a rule of caution' and, 'percentage of reservation in proportion to population did not violate Article 16(4 )', a virtual go by was given by various states to the balancing equality created by courts and reservations were made much beyond 50% and <ORG> had no option but to uphold them.
Precedent	Thus the combined effect of these principles, developed by <NAME> and <NAME>, on the one hand and <NAME>, <NAME> and <NAME> on the other was that reservation up to 50% under Articles 15(4) and 16(4) and up to, 'reasonable extent' under Article 16(1).
Precedent	Under one it became SC/ST and BC and under the other wards of Military and Defence personnel, <NAME> v. State of Haryana , Political, sufferers, sportsman, Children of MISA, State of Karnataka v. <ORG> R (1964) 2 Kerala p. 53 and <CITATION_253270> .
Precedent	, detenue etc.
Precedent	Is this sound either constitutionally or legally or socially?
Precedent	(2)  674.
Statute	Article 16(1 ), (2) and (4) is extracted below:  16.
Statute	Equality of opportunity in matters of public employment-  (1) There shall be equality of opportunity for all citizens in matters relating to employment or appointment to any office under the <ORG>.
Statute	(2) No citizen shall, on grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex, descent, place of birth, residence or any of them, be ineligible for, or discriminated against in respect of, any employment or office under the <ORG>.
Precedent	(4) Nothing in this article shall prevent the <ORG> from making any provision for the reservation of appointments or posts in favour of any backward class of citizens which, in the opinion of the <ORG>, is not adequately represented in the services under the <ORG>.'
Precedent	675.
Precedent	Originally this Article as introduced in <ORG> was Article 10 and its Sub- article (3) identical to Sub- article (4) of Ar ticle 16 provided for reservation, 'in favour of any class of citizens'.
Precedent	It was <ORG> which qualified the expression, 'class of citizens' by adding the word 'backward' before it.
Precedent	Effect of this addition was that clause got narrowed and the reservation could be made only for those class of citizens who could be grouped as backward.
Precedent	Putting it the other way the framers of the Constitution decided against expansive reservation which under original proposal could have extended to any class of citizens.
Precedent	What was thus consciously and deliberately given up by exercising the option in favour of only those class of citizens who could be identified as backward then reservation in favour of any other class of citizens cannot legitimately and legally be accepted as valid.
Precedent	Extending it to other class of citizens under cover of reasonable classification would be constitutional distortion.
Precedent	What should be deemed to be prohibited in the light of historical background cannot be brought back from the backdoor o n principle developed by the American courts under Equal Protection Clause as they had to rise to the occasion due to absence of a provision like Article 16(4 ), and the fractured interpretation put in the <ORG> cases, which eroded the very foundation of Equal Protective clause 'mainly intended for the benefit of Negro freedom'.
Precedent	676.
Precedent	Reservation co-related with population was not accepted even by <ORG>.
Precedent	On plain construction inadequacy of representation cannot be the measure of reservation.
Precedent	That is creative of jurisdiction only.
RatioOfTheDecision	In fact Dr. <NAME>'s illustration while persuading all sections to accept the drafting committee proposal is very instructive.
RatioOfTheDecision	Supposing, for instance, reservations were made for a community or a collection of communities, the total of which came to something like 70 per cent of the total posts under the <ORG> and only 30 per cent are retained as the unreserved.
RatioOfTheDecision	Could anybody say that the reservation of 30 per cent as open to general competition would  be satisfactory from the point of view of giving effect to the first principle, namely, that there shall be equality of opportunity?
RatioOfTheDecision	It cannot be in my judgment.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore the seats to be reserved, if the reservation is to be consistent with Sub-clause (1) Article 10 , must be confined to a minority of seats.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is then only that the first principle could find its place in the Constitution and effective in operation.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even otherwise if the framers would have intended to provide for reservation to extent of backwardness of the population it would have been simpler to use the expression, 'in proportion to it' after the word 'backward class of citizens' and before 'is not' adequately represented.
Precedent	Article 16(4) then would have read as under:-  Nothing in this Article shall prevent the <ORG> from making any provision for the reservation of appointments or posts in favour of any backward class of citizens in proportion to it is not adequately represented in the services under the <ORG>.
Precedent	No rule of interpretation i n absence of express or implied indication permits such substituted reading.
Precedent	677.
Precedent	In <NAME>, (supra 46) <NAME>, introduced concept of proportional equality from two American decisions <NAME> v. <NAME> 351 US (12) and <NAME> v. <ORG> 383 US 663 [1966].
RatioOfTheDecision	None of the decisions were concerned with affirmative action.
RatioOfTheDecision	The one related to payment of charges for translation of manuscript in appeal and other with levy of poll tax at uniform rate indiscriminately.
RatioOfTheDecision	In view of clear phraseology and the background of enactment of Article 16(4) any interpretation of it on ratio of American decisions cannot be of any help.
RatioOfTheDecision	Our Constitution does not approve of proportional representation either in services or even in <ORG> as is illustrated by Article 331 of the Constitution which empowers the President to nominate not more than two members of the Anglo-Indian community to <ORG>, irrespective of their population, if they are not adequately represented.
RatioOfTheDecision	Same is the theme of Dr.  <NAME>'s speech, in Constituent Assembly, extracted earlier.
RatioOfTheDecision	For the same reasons the observation of <NAME>, J. in <NAME> (supra), ...Decided cases 01 this Court have no doubt laid down that the percentage of reservation should not exceed 50%.
RatioOfTheDecision	As I read the authorities, this is, however, a rule of caution and does not exhaust all categories.
RatioOfTheDecision	Suppose for instance a <ORG> has a large number of backward classes of citizens which constitute 80% of the population and the Government, in order to give them proper representation, reserves 80% of the jobs for them, can it be said that the percentage of reservation is bad and violates the permissible limits of Clause (4) of Article 16.
RatioOfTheDecision	The answer must necessarily be in the negative.
RatioOfTheDecision	cannot be accepted as correct construction of Article 16(4).
Precedent	True as observed by <NAME>, J., in <NAME> (Supra) and <NAME>, J., in <NAME> (supra) that there is no consitutional provision restricting reservation to 50% but with profound respect, the de bates in <ORG>, the provisions in the Constitution do not support the construction of Article 16(4) as empowering government to reserve posts for backward class of citizens in proportion to their population.
Precedent	Any construction of Article 16(4) cannot be divorced without taking into account Article 16(1).
Precedent	Equality in services has been balanced by providing equal opportunity to every citizen at the same time empowering the <ORG> to take protective measure for the backward class of citizens who are not adequately represented.
Precedent	This balancing of equality cannot be lost sight of while interpreting these provisions.
Precedent	Since there is no clear indication either way the role of the courts become both important and responsible, by interpreting the provision reasonably and with common sense so as to carry out the objective of its enactment.
