Precedent	And the purpose was to enable the backward class of citizens to share the power if they were not adequately represented but not to grant proportional representation, a  typical British concept rejected by our Bounding Fathers.
Precedent	(4)  678.
RatioOfTheDecision	Equality has various shades.
RatioOfTheDecision	Its understanding and application have been shaped by social, economic and political conditions prevailing in the society.
RatioOfTheDecision	The reigning philosophy since 18th century has been the <ORG>'s responsibility to reduce disparities amongst various sections of the population and promoting a just and social order in which benefits and advantages are evenly distributed.
RatioOfTheDecision	To achieve this basic objective various theories have been advanced from time to time.
RatioOfTheDecision	The formal equality advanced by <NAME> that equals should be treated equally and unequals unequally was as much result of social and economic conditions as the <NAME> theory of justice or the <NAME>'s concepts of right of all to treatment as equals.
RatioOfTheDecision	Liberty and right to equality taken individually may appear to pull in different directions.
RatioOfTheDecision	But viewed as part of justice and fairness the two are the primary tenets of modern egalitarian society.
RatioOfTheDecision	The real difficulty is tra nslating them into practical working.
RatioOfTheDecision	The American concept of 'equal but separate' doctrine is the best illustration of distance between theory and practice of equal protection.
RatioOfTheDecision	The recognition and realisation that neither all men are equal nor are the circumstances in which they are born or grow are same gave rise to classification and grouping of persons similarly situated and extending them equal or same treatment.
RatioOfTheDecision	But the classification has to be reasonable and rational bearing a just relation with the legislative purpose and should not be invidious or arbitrary.
RatioOfTheDecision	In our constitutional scheme the classification in matters of employment or appointment in the services has been done constitutionally.
RatioOfTheDecision	From the entire class of all citizens any backward class has been classified for beneficial or benign treatment.
RatioOfTheDecision	The legislature or executive therefore cannot transgress it.
RatioOfTheDecision	Since the Constitution treats all citizens alike for purposes of employment except those who fall under Article 16(4) any further classifica tion of grouping for reservation would be constitutionally invalid.
RatioOfTheDecision	No legislative exercise can transcendent the constitutional barrier.
Precedent	For valid classification legislature or executive measures must be co-related with legislative purpose or objective.
Precedent	Once the Constitution itself unfolded the purpose of achieving the goal of equality by permitting reservation for backward classes, only, any further reservation being beyond constitutional purpose would be impermissible and per se invalid.
Precedent	679.
Precedent	Abstract equality is neither the theme nor philosophy of our Constitution.
Precedent	Real equality through practical means is the avowed objective.
Precedent	Atoning for the past injustices on backward classes through Constitutional mechanism was morality raised to legal plain.
Precedent	Admonition to State not to deny equality before law or equal protection of laws found on sound public policy, is in reality the measure of fundamental right which every person enjoys.
Precedent	But, principle of the equal protection of law does not mean that, 'every law mus t have universal application to all persons who are not by nature, attainment or circumstance, in the same position', <NAME> v. <ORG> and Anr.
Precedent	and the varying needs of different classes of persons require special treatment.
Precedent	Principle of reasonable classification was developed by theorists and courts to enable <ORG> to function effectively by classifying reasonably.
Precedent	But the theory developed by <NAME> and <NAME> that equal Protection clause really dealt with the problem with the relation of two classes to each other one of individuals possessing the definite trait and the other of individuals tainted by the mischief at which the law aims said to be, 'the first comprehensive analysis of the Equal Protection Clause' may be applicable while considering the scope of Article 14 but once the Constitution makers treated employment in services separately by creating fundamental right in favour of all citizens in pursuance of the ideal of P reamble to secure to all its citizens equality in opportunity and status then it has to be understood in its own perspective.
Precedent	Various sub-articles of Article 16 specially Clause 4 indicates constitutional classification and creation of two classes one dealt with in Article 16(1) and the other in Article 16(4).
Precedent	Principle of reasonable classification for purposes of creating another class or planting one class in another would be constitutionally infirm.
Precedent	680.
RatioOfTheDecision	All the same the legislative anxiety of affirmative action by preferential treatment to disadvantaged group lagging behind may not be doubted.
RatioOfTheDecision	Difference between reservation and preferential treatment is that in one a group or class or collectivity is separately provided for and the competition is amongst them only.
RatioOfTheDecision	Whereas in preferential treatment the collectivity is part of the same group but it is permitted some weightage due to social, economic or any justifiable reason.
RatioOfTheDecision	For purposes of achieving equality by result Article 16 creates two compartments , one general and the other reserved and then both are paired together.
RatioOfTheDecision	But preference is available in the same compartment.
RatioOfTheDecision	Validity of one depends on constitutional sanction whereas the second has to stand on test of reasonableness.
RatioOfTheDecision	For instance the reservation of backward class cannot be assailed as being violative of constitutional guarantee whereas preferential treatment can be upheld only if it is reasonable with the nexus it seeks to achieve.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 16 unlike Article 14 is a positive right of equal opportunity.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, any preferential treatment shall have to be tested in the light of the constitutional objective the Article seeks to achieve.
RatioOfTheDecision	That is what is its natural, operation and effect.
RatioOfTheDecision	Reservation made for backward class of citizens achieves the constitutional goal of achieving equality of opportunity of all.
RatioOfTheDecision	Same cannot be said for others.
RatioOfTheDecision	Any reservation for any other class would be, as already explained, contrary to constitutional objective thus invalid.
Precedent	Wards of military personnel or pol itical sufferers or any other class cannot be extended the benefit of benign discrimination as that would be violative of equality of opportunity.
Precedent	In absence of any objective or purpose discernible from the Constitution the <ORG> action would be liable to be struck down for absence of necessary co-relation between constitutional purpose and its means.
Precedent	Nexus such as national purpose or principle contained in Article 15(4) would not justify such action.
Precedent	Even preferential treatment by way of weightage may be permissible in very limited cases and any such measure would be liable to strict judicial scrutiny.
Precedent	Principle of Article 14 of reasonable classification may be relevant only to limited extent as to whether it is backed by reason and is justified but since it has to be tested further on touchstone on Article 16(1) the reasonable classification must be so tailored as not to contravene the right to equal opportunity.
Precedent	681.
RatioOfTheDecision	No provision of reservation or preference can be so vigorously pursued as to destroy the  very concept of equality.
RatioOfTheDecision	Benign discrimination or protection cannot under any constitutional system itself become principle clause.
RatioOfTheDecision	Equality is the rule.
RatioOfTheDecision	Protection is the exception.
RatioOfTheDecision	Exception cannot exhaust the rule itself.
RatioOfTheDecision	True no restriction was placed on size of reservation.
RatioOfTheDecision	But reason was the consensus understanding that it was for minority of seats.
RatioOfTheDecision	That apart the reservation under Article 16(4) cannot be taken in isolation.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 16(1) and Article 16(4) being part of same objective and goal, any policy of reservation must constitutionally withstand the test of inter action between the two.
RatioOfTheDecision	In this perspective reservation cannot be except for, 'minority of seats'.
RatioOfTheDecision	Our founding fathers were aware that such policies were bound to have political overtones.
RatioOfTheDecision	Various considerations may result in influencing the political decision.
RatioOfTheDecision	That is why their validity in the constitutional framework was left to the courts.
RatioOfTheDecision	Observations by Dr. <NAME> in <ORG> are quite pertinent, If the local  Government included in this category of reservations such a large number of seats; I think one could very well go to <ORG> and <ORG> and say that the reservation is of such a magnitude that the rule regarding equality of opportunity has been destroyed and the court will then come to the conclusion whether the local Government or <ORG> has acted in a reasonable and prudent manner.
RatioOfTheDecision	Since this Court has consistently held that the reservation under Articles 15(4) and 16(4) should not exceed 50% and the States and the Union have by and large accepted this as correct it should be held as constitutional prohibition and any reservation beyond 50% would liable to be struck down.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore,  (i) Reservation under Article 16(4) should in no case exceed 50%;  (ii) No reservation can be made for any class other than backward class either under Article 16(1) or 16(4).
RatioOfTheDecision	(iii) Preferential treatment in shape of weightage etc.
RatioOfTheDecision	can be given to those who are covered in Article 16(1) but t hat too has to be very restrictive.
RatioOfTheDecision	'H'  682.
RatioOfTheDecision	Promotion is the most sensitive branch of service jurisprudence.
RatioOfTheDecision	Although its purpose is manifold but the principle objective is, 'to secure the best possible incumbents for the higher positions while maintaining the morale of the whole organisation' as it not only, 'serves the public interest' but is founded on the inherent principle that the higher one moves the greater is the responsibility he assumes.
RatioOfTheDecision	683.
RatioOfTheDecision	Manner and method of promotion is usually linked with the nature of posts, if it is selection or non-selection.
RatioOfTheDecision	Reservation, for <ORG>/ST, has been extended, to both, by this <ORG> in Rangachari and Soshit Karamchari respectively reiterated in <CITATION_1289642> and <CITATION_1685522> .
RatioOfTheDecision	.
Precedent	In Rangachari it was held, 'The condition precedent may refer either to numerical inadequacy of representation in the services or even to the qualitative inadequacy of representation'.
Precedent	In the context the expression, 'adequately represented imports consideration of size as we ll as values, numbers as well as the nature of appointments'.
Precedent	684.
RatioOfTheDecision	But, inadequacy of representation is creative of jurisdiction only.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is not measure of backwardness.
RatioOfTheDecision	That is why less rigorous test or lesser marks and competition amongst the class of unequals at the point of entry has been approved both by this <ORG> and American courts.
RatioOfTheDecision	But a student admitted to a medical or engineering college is further not granted relaxation in passing the examinations.
RatioOfTheDecision	In fact this has been explained as valid basis in American decisions furnishing justification for racial admissions on lower percentage.
RatioOfTheDecision	Rationale appears to be that every-one irrespective of the source of entry being subjected to same test neither efficiency is effected nor the equality is disturbed.
RatioOfTheDecision	After entry in service the class is one that of employees.
Precedent	If the social scar of backwardness is carried even, thereafter the entire object of equalisation stands frustrated.
Precedent	No further classification amongst employees would be justified as is not done am ongst students.
Precedent	685.
Precedent	Constitutional, legal or moral basis for protective discrimination is redressing identifiable backward class for historical injustice.
Precedent	That is they are today, what they would not have been but for the victimisation.
Precedent	Remedying this and to balance the unfair advantage gained by others is the constitutional responsibility.
Precedent	But once the advantaged and disadvantaged the so-called forward and backward, enter into the same stream then the past injustice stands removed.
Precedent	And the length of service, the seniority in cadre of one group to be specific the forward group is not as a result of any historical injustice or undue advantage earned by his forefather or discrimination against the backward class, but because of the years of service that are put by an employee, in his individual capacity.
Precedent	This entitlement cannot be curtailed by bringing in again the concept of victimisation.
Precedent	686.
Precedent	Equality either as propagated by theorists or as applied by courts seeks to remove inequality by, 'parity of treatm ent under parity of condition'.
Precedent	But once in 'order to treat some persons equally, we must treat them differently' has been done and advantaged and disadvantaged are made equal and are brought in one class or group then any further benefit extended for promotion on the inequality existing prior to be brought in the group would be treating equals unequally.
Precedent	It would not be eradicating the effects of past discrimination but perpetuating it.
Precedent	687.
Precedent	Constitutional sanction is to reserve for backward class of persons.
Precedent	That is class or group interest has been preferred over individual.
Precedent	But promotion from a class or group of employees is not promoting a group or class but an individual.
Precedent	It is one against other.
Precedent	No forward class v. backward class or majority against minority.
Precedent	It would, thus, be contrary to the Constitution.
Precedent	Brother <NAME>, for good and sound reasons has rightly opined, that, Rangachri cannot be held to be laying down good law.
Precedent	* * * * * 'I'  688.
Precedent	Reservation, for, 'economically backward sections  of the people who are not covered by any of the existing schemes of reservation', again, raises an important issue.
Precedent	De facto difficulties in determining such backwardness stands established by failure of the government to evolve any workable criteria even after lapse of one year since, 25th September, 1991, the date on which the order dated 23rd August 1990 directing reservation for backward class was amended and it was announced that, 'the criteria for determining the poorer sections of the <ORG> or the other economically backward sections of the people who are not covered by any of the existing schemes of reservations are being issued separately.'
RatioOfTheDecision	But the de jure hurdles appear, even, greater.
RatioOfTheDecision	Any reservation resulting in curtailing right of equal opportunity is to withstand the test of equal protection or benign discrimination.
RatioOfTheDecision	Latter has been permitted for a class which had suffered injustices in the past and is suffering even now.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is an atonement of past segregation and discrimination such as Negroes  in America and <ORG> of our country.
RatioOfTheDecision	And is being extended even to those who could legitimately be considered to be backward class.
RatioOfTheDecision	Since Article 16(4) has a constitutional purpose and is to operate only so long the goal is not achieved economic backwardness does not qualify for such protective measure.
RatioOfTheDecision	As even if such a class or collectivity is held to fall in the broader concept of the expression backward class of citizens it would not be eligible for the benefit as it would be incapable of satisfying the other mandatory requirement of being inadequately represented in services without which the <ORG> cannot have any jurisdiction to exercise the power.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 16(4) thus by its nature, and purpose cannot be applicable to economically backwards, except probably when a proper methodology is worked out to determine inadequacy of representation of such class.
Precedent	689.
RatioOfTheDecision	Is it possible to reserve under Article 16(1)?
RatioOfTheDecision	Detailed reasons have been given, earlier, against any reservation under cover of doctrine of reason able classification.
RatioOfTheDecision	Eradication of poverty which, 'is not to be exalted or praised, but is an evil thing which must be fought and stamped out' is one of the ideals set out in the Preamble of the Constitution as it postulates to achieve economic justice and exhorts the <ORG> under Article 38(2) to, 'minimise the inequality of income'.
RatioOfTheDecision	All the same can the <ORG> for this purpose reserve posts for the economically backwards in service.
RatioOfTheDecision	Right to equal protection of laws or equality before law in, 'benefits, and burdens' by operation of law, equally, amongst equals and unequally amongst unequals is firmly rooted in concept of equality developed by courts in this country and in America.
RatioOfTheDecision	But any reservation or affirmative action on economic criteria or wealth discrimination cannot be upheld under doctrine of reasonable classification.
RatioOfTheDecision	Reservation for backward class seeks to achieve the social purpose of sharing in services which had been monopolised by few of the forward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	To bridge the gap, thus, created th e affirmative actions have been upheld as the social and educational difference between the two classes furnished reasonable basis for classification.
RatioOfTheDecision	Same cannot be said for rich and poor.
RatioOfTheDecision	Indigence cannot be rational basis for classification for public employment.
RatioOfTheDecision	Any legislative measure or executive action operating unequally between rich and poor has been held to be suspect.
RatioOfTheDecision	A provision requiring a person to pay for trial manuscript before filing criminal appeal was struck down in <NAME> v. Illinois 351 US 12 (195) as it amounted to denial of right of appeal to poor persons.
RatioOfTheDecision	In <NAME> v. <ORG> 383 US 663  Poll tax for voting was invalidated as, 'wealth, like race, creed or colour, is not germane to one's ability to participate intelligently in the electoral process'.
RatioOfTheDecision	Protection was given to the appellants in effect or consequence of equal protection clause.
RatioOfTheDecision	Duty of <ORG> to protect against deprivation due to poverty should not be confused with <ORG>s obligation to treat everyone uni formly and equally without discrimination.
RatioOfTheDecision	Protection against application of law due to difference in economic condition, cannot be equated with classification based on disproportion in wealth.
RatioOfTheDecision	Former is in realm of justice and fairplay whereas latter is equal protection to which every one is entitled.
RatioOfTheDecision	In the former unjust application of law may be cured by removing the offending part and thus apply the law uniformly to rich and poor.
RatioOfTheDecision	Whereas in latter the classification has to be justified on the nexus test.
RatioOfTheDecision	Poverty may have relevance and may furnish valid justification while dealing with social and economic measure.
RatioOfTheDecision	Any legislation or executive measure undertaken to remove disparity in wealth cannot be suspect but a classification based on economic conditions for purposes of Article 16(1) would be violative of equality doctrine.
RatioOfTheDecision	690.
RatioOfTheDecision	More backward and backward is an illusion.
RulingByPresentCourt	No constitutional exercise is called for it.
RulingByPresentCourt	What is required is practical approach to the problem.
RulingByPresentCourt	The collectivity or the group ma y be backward class but the individuals from that class may have achieved the social status or economic affluence.
RulingByPresentCourt	Disentitle them from claiming reservation.
RulingByPresentCourt	Therefore, while reserving posts for backward classes, the departments should make a condition precedent that every candidate must disclose the annual income of the parents beyond which one could not be considered to be backward.
RulingByPresentCourt	What should be that limit can be determined by the appropriate <ORG>.
RulingByPresentCourt	Income apart provision should be made that wards of those backward classes of persons who have achieved a particular status in society either political or social or economic or if their parents are in higher services then such individuals should be precluded to avoid monopolisation of the services reserved for backward classes by a few.
RulingByPresentCourt	Creamy layer, thus, shall stand eliminated.
RulingByPresentCourt	And once a group or collectivity itself is found to have achieved the constitutional objective then it should be excluded from the list of backward class.
RulingByPresentCourt	Therefore, (1) No reservatio n can be made on economic criteria.
RatioOfTheDecision	(2) It may be under Article 16(4) if such class satisfies the test of inadequate representation.
RatioOfTheDecision	(3) Exclusion of creamy layer is a social purpose.
RatioOfTheDecision	Any legislative or executive action to remove such persons individually or collectively cannot be constitutionally invalid.
RatioOfTheDecision	* * * * * 'J'  691.
RatioOfTheDecision	Various infirmities were highlighted in the report of <ORG> and the consequent invalidity of the government order issued on it.
RatioOfTheDecision	Attack on the report varied from the reference being beyond Article 340 to manner and method of ascertaining backwardness by issuing questionnaire to hardly one per cent of the population, interviewing interested and biased persons only, relying on obsolete material such as caste census of 1931, importing personal knowlege, rewriting Hindu Varna by adding intermediate or middle caste between twice born and sudra, working out backward population erroneously as in 1931 only 67% of the population was Hindu and if 22% were SC and 43 % backward then the remaining were 20% inflating backward classes by conjectures and assumptions as <ORG> identified 2399 whereas the Second determined it at 3743 and <ORG> published a project report identifying only 1057 backward classes, and adopting caste as the sole and the only criteria for identifying backwardness etc.
RatioOfTheDecision	Action of the <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	in accepting the report and issuing the Government Order was challenged for exhibition of sudden alacrity not on objective consideration but for extraneous reasons, acceptance of the report without any discussion or debate in the <ORG> which was the least considering the far-reaching consequences of such report, acting by executive order instead of legislative measure, when reservation for backward class was being made in <ORG> services for the first time, propriety of basing the action on a report rendered 10 years earlier without any regard to social and economic changes in the meantime when such period is normally consid ered sufficient for review and re-assessment of continuance of such actions, etc.
RatioOfTheDecision	692.
RatioOfTheDecision	Many of these challenges appear to be well founded but any discussion on it is unnecessary for two reasons, one failure of any objective consideration of the report by the <ORG> before issuing the orders and others some of the basic infirmities have been dealt with while dealing with the issue of identification of backward classes.
RatioOfTheDecision	Above all what is not provided in the Constitution, what was not accepted by the <ORG> in 1956 what has not been approved by this <ORG> even for backward classes in Article 16(4) was adopted by the <ORG> as the basis in its report submitted in 1978 for 'socially and educationally backward classes', an expression narrower and different than 'backward classes' and implemented in 1990 by the <ORG> without even placing it before the <ORG> or any objective consideration by it.
RatioOfTheDecision	An order reserving posts can no doubt be made even by the executive but the decision being of utmost  importance as reservation was being made in services under the <ORG> for the first time the propriety demanded that it should have been placed before the <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	For growth and development of healthy conventions and traditions no provision in the Constitution or statute is needed.
Precedent	It may, however, not be out of place to mention that where rules framed under Rule 309 exist no executive order in violation of it can be passed.
Precedent	693.
RatioOfTheDecision	Vital issues, by agreement of both sides, relating to reservation and preferential treatment in services have been discussed.
RatioOfTheDecision	On many of these this <ORG>, to use the words of <ORG>, has not spoken with, 'one voice'.
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, these public interest petitions, filed in unfortunate circumstances which are not necessary to be narrated, were referred to be heard by a larger bench of nine judges, 'to finally settle the legal positions relating to reservations'.
RatioOfTheDecision	694.
RatioOfTheDecision	Finality, is necessary not only for courts or tribunal but for the guidance of the affirmative action  ameliorative or preferential by the <ORG> or the <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	What should not be lost sight of is if history of discrimination and segregations of the SC/ST and the socially, educationally and economically backward in the darkest chapter of our social history, with no parallel any where in the world, then constitutional therapy to eradicate it root and branch too is unparalleled and even most developed and democratically advanced democracies, cannot match the socially oriented effort to achieve an egalitarian society.
RatioOfTheDecision	Practical equality or equality by result is the approach.
RatioOfTheDecision	Effort is to usher in a progressive society by bridging the gap between the forward and backward by demolishing the social barriers and enabling the lowest to share the power to remove inferiority and infuse feeling of equality.
RatioOfTheDecision	But without sacrificing efficiency and disturbing the equality equilibrium by confining it to minority of posts and treating them preferentially for such length of time, as a self operating mechanism, coming  to an end once the constitutional objective of enabling them to stand on their own is fulfilled.
RatioOfTheDecision	Why reservation policy in services or the benefits of welfare measures pursued by different States for the weaker sections of the society have not percolated to the needy and deserving at the rock bottom is more a political issue than constitutional or legal.
RatioOfTheDecision	But no effort can succeed unless the policy makers eschew extraneous considerations and tackle the problem sincerely and with understanding.
RatioOfTheDecision	So long the identification of the backward class is not made properly and practically it would serve the vested interest only.
Precedent	And the 'halves' among Sudra or the intermediate backward classes shall not permit it to reach the have-nots the real and genuine backward classes.
Precedent	695.
RatioOfTheDecision	No exception can be taken to the recommendations of <ORG> for reservation for backward class of citizens in services by the <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	But commissions are only fact finding bodies.
RatioOfTheDecision	The constitutional responsibility of reserving posts  rests with the government.
RatioOfTheDecision	Unfortunately neither in 1990 nor in 1991 this duty was discharged constitutionally or even legally.
RatioOfTheDecision	Whether the report was within the term of reference and if the <ORG> in identifying socially and educationally backward class repeated the same mistake as was done by the first <ORG> and if the <ORG> could adopt two different yardsticks for determining backwardness among Hindus and non-Hindus were aspects which were required to be gone into by the <ORG> before issuing any order.
RatioOfTheDecision	The exercise of power to reserve is coupled with duty to determine backward class of citizens and if they were adequately represented.
RatioOfTheDecision	If the <ORG> failed to discharge its duty then the exercise of power stands vitiated.
RatioOfTheDecision	No further need be said except to extract following words of <NAME> gives time for the sober second thought * * * * * CONCLUSIONS  696.
RatioOfTheDecision	Both the impugned orders issued by the respective governments in 1990 and 1991 reserving appointments  and posts for socially and educationally backward classes of citizens, without discharging their constitutional obligation of examining if the identification of backward class by the <ORG> was in consonance with constitutional principle and philosophy of the basic feature of the Constitution and if the group or collectivity so identified was adequately represented or not which is the sine qua non for the exercise of the power under Article 16(4 ), are declared to be unenforceable.
RatioOfTheDecision	(1) Reservation in public services either by legislative or executive action is neither a matter of policy nor a political issue.
RatioOfTheDecision	The higher courts in the country are constitutionally obliged to exercise the power of judicial review in every matter which is constitutional in nature or has potential of constitutional repercussions.
RatioOfTheDecision	(2) (a) Constitutional bar under Article 16(2) against state for not discriminating on race, religion or caste is as much applicable to Article 16(4) as to Article 16(1) as they are part of the sam e scheme and serve same constitutional purpose of ensuring equality.
RatioOfTheDecision	Identification of backward class by caste is against the Constitutional.
RatioOfTheDecision	(b) The prohibition is not mitigated by using the word, 'only' in Article 16(2) as a cover and evolving certain socio-economic indicators and then applying it to caste as the identification then suffers from the same vice.
Precedent	Such identification is apt to become arbitrary as well as the indicators evolved and applied to one community may be equally applicable to other community which is excluded and the backward class of which is denied similar benefit.
Precedent	697.
Precedent	Identification of a group or collectivity by any criteria other than caste, such as, occupation cum social cum educational cum economic criteria ending in caste may not be invalid.
Precedent	(c) Social and educational backward class under Article 340 being narrower in import than backward class in Article 16(4) it has to be construed in restricted manner.
Precedent	And the words educationally backward in this Article cannot be disregar ded while determining backwardness.
Precedent	(3) Reservation under Article 16(4) being for any class of citizens and citizen having been defined in Chapter II of the Constitution includes not only Hindus but Muslims, Christians, Sikhs, Buddhists Jains etc.
Precedent	the principle of identification has to be of universal application so as to extend to every community and not only to those who are either converts from Hinduism or some of who carry on the same occupation as some of the Hindus.
RatioOfTheDecision	(4) Reservation being extreme form of protective measure or affirmative action it should be confined to minority of seats.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even though the Constitution does not lay down any specific bar but the constitutional philosophy being against proportional equality the principle of balancing equality ordains reservation, of any manner, not to exceed 50%.
RatioOfTheDecision	(5) Article 16(4) being part of the scheme of equality doctrine it is exhaustive of reservation, therefore, no reservation can be made under Article 16(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	(6) Reservation in promotion is consti tutionally impermissible as, once the advantaged and disadvantaged are made equal and are brought in one class or group then any further benefit extended for promotion on the inequality existing prior to be brought in the group would be treating equals unequally.
RatioOfTheDecision	It would not be eradicating the effects of past discrimination but perpetuating it.
RatioOfTheDecision	(7) Economic backwardness may give jurisdication to state to reserve provided it can find out mechanism to ascertain inadequacy of representation of such class.
RatioOfTheDecision	But such group or collectivity does not fall under Article 16(1).
Precedent	(8) Creamy layer amongst backward class of citizens must be excluded by fixation of proper income, property or status criteria.
Precedent	698.
Precedent	Reservation by executive order may not be invalid but since it was being made for the first time in services under the <ORG> propriety demanded that it should have been laid before <ORG> not only to lay down healthy convention but also to consider the change in social, economic and political conditions of  the country as nearly ten years had elapsed from the date of submissions of the report, a period considered sufficient for evaluation if the reservation may be continued or not.
Precedent	699.
